Current Commentary

Prerequisites for Entrepreneurial Training in Education 35

— Ji

Our society has a traditional, morbid phenomenon. Those who receive higher education always adopt the habits of scholars and officials of the past. They are often physically inactive and ignorant of agriculture. Conversely, farmers and laborers who work hard and engage in production are often regarded as uneducated people. This was the case in the past during the imperial examination era, and it remains unchanged even with the abolition of the examinations and the rise of schools. Its impact is indeed significant. The effectiveness of past education, judging solely by its contribution to national welfare and the people's livelihood, is virtually zero. The lifestyle of the 20th century is incomparable to that of the 15th and 16th centuries. Moreover, a nation claiming to be modern cannot survive by relying on outdated production methods. Therefore, as time goes by, the crisis becomes more apparent. Today, our country faces national difficulties, with everything waiting to be rebuilt, and the people are bewildered, not knowing where to turn. In fact, the crux of the problem is not difficult to discern. It still lies in the fact that education has not been put on the right track. In recent years, the call for production education has been rampant. However, the spirit of production and construction, "sufficient to enrich national welfare and the people's livelihood, quell internal strife, and resist foreign aggression," is still rarely seen in education. Generally, students, influenced by traditional habits, become like the scholars and officials of the past without even realizing it. However, apart from a few lucky individuals, they lack the connections to seek official positions and the skills to find employment. The phenomenon of graduation leading to unemployment has been exposed nationwide, further burdening the nation and society.

Enlightened people within the country, feeling this deeply, have collectively attributed it to the errors of past education. They have jointly proposed that future education should be guided by production. Education authorities have also begun to focus on adding and expanding practical subjects such as science and engineering, while reducing courses in literature and law, as a means of adjustment. Their intention is that if young students can acquire production skills, they will certainly be needed by our country's society, where "hundreds of industries are waiting to be revived, and everything is waiting to be rebuilt," when they leave school in the future. For young individuals, this can ensure opportunities for service, and it will also greatly benefit the overall national welfare and the people's livelihood. However, in my humble opinion, I feel that the reality may not be so. It is undeniable that our society is in a state where "hundreds of industries are waiting to be revived, and everything is waiting to be rebuilt." However, before these industries are revived and rebuilt, how can we accommodate a large number of young people with new production skills? If those who reform education in the future only focus on cultivating young people's production skills without addressing the issue of where to place talents after their skills are developed, the result will only be the creation of a large number of highly educated unemployed vagrants. If young students, after completing their studies, still cannot avoid being displaced and wandering about, then what is the point of us expecting production education to remedy the national welfare and the people's livelihood? Do we not see that many students who study science and engineering abroad, after returning to the country, are unable to enter the industrial sector to display their talents and instead become teachers in schools to make a living? The lessons from the past are not far away, and we should learn from them.

Therefore, the most crucial issue in our country's education today is not only whether students have the opportunity to acquire production knowledge while studying, but also whether students can practically apply their acquired knowledge after graduation to independently create new opportunities. In other words, the highest goal of running education in our country in the future should be to cultivate talented individuals who are astute, capable, and independently entrepreneurial, and it should not be enough to merely cultivate students' production skills. Only in this way will young people not only avoid panic after leaving school due to the lack of social opportunities but also be able to automatically start their own businesses, thereby driving the giant wheel of social evolution.

This is undoubtedly a difficult task. However, there is a passive but necessary prerequisite that we can strive for and implement today. This is to break the traditional habits of scholars and officials. If these habits can be broken, then students will fundamentally have no base thoughts of relying on the old environment to seek wealth and glory. On the one hand, they will be unwilling to accept the protection of evil forces, and on the other hand, they will be unable to withstand the oppression of the old environment. When driven to their wits' end, they will surely break through and find their own path. If students in the future can maintain the virtues of the farming and laboring classes in adapting to the old environment, and also combine them with the courage and knowledge to resist the old environment, then a multitude of independently entrepreneurial talents can emerge. Those who bear the mission and great ambition of reforming education, should they first break the thousands of years of lax and complacent habits of scholars and officials by setting an example themselves? I look forward to it.

French Cabinet Reorganization: Entire Collapse Averted; Minister of Justice Forced to Resign; Laval Appointed Minister of Foreign Affairs 36

(Paris) After a heated cabinet meeting, the government was on the verge of complete collapse. Today, Minister of Justice Chéron submitted his resignation, which was accepted by Prime Minister Doumergue. He indicated that a successor would be decided next week. Chéron's resignation was the result of intense criticism in the press following the assassination of the King of Yugoslavia, which brought up the Stavisky affair and the Prince assassination case. It is said that during the cabinet meeting, several ministers insisted on Chéron's resignation, otherwise they would dissolve the coalition cabinet. After accepting Chéron's resignation, Prime Minister Doumergue announced that the cabinet reorganization would be completed by the end of next week. The vacancy left by Foreign Minister Barthou has been filled by Colonial Minister Laval, and Laval's vacancy has been filled by Piétri. Doumergue also announced that the position of Minister of Interior has been filled by Marchandeau, succeeding Sarraut. Therefore, the only unfilled position is that of Minister of Justice. (National Telegram, 13th)

Balance of Power Among Parties Unchanged; French President Leads Ministers of Army, Navy, and Air Force to Yugoslav Capital to Attend Funeral 37

(Paris) This partial cabinet reorganization maintains the balance of power among the parties in the "Party Truce Cabinet" without any changes. Prime Minister Doumergue explained this at today's Council of Ministers, stating that he could have appointed Minister without Portfolio Herriot or Tardiou as Minister of Foreign Affairs, as they would have been able to handle the position well. However, he preferred that both remain as Ministers without Portfolio, leading their respective political friends to support the cabinet's actions. In addition, he had considered asking Minister of Public Works Flandin to become Minister of Foreign Affairs, as Flandin has extensive experience in foreign negotiations. However, in the end, it was decided to appoint Laval as Minister of Foreign Affairs because Laval had previously served as Minister of Foreign Affairs and had undertaken important missions to Berlin and Washington. He has served as various ministers and even as Prime Minister, accumulating countless experiences, making him the most suitable person for the position of Minister of Foreign Affairs. As for the resignation of Interior Minister Sarraut, the Prime Minister and President expressed their appreciation. His vacancy was filled by Marchandeau, a member of the Chamber of Deputies of the Radical Socialist Party. Marchandeau had served as Secretary-General of the Council of State during the Steeg and Herriot cabinets and as Minister of Budget in the Chautemps cabinet. Furthermore, after Laval's transfer to Minister of Foreign Affairs, the vacancy of Colonial Minister was filled by former Minister of Commerce Rollin, as the colonial economy is closely related to the mother country's commercial policy. Rollin's past experience can help solve the economic difficulties of the colonies. The Council of Ministers unanimously passed the above cabinet reorganization plan. After the cabinet was reorganized, Minister of Justice Chéron submitted his resignation. Chéron stated that the various accusations from the outside world were directed at him personally and were all absurd and inappropriate. However, the political reform work has not yet been completed and is urgent. He did not want to hinder the Prime Minister's progress due to him alone. Therefore, he submitted his resignation. Prime Minister Doumergue thanked Chéron for his loyal cooperation and approved his resignation. However, given the current environment, the position of Minister of Justice is extremely important. Therefore, the Prime Minister believes that a successor cannot be decided before Monday. If a suitable candidate cannot be found among the senators, the Prime Minister intends to select a prominent judge as Minister of Justice. For example, Chief Prosecutor of the Supreme Court, Madec, is one of the people the Prime Minister has in mind. (Havas Telegram, 13th)

(Paris) This afternoon's Council of Ministers was chaired by President Lebrun. After announcing the opening of the meeting, the President delivered a speech commemorating the great French statesman, the late Foreign Minister Barthou, and recounted his achievements in diplomacy. Prime Minister Doumergue then thanked the President and assured him that the cabinet would resolutely continue the tasks already underway. The Council of Ministers subsequently decided that President Lebrun, along with Minister of Army Pétain, Minister of Navy Piétri, and Minister of Air Force Denain, would go to Yugoslavia to represent France at the funeral of King Alexander of Yugoslavia. Minister of Air Force Denain will lead a squadron of French aircraft to Yugoslavia. Next, Interior Minister Sarraut stated that after the Marseille tragedy, he had dismissed the chief of the detective squad, Bédouin, and removed him from his official rank. The prefect of Bouches-du-Rhône, Jouhannaud, was dismissed and placed on probation. The chief inspector of the detective squad in charge of handling officials' travel affairs, Cestreton, was dismissed. However, the Interior Minister himself was negligent in his management and should take the blame. Therefore, in addition to submitting his resignation to the Prime Minister two days ago, he now personally tendered his resignation at the Council of Ministers. Sarraut also said, "The reason why a leader is a leader is that he must take responsibility. Even if the leader leads his subordinates to fulfill their duties, if a major tragedy that the public detests occurs, the leader is still blameworthy. If I bear the blame and am not punished, my conscience will not be at ease. Therefore, I must submit my resignation to you." Finally, he said that although he was retiring, he would still be loyal to peace and repay Prime Minister Doumergue's kindness as a private citizen. Although there was some regret in this request for retirement, he was quite honored. Prime Minister Doumergue repeatedly praised Sarraut, saying that the Interior Minister's resignation was to avoid placing the government in a difficult position, and his generosity was especially appreciated. Thereupon, Prime Minister Doumergue requested the President to sign the appointments of the succeeding cabinet members. As for the resignation of Minister of Justice Chéron, it was not considered at the Council of Ministers, as Chéron had voluntarily submitted his resignation after the Council of Ministers, intending to facilitate the smooth progress of the cabinet's partial reorganization. As for the chief of the National Detective Squad, a successor has not yet been appointed. The vacancy of prefect of Bouches-du-Rhône will be filled during the next prefectural reshuffle. (Havas Telegram, 13th)

(Paris) Prime Minister Doumergue considered the issue of filling the cabinet vacancy after the resignation of Minister of Justice Chéron this morning. It has now been confirmed that Prime Minister Doumergue intends to invite Senator Régnier, the general rapporteur of the Finance Committee, to assume the position of Minister of Justice. However, so far, he has not yet contacted Régnier himself. Therefore, the new Minister of Justice will not be decided before tonight or tomorrow. (Havas Telegram, 14th)

Belgrade Yugoslav national patriotic organizations today appealed to the people to unite in a spirit of sacrifice and composure during this time of national mourning, so as not to create unnecessary incidents. Italian expatriates here today also wrote to the Prime Minister of the Yugoslav Cabinet, saying, "All Italian expatriates here express our condolences for the national mourning of the Yugoslav people and express our grief for the tragic death of His Majesty Alexander. We ask you to convey our deep condolences to the Royal Family and the Government." (National Telegram, 13th)

Rome Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has strictly prohibited newspapers from broadcasting criticisms of the Marseille tragedy. The Italian Prime Minister believes that if Italy and Yugoslavia do not engage in provocative behavior, the friendly relations between the two countries can be maintained. According to reports, the Yugoslav government protested to the Italian government yesterday because an Italian newspaper broadcast that Yugoslavia was on the verge of disintegration, saying that Yugoslavia regarded this as an unfriendly act. Political circles here also explained the reasons why Italy and Yugoslavia should restrain their rash behavior, saying that Italy and France are now eager to reach a compromise, but Yugoslavia's disputes are likely to undermine it. (Paris) It has been confirmed by the French General Directorate of Police that the Yugoslav terrorist organization harbored by Hungary, known as the "Babary Pivot," was the instigator of the Marseille tragedy. (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

(Paris) The Hungarian Embassy here today issued a statement strongly denying Hungary's involvement in the Marseille tragedy, in which Hospitch, an accomplice of Marseille assassin Kalimen, confessed everything to the French police. The Hungarian Ministry of Foreign Affairs also firmly denied the existence of such an assassination terrorist organization in Hungary. However, newspapers here now say that Hungary should bear moral responsibility for the Marseille tragedy. They also say that Hospitch's confession may have serious consequences. Newspapers in Budapest vigorously refuted this statement, saying that while there are political refugees from Croatia living in Hungary, there are also many who have taken refuge in Paris. It is now believed that Kalimen, Hospitch, and the other two who escaped are all members of the refugee organization in Hungary. Yugoslavia protested to the Hungarian government on April 26 about this matter. The Yugoslav government also sent a letter to the League of Nations, saying that Hungary not only tolerated this organization but also helped to establish it. The League of Nations discussed this matter on June 5. At that time, the Hungarian representative complained that shootings occurred on the Yugoslav-Hungarian border, and the Yugoslav representative replied that if we shoot, it is because the opposite side of the border is a real den of bandits. (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

Remains of Deceased King of Yugoslavia Return Home 39

Ten Thousand People Await at Dawn

Salvos of Artillery; Aircraft Soar

Spalato The remains of the late King Alexander I have been transported back to the country today. The destroyer Dubrovnik, carrying the coffin from France, entered the port at 6:00 a.m. this morning. At that time, the sky was slightly bright, and people waiting to welcome him had arrived one after another. All diplomatic representatives in Belgrade, senior government officials, army and navy officers, and tens of thousands of people were silently waiting. The time of the coffin's arrival at the port was announced last night, so people from nearby villages also came here. When the warship entered the port, all the docked warships and surrounding forts fired salutes. British and French warships also participated in the firing, and military aircraft soared into the sky. Government officials sent personnel to the warship to open the coffin and formally identify the body of the late king. Then, the coffin was opened again and brought ashore, where senior naval officers placed it in a very large colored canopy. Government officials and diplomatic representatives offered wreaths, and the people all bowed their heads in tribute. The special train transporting the coffin departed at 10:30 a.m., heading straight for the capital. (National Telegram, 14th)

Marseille Tragedy: A Beautiful Woman Was an Accomplice; She Supplied the Weapons 41

(Paris) The French police are currently conducting a thorough search for a beautiful woman named Gardello Chuv, who is said to be an accomplice of Kalimen, the assassin of King Alexander of Yugoslavia and French Foreign Minister Barthou. She was seen traveling with Kalimen two days before the Marseille tragedy. It is widely believed that the handgun used by Kalimen was smuggled into Marseille by the woman. Today, a British expatriate, whose father is Bulgarian and mother is Turkish, was arrested in Chamonix. He is suspected of being an accomplice in the Marseille murders. After being interrogated by local authorities, he has been transferred to Annecy. As for Hospitch, an accomplice of assassin Kalimen, also known as Novak, and Mr. Piniés, they were detained in the special police chief's office at the Annecy station for sixty hours and were transferred to Ariège tonight, where they will be formally charged with conspiracy to murder King Alexander of Yugoslavia and French Foreign Minister Barthou, and will be temporarily detained there pending the trial in Marseille. (Reuters Telegram, 13th)

Marseille As a result of the efforts of the police task force, it has been determined that a terrorist group was hiding in Aix-en-Provence. The assassination of King Alexander of Yugoslavia was carried out by the group. The group consisted of four or five people, led by a stunningly beautiful woman, residing in a first-class hotel, while her accomplices, Kalrman Cherny K伐台尼克 and three others, stayed in small hotels with simple luggage to avoid attention. The woman was registered under the name Marie Woodlov, and her luxurious suitcases were full of weapons. The weapons used by assassin Kalrman were carried in her suitcases. This shows that the assassination was meticulously planned in advance. The girl had a companion who came to the hotel to meet her at night. His real name was 哀貢克伐台尼克, but he registered at the hotel as Kalame. That night, he went to Avignon. The next day, Kalrman went from Aix-en-Provence to Marseille. Another accomplice, Cherny, went to Avignon at night after the incident, and then from Avignon to Fontainebleau. Police found traces of him in Fontainebleau, but he has not been apprehended yet. As for the whereabouts of the mysterious woman, Marie Woodlov, they had not been determined as of 6:00 p.m. today. (Havas Telegram, 13th)

Japanese Army and Colonial Ministry Compete for Control of Manchuria; Prime Minister Okada in a Dilemma; All Parties Fear Political Turmoil 43

(Tokyo) The issue of reforming the resident Manchurian organization, centered on the case of the military police commander concurrently serving as the police chief, has become a dispute between the on-site personnel and the central authorities. The Army and Colonial Ministries have each issued statements, and the conflict between the two sides is very obvious. The government instructed at the cabinet meeting on the 12th that the solution to this problem should await the handling of the situation by the current commander in Manchuria, Hishikari. Before receiving the report from the commander, they will take a wait-and-see attitude. However, even after the cabinet discussion, the Army authorities felt that the government's top officials' attitude was too moderate. On the 13th, they issued a statement, and Army Minister Hayashi also planned to meet with the Prime Minister within a day or two, with little hope that the cabinet's decision on the reform of the resident Manchurian organization would be implemented quickly. As for the Colonial Ministry, which is in opposition to the Army, even though Okada, who also serves as the Colonial Minister, issued instructions, it is difficult to remain silent on the Army's statement. Therefore, it was decided to issue a rebuttal statement on the 14th. Thus, the Army and Colonial Ministry authorities are completely in a state of conflict. Prime Minister Okada believes that this situation exposes the lack of unity within the cabinet and undermines the government's prestige, which has a significant impact on the political world. He has now decided to step in and make a ruling. All parties are paying close attention to this case. (Jiji Press Telegram, 14th)

(Tokyo) The dispute over the reform plan for the resident Manchurian organization has shifted from the local level to a conflict between the Army and Colonial Ministries, becoming a battle of statements, exposing the lack of unity within the cabinet. The situation is quite serious. The government has no intention of modifying the reform plan that has been decided upon by the cabinet and still wants to maintain it to the end in order to implement the original plan. As for the current dispute, it has decided not to contradict the original plan and to wait for Commander Hishikari's work on the ground to find an opportunity and method for suppressing the situation. If Commander Hishikari's work does not yield results, the government will immediately assert its authority, based on the principle that the police should not be militarized, and issue a major statement. At the same time, it will clearly explain the purpose of the new organization's official system in the reform, consult the cabinet, and quickly decide to implement it. Therefore, this issue will depend on the situation on the ground. Although the Army and Colonial Ministry have been in opposition for the past few days, there will soon be a shift in the situation. (United News Agency Telegram, 14th)

(Tokyo) Kantō Governor-General Hishikari has now sent a telegram to the Minister of Colonial Affairs, reporting on the situation on the ground regarding the reform plan. The second report was received by the Colonial Ministry on the 13th. The general content is as follows: The opinions of the officials of the Kantō Government-General are as follows: (1) Military officers must not participate in the Police Department; (2) The duties of the police and the military police should be clearly separated and not infringe upon each other; (3) The Police Chief must not be concurrently held by the military police commander.

If the above points are violated, the entire staff will submit their resignations and decide to leave the new organization. This trend can be inferred, and it is not yet known what kind of situation it will cause in the future. If they deliberately oppose their will or control them by force, it may be difficult to obtain complete sincerity in their work. The Governor-General is repeatedly anxious about this case and hopes that at this time, he will be able to understand the emotions of the officials of the Kantō Government-General and establish an appropriate solution. This is what I pray for. (United News Agency Telegram, 14th)

(Tokyo) The Army and Colonial Ministry's opinions on the reform plan for the resident Manchurian organization are in direct conflict, exposing the disunity within the cabinet at a time of major crisis, which may cause serious consequences. Moreover, the government's hope that Commander Hishikari would work on the ground has now come to a standstill after receiving the report. Therefore, the government's wait-and-see attitude is also not allowed by the facts. However, how to suppress the opposition in the Kantō region in the future and how to implement its established policy are problems that the government authorities are painstakingly worried about. (United News Agency Telegram, 14th)

Germany Asks US to Abolish Reciprocity Treaty; US Demands Maintenance of Dawes Loan 46

(Washington) Germany today requested the United States to amend the most-favored-nation clause in the German-American commercial treaty, claiming that the clause conflicts with commercial treaties Germany is negotiating with other countries. This request was submitted to the State Department by the German Ambassador to the United States, Luther, along with an explanation stating that Germany is willing to extend the current commercial treaty, but the most-favored-nation clause must be removed. To facilitate treaty revision, Ambassador Luther formally notified that Germany intends to cancel the entire treaty when it expires on October 14 next year. Taking this opportunity, the State Department also formally notified Germany that the United States will not tolerate any discrimination against American bondholders of the Dawes Loan and expressed dissatisfaction that Germany proposed paying only 75 percent of the $2.1 million in interest due on October 15. The State Department believes that Germany's current debt situation is actually favorable to European bondholders, while Germany requests to amend the commercial treaty because it believes the treaty is excessively favorable to the United States. (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

Britain Endeavors to Expand its Air Force (London Correspondence) 60

Military Equipment is Relatively Backward Due to Financial Difficulties

Britain is a relatively conservative and calm nation. She is not overly trendy, especially in international politics, maintaining a gentlemanly attitude but never lagging behind. When the time is right, she acts immediately. For example, Europe has recently been arguing fiercely over military equipment. Germany withdrew from the League of Nations as a result, France is doing everything to guarantee security, Japan is using 50 percent of its national treasury for military spending, and the United States is preparing to build more than 100 warships. Britain, however, has not had any startling plans and seems unenthusiastic about military equipment. Recently, however, the situation has changed. The crisis in Europe is becoming increasingly urgent, and military needs are becoming more pressing. Britain has risen up to expand its air force and improve the mechanization of its army. According to figures released by the Aviation Ministry, the British Air Force ranks fifth in the world. First is France (with 1,600 first-line aircraft), second is the Soviet Union (with approximately 1,300 to 1,500 first-line aircraft), third is the United States, and fourth is Italy (each with approximately 1,100 aircraft). Britain has only 850 aircraft. Therefore, over the next five years (starting in 1934), it will expand by 77 flying squadrons, each squadron containing 12 single-engine aircraft or 10 to 12 twin-engine aircraft. If they are airships, each squadron will have only four, totaling 840 new aircraft.

Regarding the economics of the air force expansion plan, according to acting Prime Minister and Conservative Party leader Baldwin, "Since the Great War, our country has actively and continuously strived for an international military reduction policy. In order to promote this policy and set an example, we have reduced our own military equipment to the extent that it is only enough to defend against danger. This was in the hope that other countries would follow our example. However, the delay in the military reduction conference has been beyond our expectations. Over the past eight and a half years (since 1926), defects have accumulated in our national defense forces, and discussions have been frequent in all areas, loudly shouting that the border is uneasy. In particular, the increase in military expenditures in various countries has created a problem of balance of power. Therefore, we must not only make up for the shortcomings of the air force, but also re-establish the air force expansion plan that has been delayed several times. We should resolve to recognize that this cannot be delayed for a single day. The method of expansion is to expand our air force capacity to a level close to that of our nearest neighbor in recent years…"

The last sentence seems to refer to France as its hypothetical enemy, but the subsequent supplementary statement pays attention to Germany. Baldwin also said, "In the era of air defense, we must pay attention to the fact that the old borders have lost their effectiveness. When you think about protecting Britain, you can no longer consider the defenses between the cliffs of Dover. You must pay attention to the fact that today's borders must extend to the banks of the Rhine."

When the air force expansion plan was proposed, Labor Party House of Lords member Ponsonby immediately advocated opposition, believing that "the military reduction conference has just ended, and French Foreign Minister Barthou has just visited London. If an arms expansion proposal is put forward, this policy will not only fail to guarantee security but will also be harmful to world peace and even cause an arms race, so it is regrettable...." He also believed that military balance with France was meaningless, and moreover, after the so-called Anglo-French understanding, would it not arouse national suspicion? However, in the end, Ponsonby's proposal was rejected by a majority of 54 to 9, meaning that the air force expansion plan passed in the House of Lords and would be transferred to the House of Commons.

In the House of Commons, the main criticism came from the Liberal Party's Samuel, who focused solely on financial issues. He said, "The air force expansion plan proposed by the Minister of Aviation costs one penny for every pound earned. This is not the first penny, nor is it the last penny. Our total military expenditure is £113 million, which is about 2 shillings and 6 pence for every pound earned. If we add past war expenses, then the annual military expenditure is £35.7 million. This number is larger than the total revenue from income tax and inheritance tax… Therefore, if this causes an arms expansion competition, Parliament really does not have the courage to approve this proposal." The government's explanation still focused on the small size of the air force and national defense security. The result was that the Labor Party's proposal was rejected, and the air force expansion plan was established. On the eve of the naval conference, Britain's actions have a tendency to prepare for war.

On the Road to the East 61

— Ming Dao

Strict Investigation Aboard Ship

Poor Economic Conditions in Nagasaki

The neighboring country of Japan is very close. A dozen years ago, even the slowest ship could travel from Shanghai to Nagasaki in just under a day. Now, it only takes 29 hours.

On the ship, everything seems to be going smoothly. People who have lived in Shanghai for a long time especially enjoy the taste of the sea breeze. However, on the other hand, we feel both amused and suffocated by things like the Japanese maritime police investigation. In the past, only doctors came to check for epidemics, with no other procedures. Now, the epidemic check seems less important, but they pay attention to each person's identity, origin, and destination. Their attitude is indeed very polite, but their attention to detail is extremely meticulous, truly showing devotion to duty. Let's put aside personal feelings and make a calm analysis. The first point is that their national organization is strict, with control over everyone entering and leaving the country (whether foreign or domestic). This is also due to Japan's geographical position, surrounded by the sea, allowing for effective monitoring of entry and exit. The second point is that they fully exercise their political power in all areas under their jurisdiction, never letting anything slide or being lazy. Perhaps this is a manifestation of their extraordinary period, making it clear that this is not peacetime but has special significance.

For example, a person who is fierce on the outside but timid on the inside is not to be feared. You can tell at a glance that they have no far-reaching ambitions. However, a person who is extremely humble in speech, very respectful in attitude, and whose purpose is very grand, employing various methods with great determination, is worth paying attention to. The maritime police on the ship belong to this category. They are always outwardly respectful to foreigners, seeking to understand your connections from all angles. They only feel at ease when they are certain that you harbor goodwill towards Japan. They are uneasy about those who have no particular likes or dislikes for Japan. If you inadvertently reveal something, they become vigilant and defensive. A friend on board said that Japanese police always assume the worst of people and try to imagine things in the worst possible light. Therefore, they always treat foreign visitors with suspicion.

Customs inspection is carried out on the pier for ordinary third-class passengers. First- and second-class passengers are inspected on the ship. It is said that inspecting on the ship is a courtesy to passengers, done for their convenience. However, when they have extra time, they can sit down and carefully examine each item. For example, paper cigarettes, radios, explosives, handguns, and cameras are subject to heavy taxes or prohibition. Even personal daily necessities are carefully inspected, fearing any hidden items. They are even more lenient with books, examining them one by one, and anything that catches their attention is recorded in a register for future review. They pay even more attention to Western books. In short, they do not avoid any trouble that can be caused.

Nagasaki is the closest port to China. In the past, many Chinese people did business here, and commerce was quite developed. Now, it has declined. Except for a very few Western-style clothing stores and restaurants, Chinese merchants have almost no place to stand. Even if there is no political interference, it is unlikely they could survive in the current economic downturn. There were only two or three Chinese merchants on board, and a dozen or so students. This shows the natural situation when Sino-Japanese relations cannot proceed smoothly.

Nagasaki is just after its annual "Great Festival." The depressed economic conditions seem to have been somewhat alleviated, but this is just a drop in the ocean, unable to quench a long drought. The slogans "Great Discount" and "Great Sale" are still posted everywhere, replacing the old with the new. Store signs hang all over the streets, but customers are few and far between, and business is slow. Nagasaki is a mid-sized city with a population of just over 220,000. Import and export trade is also quite active, and the harbor is filled with an American merchant ship and a visiting French warship, but there are few foreign merchants and tourists. Although the authorities are trying hard to use strong stimulants to excite the general public, the inherent vitality is insufficient, and the stimulation is only temporarily effective. There are indeed few people begging on the streets, but I personally saw two or three people with insufficient clothing picking up discarded scraps of paper along the main street. As for people who are not getting enough nutrition, there are many more. These are just a few brief observations of what I saw on the surface, reported to my fellow countrymen. (Nagasaki, October 11)

Guangzhou Agricultural Exhibition 62

Exhibits Displayed in Ten Rooms

Opened on the 7th and Exhibited for Seven Days

Guangzhou Correspondence: The city's agricultural exhibition opened on October 7 at the Pingmin Palace on Danan Road. A majestic archway was built in front of the venue, with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen hanging above, flanked by the flag of the Party and the Nation. Below was the exhibition slogan, "Urbanizing the Countryside, Ruralizing the City." To the left of the entrance was the Disciplinary Department, and to the right were the Fire and Rescue Departments. A silk-reeling machine was displayed in the main hall. The various exhibition rooms were to the right, and potted flowers and trees were displayed on the left. The opening ceremony was held at noon on that day, presided over by Mayor Liu Jiwen, who announced the reasons for holding the exhibition. Guests then gave speeches in turn, and the ceremony concluded at around 2 PM, followed by the public exhibition. The venue was divided into ten rooms, displaying exhibits from various departments, mostly focusing on sericulture and rice cultivation, as these are the main agricultural products of Guangdong Province. The first room was for sericulture, with the words "Reviving Guangdong Silk" written in the center of a rotating globe made by the Shunde Sericulture Implementation Zone at the entrance. There were over 200 exhibits inside. The second room had charts and evidence of silk improvement methods. The third room displayed improved silk products. The above three rooms were all for sericulture, and there were also paper products made from mulberry branches and a model of the rise and fall of the sericulture industry in Shunde County. When the silk industry in the province was at its peak, the annual value of silk exports exceeded 100 million yuan, but in recent years, it has decreased to 20 to 30 million yuan, leading to the economic bankruptcy of silkworm farmers and shaking the entire social economy. The fourth room was for aquatic products, with diagrams of fish pond oyster farming and models of trawler ships, as well as specimens of aquatic products such as fish and shrimp, totaling over 200 items, all produced by the Agriculture and Forestry Bureau. The fifth room was for agricultural economics and meteorology, with diagrams of new rural economic construction. The structure utilizes the organization of cooperatives, operates cultivation, and equips it scientifically, so that agricultural harvests achieve excellent results. In addition, there were hundreds of agricultural charts, mostly produced by the Agricultural College of Sun Yat-sen University, Lingnan University Agricultural College, and Zhongkai School. The sixth room was for forests, soils, and fertilizers, with soil specimens, fertilizer specimens, forest seeds, and timber charts from various counties and cities in the province, totaling hundreds of items. The seventh room was for agronomy, horticulture, pests, and diseases, with improved methods for grafting and promoting the growth of sugarcane and fruit trees, as well as over 1,000 insect specimens. The research and methods of the Agriculture and Forestry Bureau in preventing and controlling agricultural pests were quite systematic, and the products of Zhongda, Nanda, and Zhongkai schools were also excellent. The improved sugarcane varieties in the room grew to over 10 feet tall and several inches in diameter in just eight months, three times larger than local sugarcane. The newly invented pest control drugs were also effective. The eighth room was for new agricultural implements, such as threshing machines, cultivators, weeders, powder sprayers, mist sprayers, single-shaft plows, A-frame plows, spike-tooth harrows, and water pumps, all of which were recently improved and more economical and durable than imported products. The tenth room was for animal husbandry and veterinary medicine, with one purebred Siberian boar and one sow, each weighing over 300 pounds, as well as over 100 Beijing ducks and Lixing chickens. The improved chickens can lay 250 to 300 eggs per year, and there are also charts detailing the steps and methods for improving pigs, chickens, and ducks. The exhibition is open to the public for seven consecutive days starting from the 7th, with entertainment and dramas to add to the fun, so the situation is very lively. (9th)

Recent News on the Economic Situation of the Nanyang Islands 63

Progress in Foreign Trade of Malaya

Due to Rising Prices of Rubber and Tin

Singapore Correspondence: The group of islands located between the Indian and Pacific Oceans are collectively known by our countrymen as the Nanyang Islands. These islands, situated in the tropics, are rich in resources and sparsely populated, hence have long been known as a paradise on earth. Diligent and hardworking overseas Chinese have ventured deep into this uniquely endowed land, rightly viewing it as a place where gold is everywhere, easily attainable. However, the world situation shifts and changes constantly. Since the winds of global economic downturn reached Asia, the first to be affected was this very paradise where gold was said to be everywhere. Native products plummeted in price, factories closed down, resulting in hundreds of thousands of workers being plunged into the gloom of unemployment. A portion of these unemployed workers were our diligent and hardworking overseas Chinese. Unable to make a living in the Southern Islands after losing their jobs, they could only return to their homeland en masse. At the same time, those compatriots who remained in Nanyang, due to the poor market situation and sluggish business, had no surplus funds to remit back to their motherland, causing the social and economic situation in our Fujian and Guangdong provinces, which rely heavily on remittances from overseas Chinese for a large part of their income, to deteriorate daily, almost beyond repair. Therefore, the economic situation of the Nanyang Islands has a close and vital relationship with our country, which we cannot afford to ignore. What exactly is the current economic situation of the Nanyang Islands? This is what our compatriots in the motherland would like to know. According to investigations, the current economic situation of the Nanyang Islands has indeed made significant progress compared to before. The biggest reason for this is the high prices of rubber and tin. As for the regions, British territories have seen more progress than Dutch territories. The reasons for this difference are twofold: first, rubber and tin are the main products of Malaya, while the Dutch territories only consider them secondary; second, the Dutch monetary system still uses the gold standard, so their prices are relatively higher, making it difficult to sell (Note: Currently, one Straits dollar is only worth a little over 84 Dutch cents). This is the slight difference in the current economic situation between the British and Dutch territories.

As for the figures of Malaya's foreign trade, according to the latest report from the local Registrar of Statistics, the total value of import trade last year was 362,474,000 yuan, and the export trade was 415,584,000 yuan. Offsetting the imports and exports, there was a surplus of 53,110,000 yuan. In the previous year, Malaya's foreign trade had a deficit of 16,430,000 yuan. Therefore, since last year, Malaya has clearly begun to recover and prosper. According to the recent report from the Singapore Chamber of Commerce, from January to July of this year, Malaya's foreign trade showed an increase of 93,000,000 yuan in export trade and 57,000,000 yuan in import trade compared to last year. Therefore, it is predicted that by the end of this year, Malaya's foreign trade will also show progress compared to last year.

The Communist Bandits of Changting Have No Natural Defenses 64

Shantou Correspondence: Because Shicheng and Changting were surrounded and attacked from the northeast and northwest, Zhu and Mao have moved their foremost front line to the boundary ridge between Ruijin and Changting. Taking advantage of the rugged terrain, they have built many fortresses. The boundary ridge leads to the Wuyi Mountains on the left and Junmen Ridge on the right. The bandits, relying on their ability to scale mountains and travel at night, are defending themselves with the terrain against the National Army. On September 26th and 27th, the battles on the Pengkou and Wenfang lines were all initiated by the bandits' night attacks. As a result, the National Army achieved a great victory. Important passes such as Zhongwu Village, Yiyang Ridge, and Banxian Rock were all recovered by the National Army. This place is only sixty to seventy *li* away from Changting City. The terrain of Tingzhou is surrounded by mountains on all sides. The most unique thing is that a high mountain rises within the city, and the walls on all sides rely on the mountains and water, making it exceptionally majestic. This mountain is called Dragon Mountain. The water of the Yin River flows southward through Shanghang and Dabu, converging into the Han River. Therefore, Tingzhou paper has always used Chaozhou as the main distribution area, and then transported for export from Shantou. The Yin River runs for dozens of *li* in the Ting area, and the quicksand is like gold, dazzling and eye-catching, also known as Golden Sand. Zhongwu Village can be called a natural barrier on the front line from Changting to Liancheng. Now that this place has been recovered by the National Army, the bandits have no natural defenses within seventy *li* of the city. It is only a matter of time before the National Army captures Changting.

The Issue of Taking Over the Eastern Tombs 65

丨 Representatives of the Committee Have Been Selected 丨

Beiping Correspondence: The issue of taking over the Eastern Tombs in Malanyu has been discussed for a long time. The reason why it could not be realized earlier was initially due to the issue of the withdrawal of the puppet troops stationed at the Eastern Tombs, which took time for repeated consultations. Then it was because the representatives of the Qing imperial family and clans in the Eastern Tombs Management Committee could not be appointed, and because the car road between Beiping and Malanyu was washed out by rain and cars could not travel, making the date of takeover impossible to determine. However, the administrative part of Malanyu was taken over by our side two months ago, and Yin Tixin was sent as the resident director of the Jiji District Office in Yu. What is now being said about the takeover is the transfer of the responsibility for the Eastern Tombs management, and the entry of our security team into Malanyu and the Eastern Tombs to maintain law and order.

In the past, the Eastern Tombs had a management committee. After the Great Wall War, puppet troops entered, and the committee could not exercise its functions. Yin Rugeng, the special commissioner of the Jiji District Office, negotiated with the Japanese side earlier, and as a result, the puppet troops stationed at the tombs decided to withdraw completely outside the pass when we took over. Our side is fully responsible for the management of the tombs. At the same time, the organization of the Tombs Protection Committee will be slightly expanded, with the addition of two representatives from the Qing imperial family and clans. After the agreement was reached by both parties, the elderly among the Qing imperial family and clans did not want to be bothered, and the younger ones did not command sufficient public respect. This is one of the real reasons why the representatives could not be appointed immediately. After Yin Rugeng repeatedly urged the Qing imperial family and clans, Pu Xian and Bo Nian have been appointed, and yesterday they notified the Jiji District Office in writing. In addition to the special commissioner of the Jiji District, the county magistrate of Xinglong, and the resident director of the Jiji District Office in Malanyu as ex officio members, the committee members are also one representative each from the Hebei Industry Department and the Civil Affairs Department, and the two representatives recommended by the Qing imperial family, to jointly organize the committee. Now that the Qing imperial representatives have been recommended, only the Civil Affairs Department is still selecting a representative, who can be appointed in the next few days. Although the date of establishment of the committee has not been determined, there is no objection to it officially starting work before the actual takeover of the Eastern Tombs.

Regarding all the preparations for the takeover of the Eastern Tombs, our side began to proceed two months ago. Yin Tixin, the resident director of the Jiji District Office in Malanyu, started the process as soon as he took office, and the date of takeover was also predetermined. Later, due to continuous rains in the north, the Pingyu road was flooded above the knees, and traffic was completely cut off, causing the takeover procedures to be stranded. The general public rumored that the takeover was indefinite, and those concerned believed that this was a fabrication by those who did not understand the truth and was not worth refuting.

Yin Rugeng, the special commissioner of the Jiji District, recently agreed with Shibayama Kenjiro, the military attache of the Japanese embassy, to inspect the Eastern Tombs in Malanyu together tomorrow (the 14th) and to agree on the date of takeover. Shibayama had originally planned a trip to Tangshan, so it was decided that after going to Malanyu with Yin, he would then travel to Tangshan. Yin had already prepared the vehicles for the trip on the day before yesterday (the 11th). Yin Tixin, the director of Malanyu, returned to Beiping because of the Miyagoe case, and also rushed to Malanyu on the day before yesterday (the 11th) to prepare everything. However, Yin Rugeng suddenly caught a cold last night (the 12th), and this morning (the 13th) temporarily sent his secretary He Xiaoyi to meet with Shibayama, informing him that he would postpone the trip due to illness. Shibayama also agreed. As for the funds for the Eastern Tombs Protection Committee, there were funds in the past, supplemented by the land tax of the tomb area. The income and expenses can be offset. The location of the committee is in the Eastern Tombs, and Yin Tixin, Li Ying (county magistrate of Xinglong), and Bo Nian were designated among the committee members to stay at the tombs regularly to preside over daily affairs (13th).

New Construction in He County, Anhui Province 66

Improving Land Tax Collection by Implementing Clear Measurement

Paying Attention to Public Health by Establishing Hospitals

Enthusiastic Assistance from Teachers and Students of Shanghai McKinnon School

Politics in our country takes the county as the unit, so reforming county administration is the key to rebuilding the countryside, and the foundation for the revival of the nation. Burying oneself in this practical work has gradually become a trend in various places in recent years. Ding County in Hebei is the most notable example. He County in Anhui is now also said to be remarkable. The construction of He County has only been in recent years, and there are several aspects of its development in the past few months that are worth mentioning. I will record a brief outline to serve as a reference for those engaged in social work.

The most important thing for county administration and rural areas is the land tax. The failure to equalize land taxes in various counties, as well as the corruption in the collection of grain by township chiefs and guarantors, has always been the biggest problem in our country. He County originally had more than a thousand people involved in land tax collection. They had no salary, so they habitually extorted money from the people illegally. Now, a grain counter has been set up in the county government, and farmers generally go directly to the county government to pay their grain. The county government grain counter now only uses about thirty people, and they have fixed salaries. Farmers used to bring an extra ten cents when paying grain, but now it has been reduced to seven cents, which is used to pay the salaries of the grain counter staff. However, this is only a passive measure to eliminate the abuses of land tax. If we want to actively rectify the land tax to equalize the burden, we must engage in clear measurement. The work of clear measurement of fields in He County was voluntarily undertaken by teachers and students of Shanghai McKinnon Middle School and St. John's University during the summer vacation. A group of six people, including Zheng Binzhi, Wu Xiangguang, and Ling Dingzhong from McKinnon Middle School, and Duan Rumei and Zhang Junliang from St. John's University, led by McKinnon Middle School teacher Lai Puwu, went to He County from Shanghai on July 2nd this summer, and returned after three weeks. They measured the third district in the north of He County and completed six maps, which have now been adopted by the county.

Secondly, medical and health care are most directly related to the suffering of the people. The people of He County are not very enlightened, and most of the doctors are people without deep research in medical and health science. The land is barren and the people are poor, so they have no extra strength to equip a new-style hospital. Dr. Fu of Shanghai Renji Hospital was invited to the county before National Day to plan everything, and County Magistrate Liu convened local people to discuss ways to help fund it. It was agreed that each gentry would donate 20 yuan per month, raising 300 yuan per month, to fund the project. Dr. Fu has now returned to Shanghai and is responsible for purchasing materials and medicines, and persuading Chinese doctors among his colleagues to go there to practice medicine. The letter from County Magistrate Liu of He County to President Shen of Shanghai McKinnon Middle School is also recorded below:

"More than two months have passed since your school's surveying team left He and returned to Shanghai. Time flies, as if it were yesterday. This move by your school will bring infinite hope to the future of politics and the welfare of the people in our county. The biggest problem with land tax in our country is the failure to equalize the burden. The rich rely on their power to conceal their grain, while the poor have to pay double. The reason for this is that there are no accurate maps to serve as the basis for measurement and investigation. The team has achieved so much in our county in the shortest period of time. They worked tirelessly under the scorching heat, and their spirit and perseverance have amazed everyone who saw them. The deep gratitude of the people of our county cannot be described in words. I sincerely express my extreme gratitude to the teachers and students of the surveying team of your school. The fact that the maps measured by the team are now being fully utilized is what I want to report to you. A few days ago, we received a letter from the leader of the team dated the 18th of this month, saying, "The entire team is currently eagerly discussing further work plans, and plans to organize three teams during the two-week winter vacation and next year's summer vacation, one for surveying, one for medicine, and one for construction, to return to He County to work. The first team will of course continue the work of this summer. As for the work plan of the second team, it has now been approved by the Renji Hospital on Shandong Road, and will receive considerable training before departure in preparation for service. The work of the third team will be to repair the streets of villages and towns, the hot spring bath in Xiangquan Town, and build ditches on various roads to facilitate transportation. The biggest job is to dredge the old river channels to allow the waters of the Yangtze River to penetrate deep into the hinterland to prevent the recurrence of drought. In a previous letter, it was said, "I would like to reiterate the proposal to return to He County for service. Although your place insists on supplying food and travel expenses, we are willing to provide our own funds. The principal and all colleagues of our school are willing to support us. The students who went to He County have been highly praised and valued by other students after returning to school, which is also worth comforting. "Another letter said, "The students still feel excited when talking about the work they did in He County last time, and He County will be strongly promoted in our school this semester. If your Excellency needs enthusiastic service in the future, there will definitely be many people. Your Excellency said that you need doctors and public health work. I have told Dr. Fu of the Renji Hospital on Shandong Road about this matter. He plans to take advantage of the summer vacation to visit your place for a week to conduct an inspection, which may be of some benefit. He may be able to find a way to persuade some Chinese doctors among his colleagues who are willing to practice medicine in your place. "The above-mentioned points in each letter make it impossible for me not to be fascinated and express my most sincere gratitude. Please convey our heartfelt welcome to the colleagues and students of your school on my behalf. If you come to our county during this year's winter vacation and next year's summer vacation to help farmers with their work and investigate the rural situation, I will do my best to provide all kinds of conveniences. As for the members of the service team, the more the better. It is true that the society in our county needs improvement and help in the most places, and it is also the most urgent."

Northwest Inspection Notes 67

— Special Correspondent Geng Ya

The Mule and Horse Fair in Ledu County

There was originally a road from Xining to Wuwei (Liangzhou) or Zhangye (Ganzhou), but the mountain slopes were high and the area was remote. It was necessary to carry food and tents and travel in groups. As a reporter traveling alone, I felt very inconvenient. Therefore, on July 5th, I still took the original road back to Lanzhou. The mountain ranges along the way stretched from west to east, with high and low layers overlapping for hundreds of *li*. Generally speaking, the mountain ranges in the front were lower in height because they ran parallel to the plains and rivers, and the color of the grass was tender yellow. The mountains in the back were higher than the previous layer, and the color of the mountains also changed from light green to dark black. The peaks were covered with white snow, and the silver light was dazzling. There were even higher peaks, a line of blue, the same color as the sky, which could be faintly seen in the depressions of the mountain peaks in the front range, but they were already hundreds of *li* away.

Two days later, I passed through Ledu. It was the county's mule and horse fair in East Lake Park. The sound of gongs and drums filled the air, and the voices of people were boiling. It could be heard from several *li* away. A stage was erected in the middle of the square, with a paper plaque with gold characters on a red background hanging on it, saying, "Welcome Regiment Commander Ma Zhiwu." The play was "Jing Zhong," performed in Qinqiang opera. In front of the stage, the officers and soldiers of Regiment Commander Ma's regiment sat on the ground holding guns, and the ordinary audience surrounded them. Women watched from further away, and Mongol and Tibetan men and women mingled in various places, their clothes colorful, and their ornaments jangling, creating an image of various ethnic groups gathering together to celebrate peace and prosperity. According to the talk, the fair had been suspended for many years and was suddenly restored this year. The audience from various villages was still enthusiastic, but the mule and horse trade was very sluggish. The officials and gentry were meeting and planned to continue the opera for ten days. The source of funds was (1) stall donations, (2) commission from gambling, and (3) a discretionary levy on sales. It was predicted that the income and expenses would be offset, and there might even be a surplus, etc.

Later, I arrived at Xincheng and escaped the heat by the Yellow River. I saw a water mill, which was simple in construction and had a good idea (of course, it could not be compared to a flour machinery company). The method was to use a wide boat, with holes on both sides, and a wooden beam running horizontally outside the edge. At both ends of the wood, boards were inserted as wheels, shaped like windmills, half submerged in the river. The water flowed and the wheels turned, and the wood rotated continuously. Then, a gear was placed in the middle of the wood to interlock with the edge wheel of the "mill" placed in the boat, horizontally and vertically. The wooden wheel rotated, and the mill also rotated non-stop. The boat was covered with a house, and a rope was tied to the shore. When the water rose, the boat (that is, the mill) rose; when the water fell, the boat lowered. The water flow was not fixed, and the boat could be moved, and the rotation of the mill wheel could not be restricted. This was not seen when I came, so I added it above.

A Brief Talk by Chairman Zhu 68

When I arrived in Lanzhou, it happened that Chairman Zhu Shaoliang had also returned from the capital, so I went to visit him. The main points of the conversation are roughly as follows: "Fortunately, the security situation in Gansu Province has gradually improved. The facts of the past one or two years can be seen in general. However, the established practice of garrison troops extracting funds locally still needs to be eliminated. When it comes to politics, it is easier to be effective. Gansu Province's finances have been insufficient for many years. This time I went to the capital to contact Minister Kong of Finance to negotiate assistance, and I have been allowed to find a way. If this can be realized early, the administration of Gansu will be easier to promote," etc. Zhu's words were concise and to the point. I admire his insight very much. If the established practice of garrison troops extracting funds locally is not eliminated, not only will the financial revenue figures be nominal, but it will be difficult to make a reliable overall plan for political construction, and it will even invisibly add to the burden on the people, who have already been exhausted. How can the poor people bear it? Now that Zhu has seen the evils of the times and is seeking ways to remedy them, the gospel of the people of Gansu can be said to be right before our eyes.

The finances of Gansu Province are indeed difficult. Since the reorganization of the provincial government last year, although no effort has been spared in reorganizing taxation, it is difficult to reform because of deep-rooted habits. The provincial government's plan for reorganizing taxation has not been followed and implemented in most counties, so that the index of income and expenditure for this year is only 5,538,728 yuan versus 6,985,791 yuan, which is still short of 1,447,063 yuan. In Gansu Province, where the land is vast and the resources are abundant, but the burden on farmers is heavy and the provincial treasury is exhausted, then it is necessary to realize the reorganization of taxation. This is a responsibility that the authorities cannot shirk. From another point of view, the huge military expenditure in this province and the meager construction expenses are also a major reason for the decline of the rural economy and the depression of production. The following is an excerpt of the financial revenue and expenditure statements of the first, second, and third months of this year, recently released by the Finance Department, to get a glimpse of the financial difficulties of Gansu Province.

January: "Old accounts" are short by 1,099,574.359 yuan, "New revenue" from land tax, commodity tax, regular and miscellaneous taxes, etc., totals 184,584.773 yuan, "Expenditures" on party affairs, internal affairs, finance, education, military affairs, judiciary, construction, transportation, and various expenses, totals 358,705.385 yuan, "Comparison" of expenditures exceeds by 174,120.612 yuan.

February: "Old accounts" are short by 1,273,694.971 yuan, "New revenue" totals 119,423.024 yuan, "Expenditures" total 201,186.835 yuan, "Comparison" of expenditures exceeds by 81,763.811 yuan.

March: "Old accounts" are short by 1,355,458.782 yuan, "New revenue" totals 290,087.264 yuan, "Expenditures" total 278,877.006 yuan, "Comparison" of new revenue exceeds by 11,210.258 yuan. In addition, there is also new revenue and old savings from the social obligations donation. After deducting expenses such as Zhongshan Hospital, Gansu National Medical Branch, Provincial Relief Institute, Relief Committee, relief funds for various counties, and former porridge factory, the actual savings are 181,483.198 yuan (Note to this table: Under the actual savings item, the previous finance department misappropriated and underpaid the principal amount of 140,911.802 yuan).

According to the above numbers, the total surplus from comparing the revenue and expenditure of the three months is 244,674.165 yuan. With such a large surplus in three months, and considering the past years of deficit, the surplus at the end of the year should reach several hundred thousand yuan. Among them, military expenditure accounts for the largest share of expenditure, and the index of construction, education, and other expenses is very weak. This is why the authorities recently reduced military expenditure and requested assistance from the central government. When the central government strictly ordered local governments to abolish exorbitant taxes and prohibit additional land taxes, the province's past revenue index, on the contrary, showed miscellaneous taxes occupying the highest position. Under such special circumstances, it is truly not easy to reorganize taxation.

Suzhou's Plan to Dredge the Wusong River 69

Dredging the Wusong River has been included in the outline of the water conservancy construction plan by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. It has been decided to subsidize 500,000 yuan for construction this winter, and the Taihu Basin Water Conservancy Committee has been entrusted to measure and prescribe the construction plan. The Wusong River surveying team organized by the committee has already set off a month ago, first going to the downstream to carry out surveying. On the 5th of this month, Sun Fushi, the secretary-general of the committee, accompanied by Liu Zhongwei, the head of the surveying and mapping section, took a steamboat from Guajingkou in Wujiang down the river to Shanghai, for a detailed inspection. When reporters visited them the other day, they said that reeds were growing in Guajingkou outside the upper reaches of the Wusong River, almost turning it into land, and a deep waterway should be opened up to facilitate water discharge. The section from Guajingkou to Jianghe Village is about 10 kilometers long and is slightly silted up. However, there are many lakes and branching rivers nearby, and there are very few boats traveling back and forth, so dredging has no major relationship with transportation and water discharge. If funds are sufficient, dredging it will be more convenient for shipping. The section from Jianghe Village to Qingyang Port is about 44 kilometers long. The river is wide and the water is deep, and the situation is very good. From Qingyang Port, more and more boats travel back and forth. The section from Qingyang Port to Xugong Port is about 24 kilometers long. The river is about 60 meters wide, and the riverbed is still deep, so there is no need for dredging. The section from Xugong Port to Xiaoshadu is about 38 kilometers long. The tide does not reach it, and it is so silted up that it is unbearable. Water transport is at its busiest, and dredging is urgently needed. This section of the river is narrow, less than 50 meters wide, and the bends are particularly severe. According to the villagers nearby, there are as many as seventy-two large and small bends. The worst ones are Fengjiabang, Yujidun, and Fanwangdu. Therefore, it is still necessary to widen and straighten this section. Two-thirds of this section is in Jiangsu Province, and one-third is in Shanghai. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has already designated the funds and will start construction soon. However, there is no news from the Shanghai Municipal Government, so the committee has submitted a request to the Ministry of the Interior to forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Government, asking them to raise funds as soon as possible so that construction can start simultaneously upstream and downstream.

Wuxi

Villagers Open Gambling Den and Gather to Resist Arrest 70

In the Xusheli area near Zhangshe in the fourth district, Tanhuang opera performances have been held recently, and gambling dens have been opened, attracting crowds to gamble. After receiving a secret report, the Public Security Bureau sent inspectors and patrol team members to the countryside to arrest them at about 8:00 p.m. the night before last. At that time, the gamblers were calling out numbers and enjoying themselves when they saw the police team coming to the countryside. A gambler named Yuan Achang took the lead in shouting to resist arrest, and Wu Ada and others used long benches and other objects to attack the police officers. For a time, the noise was deafening and the order was in chaos. Seeing the situation was bad, the police team fired warning shots and arrested eleven gamblers including Yuan Achang, Wu Ada, and Zhou Peixing on the spot. Unexpectedly, after walking only a few steps, the gamblers united hundreds of villagers and chased after them, hoping to snatch them away. After the police team fired warning shots again, the pursuers retreated. After walking about two *li*, the gamblers came again, and the police officers had to fire warning shots three times before they fled in all directions. That night, the arrested gamblers were taken to the bureau and transferred to the court yesterday for interrogation.

Provincial Committee Members Come to Wuxi to Survey the Famine 71

This year's drought and famine have affected more than 300,000 *mu* of fields in this county. Previously, the county government committee members went to various districts to survey the famine and requested the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Departments to send committee members to Wuxi for a repeat survey. It is now known that the Finance Department has ordered Ye Tiesheng, the accounting director of Wujin County, and the Construction Department has ordered Tang Xixiang, the director of the silkworm test station, to be famine survey committee members in this county. They arrived in Wuxi the day before yesterday. After meeting with County Magistrate Yan, they went with the original survey committee members of this county, Zang Hu and Zhu Fang, to inspect the fourth and sixth districts. They are scheduled to go to the ninth district for inspection again today.

Large Shipment of Opium Transported to Wuxi for Sale 72

The three local opium dens, Yongxing, Futai, and Dachang, officially opened yesterday (the 14th). Earlier, each business sent representatives to the town of Zhenjiang to negotiate with the Yongfeng and Tongchang opium warehouses. They purchased five large crates of Sichuan and Yunnan opium, totaling 5,000 taels. At around 9 PM the previous evening, they hired a car to travel directly from the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway to Jurong. From Jurong, they transferred to Lishui, Liyang, and Yixing before reaching Wuxi. Along the way, they were protected by soldiers from the Provincial Security Department. Upon arrival at the Yuantong Road intersection inside Guangfu Gate, the goods were unloaded and transported by rickshaw to each business for sale. However, the total number of opium smokers in this county is approximately 15,000, with 9,577 registered. The amount of opium transported to Wuxi this time is insufficient to meet the demand. Therefore, there are plans to continue purchasing goods from Zhenjiang within the next few days. The county's anti-opium association has completed the registration of opium smokers, and all smoker licenses have been filled out. Therefore, the following regulations for issuing licenses to opium smokers have been specially formulated: 1. Opium smokers must begin collecting their licenses from their original registration location starting October 16th, until October 31st. 2. When collecting their licenses, opium smokers must present their original receipt and submit three 2.5-inch headshot photographs. Licenses will not be issued without photographs. 3. Opium smokers must follow the procedures to collect their licenses. All registration locations are strictly prohibited from collecting service fees. Violators will be investigated and severely punished.

Zhang Yu, a woman from Xiangshan, had been selling and smoking red pills for years, residing at No. 5, Jiezhu Lane in this port. The order was presented to the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission's Nanchang Headquarters and approved.
