Page 10

Local News

Ministry of Finance Increases Silver Export Tax to Prevent Silver Export 79

Currently, the silver export tax rate has been specially formulated.

An order was issued to the Customs Administration to instruct its subordinates to comply.

The order will be uniformly implemented starting the 15th of this month.

The Ministry of Finance, based on a request from the Shanghai Silver and Money Exchange Association and others to find ways to prevent the export of silver, has specially formulated a silver export tax rate. It will be uniformly implemented starting the 15th of this month. Yesterday, an order was issued to the Customs Administration to instruct the Inspector General of Customs and the Superintendents and Commissioners of Customs to comply. A New News Agency reporter found and recorded the original submission and order as follows:

Submission from the Silver and Money Exchange Association, etc. 80

A submission from the Shanghai Silver and Money Exchange Association and others to the Ministry of Finance states: Regarding the matter of requesting measures to prevent silver exports, since the price of silver overseas has risen sharply, domestic silver in China has been concentrated in Shanghai and then exported abroad. The amount of exports is increasing daily, leading to financial desolation and economic depression in the interior. The amount of silver in Shanghai has been gradually increasing due to exports, and as the price of silver rises, domestic prices are falling, making it impossible for factories to maintain operations, and workers are roaming the streets. If this continues, we fear that resources will be depleted, affecting finance, the national economy, and the people's livelihood, all of which will suffer. Your Excellency presides over the nation's financial policies and is aware of these dangerous signs. Therefore, we earnestly appeal that you quickly take measures to prevent this, to protect resources and maintain the national foundation. We await your orders with the utmost respect. Respectfully submitted to Minister of Finance Kong, Lin Kanghou of the National Federation of Commerce, Qin Runqing, representative of the Money Exchange Association, Chen Zeqing, representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Ye Fuxiao and Chen Guangfu, representatives of the Banking Association.

Order from the Ministry of Finance to the Customs Administration 81

An order from the Ministry of Finance to the Customs Administration states: Director Shen of the Customs Administration, Shanghai Banking Association, Money Exchange Association, and Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce have submitted that recently, overseas silver prices have risen sharply, domestic silver reserves are increasingly being exported, and there are concerns that resources will be depleted, affecting finance, the national economy, and the people's livelihood. They earnestly request prompt measures to prevent this. China uses silver as its standard, and the currency material should be carefully preserved. If the price of silver rises sharply and differs greatly from general prices, it will inevitably affect finance and harm society. The balance of international exchange rates should also be maintained. The association's request to take measures to prevent this and protect resources is essential. Therefore, the silver export tax rate is specially formulated as follows: (1) Silver standard coins will be subject to an export tax of 10%, minus a minting fee of 2.25%, resulting in a net tax of 7.75%. (2) Large silver ingots and other types of silver will be subject to an additional export tax of 7.75%, combined with the original 2.25%, for a total of 10%. If the exchange rate of the London silver price converted to Shanghai exchange is different from the exchange rate approved by the Central Bank that day, a balancing tax should be added according to the difference after paying the above export tax. This will be uniformly implemented starting the 15th of this month. You are hereby ordered to instruct the Inspector General of Customs and the Superintendents and Commissioners of Customs to comply and implement this order.

Central Bank Announcement 82

The Central Bank announces that, starting October 15th of this year, in accordance with the government's instructions on silver export taxation, the bank will calculate the difference between the London silver price and the Shanghai telegraphic transfer to London, and notify customs after approving it at 11:30 AM every business day for easy conversion. This is hereby announced.

Sino-American Negotiations on the Silver Issue 83

The American Reply to Our Country Has Been Forwarded to the Capital

Balanced Imports and Exports Can Prevent Silver Outflow

According to a New News Agency report, the Ministry of Finance is exchanging views with the U.S. government on the issue of China's large silver exports. Yesterday, according to sources, the U.S. reply to China has been forwarded from Washington to the capital. However, the content of the reply will not be announced until the Chinese and American authorities agree on a date. Regarding remedial measures for silver exports, according to the opinion of a certain economic expert, to prevent the export of silver, the people of the country should implement the use of domestic goods in principle. Since China is an importing country, as long as the people of the country have a unified determination not to use foreign goods and to balance imports and exports, silver will not flow out, and the price of silver will stabilize accordingly.

Chamber of Commerce Cables the Central Political Council to Correct the Stamp Tax Law 84

The Tax Rate is Increased Up to Fifty Times Compared to the Current Rate

Commercial Strength Cannot Bear the Burden; It Should Be Corrected According to Law

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Central Political Council yesterday, requesting the correction of the stamp tax rate. The original text reads: Nanjing Central Political Council, in the principle of the Stamp Tax Law passed by the Council last year, Article 5 states that the stamp duty should be heavier for certificates that have greater effect or rights, or that are used for a longer period, and the stamp duty should be lighter for certificates that have lesser effect or rights, or that are used for a shorter period. Article 6 states that certificates of frequent acts should mostly adopt a simple and easy fixed-rate tax, and certificates of rare acts should mostly adopt an easy-to-calculate progressive tax. It is now reported that the Stamp Tax Law decided by the Legislative Yuan, such as the most common shipping invoices, bills, and silver receipts in the business community, will be taxed one cent for those from three yuan to ten yuan, and one cent will be added for every ten yuan thereafter, up to one yuan. According to the situation, a progressive tax law is adopted, which is obviously inconsistent with Article 6 of the principles set by the Council. Compared with the current stamp tax regulations, the above items are limited to two cents, but now they are limited to one yuan. Compared with each other, the price is almost fifty times higher, and the use time of invoices and bills, with the monthly closing of accounts at the end of the month, is mostly half a month or a month, and the annual closing of accounts is only three festivals at most. It is very short, and the tax is increased up to fifty times compared to the current rate, which is also inconsistent with Article 5 of the principles set by the Council. According to the law, if a merchant has goods worth a thousand yuan, from issuing the goods and opening the account to receiving the payment, he must pay three yuan in stamp duty, which is equivalent to paying a tax of three thousandths of the price of the goods, while the current regulations require only three cents of stamp duty, regardless of the price, from issuing the goods to receiving the payment. Compared with each other, the difference is a hundred times, which is difficult for businesses to bear. It is requested to correct it quickly based on the principles decided last year. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Disaster Report 91

After the formalities were completed, Xu Shiying gave a report, saying that since the beginning of summer this year, rainfall has been out of season, and drought has been severe. The disaster situation is rare. As of September 25, the Relief Committee has repeatedly received reports from the Civil Affairs Departments of the provinces, the Relief Committee, and the county-level organizations and groups, and collected materials from the Industrial Department's Central Agricultural Experiment Institute to compile statistics. This year's drought area covers 369 counties in eleven provinces, including 74 in Jiangxi, 71 in Zhejiang, 62 in Hunan, 47 in Anhui, 32 in Jiangsu, 24 in Hubei, 23 in Shanxi, 15 in Hebei, 11 in Henan, 8 in Gansu, and 2 in Guizhou. The affected cultivated land is about 133.83 million mu. Although there are no accurate statistics on the number of victims, it is estimated to be more than 10 million people. There are still reports arriving later. In addition, the flood disaster this year is not light. According to reports, there are about 280 counties in fourteen provinces, including Hebei, Shaanxi, and Shanxi, with about 31.025 million mu of affected cultivated land. The concise list of disaster situations in the provinces in 23 years has been compiled and sent. Although it cannot be said to be very detailed, it is enough as a reference. It is a pity that disasters have been frequent in recent years, the rural areas have been declining, and now they have suffered a great calamity. In the blink of an eye, the winter season is approaching, and there is no food or clothing. Hunger and cold are intertwined. How can our disaster-stricken people spend the end of the year? How should we plan relief to save the people's lives and consolidate the country's foundation? I sincerely ask you to express your great insights and plan together. I can't help but look forward to it.

Chairman's Speech 92

Chairman Kong Xiangxi said in his speech, "Our country has been plagued by floods for years, and now it is followed by severe drought. According to a survey by the Ministry of Finance, the disaster in the Yangtze River basin is caused by the lack of rain for three or four months, resulting in barren land and people unable to make a living. People should have a spirit of mutual assistance, and should work for mankind, society, and the country. Today, all sectors of Shanghai have initiated the fundraising of the Drought Relief Association in the provinces to engage in relief and enable people all over the country to avoid freezing and starvation. However, the disaster situation is serious, and it is only possible to have economic benefits if we all make efforts together. Some compatriots are also immersed in cigarettes and alcohol, and are unwilling to contribute even a hair or a penny to relief efforts. However, disaster relief is our duty, and we should work hard to raise funds and actively carry out relief efforts. In addition to relief, we should also work hard to dredge rivers and build roads. In this way, the disaster of floods and droughts can be reduced in the future. This is the main point of today's meeting."

Election of President 93

Immediately after, Chairman Lin of the National Government was elected Honorary President, and Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, Ju Zheng, Chu Minyi, and six others were elected Honorary Vice Presidents. Kong Xiangxi was elected President, and Xu Shiying, Wang Zhengting, Wang Yiting, and three others were elected Vice Presidents. In addition to the attendees as natural directors and supervisors, the remaining directors and supervisors were appointed by the President and Vice Presidents, and the directors of each group were appointed. (1) General Affairs Group: Qu Wenliu as Director, Huang Hanzhi and Qian Jinping as Deputy; (2) Fundraising Group: Du Yuesheng as Director, Gui Yanfang and Zhang Weiruo as Deputy; (3) Finance Group: Zhao Jinqing as Director, Lin Kanghou and Song Ziliang as Deputy; (4) Design Group: Wang Xiaolai as Director, Chu Huiseng and Guan Jiongzhi as Deputy; (5) Investigation and Distribution Group: Wen Lanting as Director, Li Shoushan and Gu Jisheng as Deputy; (6) Audit Group: Zhang Xiaolin as Director, Pan Xulun and Xu Yongzuo as Deputy; (7) Chief Secretary Fan Zhenchu, Huang Bodu as Deputy.

Articles of Association 94

The Articles of Association of the Shanghai All-Circles Drought Relief Association for the Provinces. Article 1: The name of this association is the Shanghai All-Circles Drought Relief Association for the Provinces. Anyone who supports the purpose of this association is a member of this association. Article 2: The members of this association publicly elect one president and three vice presidents to preside over the association's affairs, and several directors and supervisors. The directors publicly elect several executive directors, and the supervisors publicly elect several executive supervisors to handle the association's affairs. This association publicly elects one honorary president and several vice presidents to guide the association's affairs. Article 3: This association has one chief secretary and one deputy chief secretary, who are publicly elected by the Standing Committee of Directors, with the approval of the President and Vice Presidents, to handle affairs. Article 4: This association is divided into the following groups: (A) General Affairs Group: in charge of documents, accounting, general affairs, receiving and dispatching, recording, reporting, and matters not belonging to other groups; (B) Fundraising Group: in charge of planning and raising relief funds and goods; (C) Finance Group: in charge of receiving relief funds and goods, storing, remitting, purchasing grain seeds; (D) Design Group: in charge of planning the association's progress and relief plans; (E) Investigation and Distribution Group: in charge of investigating distribution and agricultural and industrial relief, and transportation matters; (F) Audit Group: in charge of auditing the receipt and payment of relief funds and goods and the association's expenses. Article 5: Each group in the preceding article has one director and two deputy directors, who are appointed by the Standing Committee of Directors. Article 6: The meetings of this association are as follows: (1) The General Assembly is held once a month; (2) The Standing Committee of Directors meets once a week; (3) If there are urgent matters, special meetings may be held. Article 7: This association may set up secretaries and staff according to the complexity of the affairs, to handle the affairs of each group, and may employ clerks to specialize in writing. Article 8: The President, Vice Presidents, Standing Directors, Supervisors, Chief Secretary, Deputy Chief Secretary, and Directors and Deputy Directors are all honorary positions. If it is deemed necessary to provide subsidies to secretaries, staff, and clerks, the Standing Committee of Directors shall determine it. Article 9: These Articles of Association shall be implemented from the date of establishment of this association.

Fundraising Declaration 95

The Fundraising Declaration of the Shanghai All-Circles Drought Relief Association for the Provinces states: Since the beginning of summer this year, rainfall has been out of season, and drought has been severe. According to reports, more than 369 counties in Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangsu, Henan, Hebei, Shanxi, Gansu, Guizhou, and other provinces have been affected by disasters. More than 133 million mu of farmland have been damaged, and even water sources have been completely dry, and there has been no harvest. Families committing suicide have been repeatedly seen in newspapers, and cannibalism is likely to take shape. It is a pity that disasters have been frequent in recent years, the rural areas have been declining, and now they have suffered a great calamity. In the blink of an eye, the winter season is approaching, and there is no food or clothing. Hunger and cold are intertwined. How can our disaster-stricken people spend the end of the year? We still have a breath, and relief cannot be delayed. Saving the country starts with saving the people, and benefiting others means benefiting oneself. It is hoped that everyone will work together to overcome the famine for one year, and that people will surely overcome the heavens and look forward to a bumper harvest next year. The future of the nation depends on it. At the beginning of the establishment of this association, we swear to be sincere and compassionate, and to perform our duties in a comprehensive and strict manner. We dare to ask people of insight from all walks of life to be brave for righteousness, open their pockets to help each other, give money to send grain, save those who are drowning, and relieve the drought. Spreading benevolence to the fields is no different from giving rain, and comparing virtue to hills is not just looking forward to the clouds. I shed tears to state my case, and I hope for your public judgment.

The Two Railway Bureaus Invite Bids for the Construction of the Sujia Section of the Railway Branch Line

The Entire Line is Divided into Six Small Sections, with Earthwork Construction to Be Built First

After the Ministry of Railways approved the construction of the Sujia section of the railway, the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Bureaus announced yesterday that they would invite bids for the earthwork construction first, so as to start construction. It is scheduled to be completed in one year. The details are recorded as follows:

Invitation to Bid: The Two Railway Bureaus announced the invitation to bid for the earthwork project of the Sujia section, stating that the railway plans to connect Jiaxing from Suzhou, passing through Wujiang, Pingwang, Shengze, Wangjiangjing, and other places. The construction of the new line is 75 kilometers long and is divided into six small sections. Contractors are invited to contract the earthwork project first. All small sections will start construction at the same time. All nationals with the project experience and ability and who are registered as Class A by the provincial and municipal governments (regardless of whether they have registered with the railway or not) who are willing to contract one or more small sections may, from October 21st, receive drawings, bidding regulations, construction instructions, and bid forms from the Engineering Department of the Railway Administration Bureau, Riverside Building, North Suzhou Road, Shanghai, and pay a handling fee of three yuan and a drawing deposit of fifteen yuan. The deadline is the end of October. The bidding and opening dates will be notified when the drawings are collected. This announcement.

Facilitating Transportation: It is planned to start construction within the year after the bidding and complete it in one year. The funds will be allocated by the Ministry of Railways. The section starts from Suzhou Station of the Jinghu section, passes through Wujiang, Shengze, Wangjiangjing, and ends at Jiaxing Station of the Huhangyong section, connecting Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The section along the line is very important for national defense transportation, and is rich in local products. In the future, after the completion of the Huhangyong section, local products along the Zhayong section, such as vegetable oil, tin foil, Shaoxing wine, fresh fruits, grains, hemp, silk cocoons, cotton yarn, sugar, and sugarcane, can be quickly transported to North China and Central China through the Sujia section, which can shorten the travel time and avoid congestion.

上寳沙田官産局實行丈測官産沙田 98

Notice to All Households to Register with the Shanghai County Government

The Industrial Society reports that Shanghai and Baoshan counties, bordering the river and sea, have many state-owned sandy fields. These fields have long been occupied and cultivated by local people, with reed marshes being the main product. The annual harvest is entirely privately owned by the people, and there are no fixed acreages or boundaries, leading to frequent disputes. No grain taxes have been paid, resulting in no revenue for the provincial treasury. In view of this, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance has instructed the Shanghai-Baoshan Sandy Field State Property Bureau in this city to actively engage in surveying and measuring. It also ordered the county governments of Shanghai and Baoshan to levy grain taxes on state-owned sandy fields. Yesterday, a reporter from the Industrial Society interviewed Wang Jiaolin, the director of the Sandy Field State Property Bureau. According to him, the surveying and measuring of sandy fields in the two counties is largely complete, but it has not yet been carried out for the reed marshes along the coast in the southeast of Shanghai County. The bureau has already submitted a request to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance for approval to implement the surveying and measuring. Therefore, it is planned to formally commence the work after the announcement. All state-owned land with grain in the area will be allowed to register with the Shanghai County Government, and land without grain production will also be allowed to be reported, so as to unify state-owned property. The procedures for this will be jointly announced by the bureau and the Shanghai County Government to inform the public. The county government will be responsible for handling the procedures for collecting grain taxes. The bureau's announcement is transcribed below: Announcement regarding the investigation of the reed marshes along the coast in the southeast of Shangyi (Shanghai County), which stretch far and wide and have long been occupied and cultivated by the people. This not only hinders the revenue of the provincial treasury but also makes it impossible to determine property rights, leading to confusion of boundaries and repeated disputes. This bureau has submitted a request to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, and has received Instruction No. 11502, approving the implementation of surveying and measuring in accordance with the established case of the Fengnan Bureau to facilitate clearing up. All households that have already paid the price and bear grain obligations should immediately bring their documents to the bureau for registration. Those households that occupy land with or without grain obligations are allowed to pay the price and obtain ownership certificates as soon as possible for proof of their business. All of the above must be done within twenty days from the date of this announcement. Those who violate, delay, or conceal information, and fail to report within the deadline, will have their unclaimed state-owned land re-leased by the bureau. There will be no tolerance. For the sake of solemnly protecting the property rights of the original households, the Shanghai County Government has been jointly issuing announcements. This announcement is hereby made.

土地局不動産抵押規則發生糾紛 99

Land Bureau's Real Estate Mortgage Rules Cause Disputes 100

Registration Rules Clearly Conflict with Civil Law

All Losses Will Be Difficult to Bear in the Future

A document from the Shanghai Lawyers Association to the Judicial Yuan states: "Regarding the obvious conflict between the city's single regulations and the current civil law, please forward it to the Executive Yuan for an order to abolish it. Qian Zhongdao, a member of the association, writes: 'Respectfully, previously, the client Zhang Heqing stated that on November 15th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, Heqing mortgaged his own property located at No. 35 Sanyutang Humin District Sanyuan Huangziwei, consisting of one mu, three fen, four ku, and three hao of land, along with the residential buildings on it, to Zhu Hongnan. Both parties signed a real estate mortgage contract, stating a mortgage amount of 60,000 taels of silver and a mortgage term of two years. They also registered the mortgage with the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau according to the real estate mortgage regulations. However, after the mortgage, the actual amount of the mortgage silver was reduced to 40,000 taels. When the two-year term expired, the mortgagor was temporarily unable to redeem the property, and it was agreed with the mortgagee to extend the term to May 10th of this year, and then again to November 10th. Unexpectedly, the mortgagee Zhu Hongnan, while agreeing to continue the extension, independently went to the Land Bureau to transfer the property, eliminating the mortgagor's property rights. The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau approved this unilateral action and officially notified and declared the elimination of all property rights of Sanyutang under the name of the mortgagor. This kind of unilateral action and the Land Bureau's implementation of this single regulation completely conflict with the explicit provisions of Article 873 of the Civil Law (Property Rights). One party completely loses its guarantee on the mortgaged property in fact, and Heqing loses real estate worth 100,000 yuan once due to a mortgage of 40,000 taels. Since the law does not provide for the follow-up of debt, what can be done about the loss? They had no choice but to ask the lawyers to provide legal remedies in order to recover the loss. Upon checking the judicial administrative regulations of this case, there are conflicts between the two parties, and it is impossible to follow the rules. It is known that your association has previously raised concerns with the higher judicial administrative organs regarding Article 5 of the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau's Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules, requesting interpretation. Based on the foregoing, the member believes that the rights and responsibilities of the parties involved are at stake. Therefore, they specifically request that you forward it to the higher judicial administrative authorities, order an interpretation of the conflict in the aforementioned regulations, so that there is something to follow, and also ask your association to take steps to help and remedy the situation.' It is argued that Article 5 of the Shanghai Land Bureau's Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules conflicts with Article 873, Section 2 of the current Civil Law. According to the principle that local regulations must not conflict with central laws, a letter was sent to the Municipal Government requesting correction. Later, a reply was received stating that the case in which your association requested the correction of the provisions of Article 5 of the Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules of the Land Bureau of this city was approved on May 1, 20th year of the Republic of China. A letter was sent stating that it was submitted to the Judicial Yuan for submission to the Executive Yuan, ordering its abolition. Until now, this government has not received the said order, so the request is difficult to approve. The Real Estate Registration Regulations implemented by the Shanghai Land Bureau were promulgated by the Beijing Government on May 21, 11th year of the Republic of China and should be approved for adoption according to the order of the National Government on August 12, 16th year of the Republic of China.) Matters under the jurisdiction of the court as stipulated in Article 3, Section 6, it is inevitable that the land administration authorities directly conducting real estate mortgage registration will conflict with the powers of the court before the Dengji Regulations are abolished and the Land Law (promulgated on March 3, 19th year) is implemented. Furthermore, the current Civil Law, regarding the definition of mortgage rights, Article 860 of the Civil Law clearly stipulates that "immovable property that is provided as security to a creditor or a third party without transferring possession may only be compensated from the proceeds of its sale." Furthermore, Article 873, Section 1 stipulates that "If the mortgage right has reached the repayment period but has not been repaid, the mortgage may apply to the court for the auction of the mortgaged property and receive compensation from the actual proceeds of the sale." At the beginning of central legislation, the method of exercising mortgage rights was clearly marked and should not be different. Therefore, Article 873, Section 2 of the same law also stipulates that "If it is agreed that the ownership of the mortgaged property shall be transferred to the mortgagee when the debt has reached the repayment period but has not been repaid, the agreement shall be invalid." Now, Article 5 of the Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules of the Shanghai Land Bureau stipulates that "the mortgage term shall be agreed upon by the mortgagee and the mortgagor and registered. If it is not redeemed after the expiration date, the mortgagee shall apply for transfer and be issued a land certificate in the name of the mortgagee, and the mortgagor's property rights shall be eliminated." The violation of the current regulations and the conflict with central laws are very obvious. According to Article 8 and Article 13 of the City Organization Law, the municipal government's handling of affairs and issuance of single regulations shall be limited to not conflicting with central laws. The Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules of the Land Bureau obviously violate the Civil Law and the Registration Regulations and are naturally invalid. The association believes that the illegal local regulations easily deprive the people of their rights and interests. On April 30, 20th year of the Republic of China, it requested the court to submit a request to the Judicial Yuan for submission to the Executive Yuan, ordering its abolition. After three years, no reply has been received. Now, according to the letter from member Qian Zhongdao, the Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules of the Shanghai Land Bureau, if they are not abolished one day, will not only affect the credibility of the central government, but it is not a small matter. The ownership of the people cannot be guaranteed. Therefore, it is requested that your department examine and approve it, and allow the submission to the Executive Yuan, ordering the Shanghai Municipal Government to abolish the Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules approved and promulgated by the Land Bureau immediately in order to correct the matter. This is for the public convenience, and so on."

川匯稍回跌旅滬川帮辦應時貨 101

Sichuan Exchange Rate Slightly Declines, Sichuan Merchants in Shanghai Purchase Seasonal Goods 102

The Xinsheng News Agency reports that after the surge in the Sichuan-Shanghai exchange rate, it rose to a maximum of 500 yuan per thousand yuan. Sichuan merchants, who purchased goods in Shanghai with Sichuan exchange, inevitably faced increased costs, greatly impacting sales. Consequently, they all telegraphed Sichuan businesses in Shanghai to suspend the purchase of outgoing goods and simultaneously convened discussions to find remedial measures. They decided to transport as much Sichuan native produce to Shanghai as possible to balance the Sichuan exchange rate. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency inquired at the Juxingcheng Bank yesterday and learned that the Sichuan-Shanghai exchange rate on October 13th was 1,398 yuan of Sichuan silver per 1,000 yuan, equivalent to 1,000 yuan of Shanghai silver, a decrease of over 100 yuan from the peak, but still more than 100 yuan higher than usual. The Sichuan merchants in Shanghai, mindful of the decline in the exchange rate, have long suspended the purchase of outgoing goods. As the Sichuan inventories are about to run out, they have been purchasing seasonal goods such as woolens and cotton yarn for shipment to Sichuan in recent days.

行兇獄囚不服原判 115

Convicted Prisoner Appeals Original Sentence for Assault 116

Appeals to the Collegiate Bench

Zhang Jinbao, a murderer from Yixing, nicknamed "Long-legged Jinbao," was sentenced to 20 years in prison for killing his apprentice, Gu Daosheng, from Dachang, at the Daji Lou Restaurant on Xiaodongmen Street in the French Concession on the afternoon of March 27th of last year. The case was investigated and prosecuted by the police and the Special Second Court. Zhang was dissatisfied and appealed to the High Third Branch Court, which rejected the appeal. He is now appealing to the Supreme Court for a third trial. The person is being held in the Special Second Court Detention Center. Unexpectedly, during the previous month, he had a dispute with a fellow inmate over smoking cigarettes. A guard, Zhu Fubao, stepped forward to stop him, but Zhang not only refused to comply but also assaulted the guard, causing injury. The detention center transferred Zhang to the Prosecutor's Office of the Special Second Court for investigation. After confirmation, he was prosecuted by the same-level criminal court for obstructing official duties. After interrogation by Judge Sun Pengxian, he was sentenced to six months in prison. The above has been reported previously. Now Zhang is dissatisfied with the verdict and has appealed to the collegiate bench. The Second Criminal Court was specially convened by Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu, along with Judges Xiong and Li, and Prosecutor Wang Ren for a preliminary hearing. According to Zhang's statement of the reasons for the appeal, the gist is that he did not assault the guard at the time, but was assaulted by the guard and was instead sentenced, which he was unwilling to accept. He requested an appeal. The court verified the confession and, due to incomplete testimony, ordered a postponement to summon witnesses to testify again. Zhang was still returned to the detention center.

捲烟漏稅之判罰 117

Penalties for Cigarette Tax Evasion 118

Wu Yaoou, a Western detective from the French Concession Cigarette Investigation Division of the Unified Tax Inspection Office of the Taxation Administration of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, along with Chinese detectives Zhou Baosheng, Zhu Qiming, and Zhao Chengshou, recently discovered that Qiu Mingde, a Ningbo native residing at No. 21 Sanqing Lane, Ximen Road, French Concession, age 38, established the Shanghai Ningtai Xinji Tobacco Company in his residence. The Jingzhong brand cigarettes produced by the company were manufactured by the Donghai Tobacco Factory at No. 25 Kai'ai Lai Road, without reporting to the Cigarette Unified Tax Inspection Office and evading taxes for sale on the market. This constituted collusion with the Donghai Tobacco Factory to cheat, violating tax regulations. Therefore, they immediately went to Qiu's home to search and confiscated 37 packs of Jingzhong brand tax-evading cigarettes wrapped in old wax paper, as well as 68 packs of the same loose cigarettes, and moldy cigarettes, totaling 213 packs, or 28,000 cigarettes, all manufactured by the Donghai Tobacco Factory. The cigarettes, along with Qiu Mingde and Shi Shenkang (age 46, Zhejiang native), the deputy manager of the Donghai Tobacco Factory, were taken to the police station. The morning before, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Special Second Court. Judge Wu Fanglian interrogated them. Police lawyer Yuan Jiahuang explained the case, and prosecuted them according to Articles 27, Section 5 and 10 of the Penalties for Tax-Evading Cigarettes of the Unified Tax Inspection Office of the Taxation Administration of the Ministry of Finance. Detective Zhu Qiming reported the search process and presented the confiscated tax-evading cigarettes to the court. The defendants, Qiu Mingde and Shi Shenkang, admitted to evading taxes for sale and manufacturing cigarettes on behalf of others. The court verified the confession and immediately announced the judgment: Qiu Mingde and Shi Shenkang were fined 150 yuan each for colluding to sell cigarettes wrapped in wax paper with false stamps to evade taxes. The confiscated tax-evading cigarettes were confiscated and turned over to the state.

Penalties for Trafficking in Red Pills 120

Ding Yanlong, from Xuzhou, was found in possession of sixty red pills of drugs at noon on the 10th of this month while passing through the jurisdiction of the Fifth Police Station of the Third District of Zhabei. Detective Zheng immediately went to the Jiaxing Road Police Station to request assistance in apprehending the shopkeeper. The police chief sent detective Zhao Lianbi secretly to arrest Chen Guifa, a Haiyan native who owned the shop. He learned that there was a distribution point at No. 243 on the same road, and then arrested his partner, Zhou Shuangfu, and confiscated a large number of red pills. They were taken to the police station together. The next morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court. The two defendants gave evasive confessions. The Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, stated that the defendants' addresses were all in the concession and did not need to be transferred. It was ordered to return them to custody. The other day, Judge Xiao Xiehan came to the Third Criminal Court to take confessions clearly, and sentenced Chen Guifa to one year and six months in prison and a fine of one hundred yuan, and Zhou Shuangfu to one year and six months. The evidence was confiscated.

Representatives of the Child Welfare Conference Visit Child Welfare Organizations 128

Representatives From Various Regions To Leave Shanghai Soon To Establish Associations

Declaration Drafted, Still Needs Revision and Publication

The National Child Welfare Leaders Conference, held in Shanghai for three days, successfully concluded the night before last. Many resolutions related to improving child welfare were passed and will be earnestly implemented. Child welfare organizations from various regions decided to join the association as group members. Representatives will separately return to their respective provinces and cities to organize local child welfare associations. It is hoped that the entire national child welfare cause will achieve widespread development, a cause for celebration for the country's future. At the final meeting the day before yesterday, the discussion of proposals lasted a long time, and the closing ceremony was not held until after 7 PM. The ceremony was quite grand, and there was a grand banquet hosted by Chairman Kong at 8 PM. Yesterday, the representatives continued to visit various child welfare organizations in the city. Starting today, the representatives from various regions will gradually leave Shanghai. The details are as follows:

Grand Closing Ceremony The Night Before Last 129

The closing ceremony of the conference was held at approximately 7 PM the night before last. Those in attendance included Xu Shiying, Qu Wenliu, Zhao Jinqing, Zhu Qinglan, Du Yuesheng, Lu Bohong, and over a hundred representatives and guests. Mr. Xiong Xiling also attended despite his illness. After formal ceremonies, Chairman Kong Xiangxi delivered the closing remarks, followed by Xiong Xiling, who congratulated the conference on its success and encouraged the representatives to promote child welfare. Subsequently, Kong read the conference declaration, and all the representatives took an oath. After the ceremony, Chairman Kong hosted a banquet for all the representatives at the New Asia Hotel, with music performances and movies for entertainment.

Visits To Various Locations Yesterday 130

Yesterday, taking advantage of the break after the closing ceremony, all the representatives were led by the association's Deputy General Secretary to visit the First Nursery in Nanshi, Xin Puyu Hall, Longhua Orphanage, the Shanghai Medical College Lung Sanatorium in Ye Family Garden in Jiangwan, and Sacred Heart Hospital, among other places. Associations To Be Established In Various Regions 131

After the representatives return to their respective provinces and cities, they will immediately begin organizing. Child welfare organizations from various regions will join the association as group members. The organizational outline is currently being drafted, and annual meetings will be convened in the future. However, the second conference is unlikely to be held next year.

Declaration Not Yet Revised 132

The conference declaration, drafted by the drafting committee, was read aloud at the conference the night before last. Most representatives argued that the wording still needed revision and was sent to the conference secretariat for revision. Because the original text was very long, it has not yet been completed and cannot be published for the time being. The general content is to promote the active maintenance of child welfare by people across the country.

Four Major Oil Companies Plot to Monopolize the Market and Boycott Diesel Fuel Refining into Kerosene 135

Sales Will Be Stopped Immediately Upon Discovery

Gasoline Sales Have Suddenly Increased in Recent Months

According to Da Gong She, after the kerosene market in China was monopolized by the United Kingdom, the United States, and Russia, the market price once fell. However, after the four major companies agreed on a distribution agreement, prices were immediately raised uniformly. Recently, they have jointly boycotted the refining of diesel fuel into kerosene and plan to actively promote the gasoline market. The details are as follows:

Boycott of Diesel Fuel Refining into Kerosene: It is reported that the four major kerosene companies in China, Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, Deuto-Gubkin, and Guanghua, have recently learned that Chinese people have successfully refined kerosene from diesel fuel, which they believe will greatly harm their kerosene business. Therefore, they have united to boycott it. The method is that the diesel fuel sold by each company in the future will only be used for machinery needs. If buyers are found to be refining kerosene, their right to purchase will be terminated. If companies sell it privately, they will be severely punished.

Gasoline Sales Suddenly Increase: It is also reported that the gasoline sold by each company has recently seen a sharp increase in use due to the gradual development of highway construction in China. The sales volume is becoming more active every day. The original national sales volume per month was 500,000 to 700,000 gallons, but in recent days, it has surged to about one million gallons. It is said that each company is also planning to actively promote its market in order to recover the losses during the period of competitive sales.

The Case of Two Women Arguing Over Position After Cheng Zhong'an's Death 143

Each Side Has Witnesses for Who Is the First Wife

The Purpose of the Lawsuit Is All About Money

丨The Judge Divides the Money for Both Parties丨

Cheng Zhong'an, a native of Sichuan, was a foreign goods broker who traveled between Shanghai, Beijing, and other places. He was extremely capable. After several years of operation, he accumulated a lot of wealth. This spring, Cheng Zhong'an and his nephew Fan Weisheng went to Beijing for trade. Unfortunately, he died of illness there in March, leaving behind tens of thousands of gold. However, Cheng had two wives during his lifetime, one was Li Abao (i.e., Cheng Li's), and the other was Jiang Yueying (i.e., Cheng Jiang's). Both lived in Shanghai, living separately. At that time, Fan immediately sent a letter to the two women, reporting the bad news. Li Abao and Jiang Yueying, after receiving the letter, had an identity problem due to the inheritance relationship, and each filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai District Court, slandering each other and demanding confirmation of Cheng Zhong'an's first wife. Each had their own reasons and presented marriage witnesses. Who exactly was the formal couple was not known to outsiders. Li Abao claimed to have been married to Cheng Zhong'an for twelve years and had a daughter who was eleven years old. She accused Jiang of being a concubine. However, Jiang Yueying claimed that she and Cheng were actually formally married, accusing Li Abao of being a casual union. The two sides attacked each other. After the court accepted the case, it had been hearing the case several times without a conclusion. The day before yesterday, Judge Han Zuoti continued to hear the case. First, witness Fan Weisheng testified, 27 years old, from Sichuan, doing medicinal material business. In 1924, my uncle Cheng Zhong'an asked me to come to Shanghai from my hometown and live with him. (Question) Who is your aunt? (Answer) Jiang Yueying. (Question) Who was the matchmaker? (Answer) I heard it was Wang Zhiya. (Question) In what year and where did they get married? (Answer) I heard it was in 1913, at Xiangfa Zhan near Zhengjia Muqiao. (Question) How much was the betrothal gift? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) Was the marriage time in the first half of the year or the second half of the year? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) Do you know Li Abao? (Answer) She is my little aunt, and she started living together in 1926. (Question) Your uncle died in March of this year. How much property did he leave behind? (Answer) At Jiang Yueying's place, there is a passbook from the Bank of China, totaling 1,500 yuan, and at Li Abao's place, there is a passbook from the Juxingcheng Bank, also for 1,500 yuan. (Question) Who has the passbook now? (Answer) Both are in Jiang Yueying's hands. Next, witness Wang Zhiya testified, 48 years old, and a friend of Cheng Zhong'an. I was the matchmaker for Jiang Yueying. (Question) How much was the matchmaker fee? (Answer) Sixty yuan. (Question) When did they get married? (Answer) In 1913, at Xiangfa Zhan in Zhengjia Muqiao. (Question) Did Cheng Zhong'an have a wife in Sichuan? (Answer) No. (Question) Who is Li Abao? (Answer) A mistress. (Question) Did she live with Cheng Zhong'an? (Answer) Yes. The interrogating officer obtained the confession. At the previous hearing, the witnesses presented by Li Abao proved that Li Abao and Cheng Zhong'an formally held a wedding ceremony twelve years ago, as if it were true. Today's witness also proves that Jiang Yueying is the formal couple. Which is right and which is wrong has already been preliminarily determined. In short, this lawsuit was started because of the money issue. Questioning Jiang Yueying how much money is in your account, she answered 3,000 yuan, etc. The officer said to Jiang Yueying, is the bank passbook with you? (Answer) They are all with me. (Question) How much is the amount? (Answer) A total of 3,000 yuan. Li Abao confessed that there is still property worth 40,000 to 50,000 in Beijing. Please order Fan Weisheng to hand it over. The officer said to Fan, how much property is there in Beijing? (Answer) Although there was 40,000 to 50,000 gold before, my uncle suffered repeated failures in business in Beijing and owed a lot of money. After repaying the debts, there are only 6,000 yuan left, which is not easy to collect for a while, etc. The interrogating officer obtained the confession and said to the two women, the current 3,000 yuan will be divided equally between the two parties. However, Li Abao has one more child and should get 500 yuan more, for a total of 3,000 yuan. Regarding the property in Beijing, order Fan Weisheng to quickly hand over all the account books to the case for inspection. Fan complied and left the court.

After repeated interrogations and investigations, the trial concluded, and yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui of the Eighth Criminal Court announced the verdict. The main points were: Xu Genyou and Chen Si, for continuously forming gangs and carrying weapons to commit robberies, were each sentenced to eight years of imprisonment. Liu Jixiu, for continuously assisting in forming gangs and carrying weapons to commit robberies, was sentenced to five years of imprisonment. Cui Anqing, for the crime of intending to provide military firearms to others for criminal purposes, was sentenced to one year of imprisonment, and for the crime of receiving stolen goods, was sentenced to three months of imprisonment, serving a total of one year and three months of imprisonment. Gao Asan, for continuous robbery, was sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment. The charges of homicide and conspiracy to commit robbery were found not guilty. Xu Rongcheng was sentenced to three years and two months of imprisonment. Xu Zhimei was sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment. Zhang Fengming was declared not guilty. Zhang Zilin was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. Wang Shanlin was sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment. Wang Chenshi was sentenced to two years of imprisonment. Yao Jinchu and Cao Guansheng were each sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Lu Yuanbing was sentenced to four years and two months of imprisonment. The confiscated guns and bullets were confiscated. Zhang Fengming was allowed to remain in custody during the appeal period.

Female Prisoner Requests to Bring Daughter to Jail 149

Judge Refuses, Orders Neighbors to Care for Her

Chen Wu, a woman from Wenzhou, and Shu Huifang, a woman from Ningbo, were recently caught privately consuming heroin pills at No. 84, Lane 690, East-West Huade Road. A few days ago, Chinese detective Sun Shaokun discovered this and, with the cooperation of foreign detectives, secretly went and arrested Chen and Shu, male and female, along with the woman's thirteen-year-old daughter. They were all taken to the Huishan Police Station and detained separately. The next morning, they were transferred to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Public Works Bureau lawyer Li Zhishan presented the case and submitted the evidence for investigation. After Judge Xiao interrogated the two defendants, they were each fined thirty yuan, and the evidence was confiscated. Chen Wu claimed she could not pay the fine and requested to be sentenced to fifteen days of detention instead. She requested that her thirteen-year-old daughter be allowed to join her in jail because there was no one at home to care for her. The court refused and instructed lawyer Li to order the Chinese police to send the girl to the second landlord of her residence to be temporarily cared for.

Rickshaw Covered in Fresh Blood 150

Doesn't Want to Be a Soldier, Shot

The day before yesterday afternoon, near Jing'an Temple in West Shanghai, a man covered in gunshot wounds and bleeding profusely was found sitting in a rickshaw. He was discovered by a patrolling officer and sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. According to the man, named Wu Fulin, twenty-one years old, from Changshu, he had just arrived in Shanghai four days ago to visit his younger brother at Gaochang Temple. He was tricked by three or four men into a house near the Little World entertainment district, where they urged him to become a soldier. Because he was afraid, he tried to escape. A guard spotted him and fired two shots, one hitting his shoulder and the other his waist. The guard then hired a rickshaw to take him to visit a friend on the Great Western Road, but he was apprehended and sent to the hospital. It is reported that the man's injuries are quite serious.

Li Zongtian and Yu Songnian

Li Zongtian, a forty-year-old Shandong native who previously worked as a detective in the Water Police Team, was given an English warrant by Detective Zhang Yunjian of the Yangshupu Police Station, entrusting him to arrest Yu Songnian (forty-four years old, from Jingjiang), the fugitive in the robbery case at the home of a certain person at No. 4 Huatongfang, Xizang Road, on December 3rd of last year. Special Items

Awakening to National Self-Reliance and Revival (3) 164

— By Zhang Yuanruo

丨At the China Vocational Education Society丨

4. The Motivation for Creating Self-Reliance: Why should I create self-reliance? What is the motivation? It can be discussed in four points: (1) In light of the emptiness of past national salvation movements, most of the so-called "movements" that are currently popular are, as Shanghainese say, a "rotten chorus," with no real substance. Some people say one thing with their mouths but think another in their hearts. During speeches, they are tearful and passionate, but when they turn around, they are laughing and joking, as if the nation does not exist and is irrelevant to them. Only personal vanity and self-interest matter to them. They are good at singing high-sounding tunes, but when it comes to doing real work, they are irresponsible. (2) In light of the national psychology of decline, the spirit of the people today can truly be described as flagging and very decadent. When doing things, they observe each other, shirk responsibility, and even criticize and undermine others while doing nothing themselves. On the other hand, when they see rights, they rush to the front. This can be seen when buying train tickets. Self-reliance is about emphasizing the obligations of the people, invigorating the spirit of the people, and inspiring the people's enthusiasm for saving and building the nation. (3) Based on the historical lessons of the nation, this point is too long to discuss in detail. Now, I can only briefly discuss it from both positive and negative sides. From the negative side, as I just said, the weakness of the Chinese nation is its susceptibility to the control of social inertia, which prevents national strength from developing and the country from having power. From the positive side, we can see that every nation in the world survives through self-improvement and hard work. In ancient times, King Goujian of Yue's "ten years of accumulation, ten years of training," where "training" refers to spiritual effort and "accumulation" refers to material effort. His efforts in education, economy, and all aspects resulted in the salvation of his country. To give a more recent example, after Germany was defeated by Napoleon, there was a philosopher named Fichte who said, "If we want to save the country and avenge our humiliation, we must first cultivate new seeds for the nation and bury ourselves in hard work for more than twenty years." From that moment on, the German people, from top to bottom, worked hard little by little, and eventually they defeated France. More recently, consider the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plans, both the first and the second. Which one was not about strengthening its national power? The longer they prepared, the more confident they became in defeating others. The Soviet Union understood the importance of national power, so it was advantageous for them to delay the war. Japan, on the other hand, was in favor of a quick war because they were already prepared. They had been working hard since the Meiji Restoration and were catching up head-on. The week before last, Mr. Wu Zhihui wrote an article in the Shanghai Morning Post, which included a passage saying that the progress of the Japanese in the past sixty years was truly astonishing. Eighty years ago, the Japanese did not even know what coal was. This statement was found by Mr. Wu in a major British newspaper and is not an exaggeration. At that time, Japan was oppressed by everyone, just like us. Since then, it has made every effort to carry out reforms, first defeating China, then defeating Russia, and now it is famous throughout the world. Even Russia, Britain, America, and France dare not lightly try to provoke it. In these sixty years, it has not only worked hard but has also caught up head-on. The whole country, regardless of men, women, old, or young, scholars, farmers, workers, or merchants, is working hard and burying themselves in their tasks, which is why it has such astonishing national strength today. Therefore, if a country wants to be successful and strong, it must undergo a long period of forging and preparation before it can succeed. It must not indulge in wishful thinking and seek luck, hoping to realize our ideals overnight. (4) Based on my advocacy over the years, although the articles I have published over the years cannot be considered good, I am not singing high-sounding tunes. I am sincerely speaking the truth. The creation of this self-reliance principle was on New Year's Day this year because I had many thoughts in my mind on New Year's Eve. I thought that with the start of the new year, the old year had passed. At this stage of carrying on the past and opening up the future, how should I strive for my new life? How should I reflect on my past mistakes? During my reflection, I came to a principle of effort, which is to save the country through self-reliance. At the same time, when we examine our previous articles, we also find a central idea. Although there are no words for self-reliance, they all contain the meaning of self-reliance. On the morning of New Year's Day, I picked up my pen and wrote an outline of self-reliance, which is divided into forty-five chapters. This is the process of my creating self-reliance.

5. The Definition and Content of Self-Reliance: The definition of self-reliance, in the most popular way, is a national salvation doctrine based on obligations and responsibilities, with the nation and society as the targets, and with national mobilization and self-improvement as the means. Its function is to touch the hearts of every citizen, inspire the nation-building enthusiasm and sense of responsibility of every citizen. Under this doctrine, every citizen should assume his or her responsibility to the country. Therefore, simply put, self-reliance is a kind of "actionism," a kind of "national actionism." When it comes to its content, it is very complicated. It can be roughly divided into four parts. The first part is the theory of self-reliance, which is divided into several chapters, such as the worldview of self-reliance, the historical view of self-reliance, the social view of self-reliance, the legal view of self-reliance, the national character of self-reliance, the timeliness of self-reliance, and the philosophical foundation of self-reliance. The second part is the comparison of self-reliance with various doctrines, such as the comparison of self-reliance with socialism, the comparison of self-reliance with liberalism and individualism, the comparison of self-reliance with democracy, and the comparison of self-reliance with fascism. The third part is about the movement of self-reliance, which is divided into the awakening of Chinese youth to save the country through self-reliance, the awakening of Chinese intellectuals to save the country through self-reliance, the awakening of Chinese farmers, workers, and merchants to save the country through self-reliance, and the awakening of Chinese civil servants to save the country through self-reliance, etc. This part focuses on how to promote the program of self-reliance and provides guidance to the entire population on how to strive. The fourth part is about the beliefs and creeds of self-reliance, which also has six or seven chapters. This is the outline of my self-reliance content. To speak in detail, it is impossible to finish in one day.

6. The Philosophical Foundation of Self-Reliance: I have very little research on philosophy and dare not say that I have any special insights. Moreover, I am now limited by time and can only talk about it very simply. (1) There is a Chinese saying, "Heaven moves with strength, and gentlemen strive for self-improvement without ceasing." The Chinese word "Heaven" has a very profound meaning, but from the perspective of our legal understanding, it can be regarded as a kind of "natural law." Gentlemen are relatively conscious and healthy people, such as all of you who came here to listen to the lecture in the heavy rain. You can all be considered gentlemen. As for the way of self-improvement, the most important thing is to never stop. If you are strong today but not tomorrow, you cannot be considered a gentleman. Because you have an exam tomorrow, you temporarily cram today, which does not count as self-improvement. Similarly, because of the stimulation of foreign aggression, you are temporarily passionate, crying bitterly, but after the event passes, you do not strive for improvement, which is also not self-improvement. Such people cannot be considered gentlemen. A gentleman must always strive without stopping for self-improvement. This is the natural law that Heaven has arranged for us. If we humans want to survive, we must follow this heavenly way, this natural law, and strive for self-improvement. Therefore, my self-reliance is based on this great, permanent, and universal natural law. I can say that self-reliance is not created by me; it is a natural principle, not my subjective invention, but a purely objective discovery. Therefore, if you do not strive for self-improvement, you are violating the way of Heaven, violating natural law, and you are not a gentleman. Even if you are a petty person, a petty person is a term that everyone does not like to hear. If you want to be a gentleman, you should embrace self-reliance. Speaking of natural law, although it has been criticized, it still has great power in modern legal philosophy. There is a movement in the French legal community called "the revival of natural law." Therefore, my thinking cannot be considered outdated and can even represent a new trend. In Chinese history, my doctrine also has a basis, such as Wang Yangming's theory of "unity of knowledge and action." In light of the fact that the people of the country were harming the country with empty words and not focusing on practical matters, he used the theory of unity of knowledge and action to correct the decadent and depressed psychology of the general public. It is said that the strength of the Japanese nation also benefited greatly from Wang Yangming's theory of unity of knowledge and action, which can further prove the great importance of my self-reliance to national revival. Secondly, Sun Yat-sen's theory of "knowing is difficult, doing is easy" can also be said to be the philosophical foundation of self-reliance. Regarding this point, everyone can read Sun Wen's theory, so I won't talk about it much. (2) In the West, my self-reliance also has its philosophical basis. The origins of Western philosophy can be divided into two major schools: the Christian thought and the Greek thought. The characteristics of Christian thought are: (1) dogmatic belief, (2) subjective tendency, (3) spiritual asceticism, (4) divine, absolute obedience, (5) authoritarianism, (6) heavenly kingdom theocentrism, (7) altruism, (8) supernaturalism, (9) moral and religious. The characteristics of Greek thought are exactly the opposite of Christian thought: (1) objective, (2) scientific, skeptical, and experimental, (3) corporeal and instinctual, (4) personal self-awareness, (5) liberalism, (6) self-satisfaction, (7) naturalism, (8) intellectual and artistic, (9) present-day human-centered. Speaking of the origins of the two schools of thought, Greek thought is very ancient, while Christian thought is relatively new. Although European philosophical thought has undergone thousands of changes, it has always been inseparable from the origins of these two schools of thought. Even the latest Fascism and Marxist Communism cannot be separated from the scope of these two schools of thought. Therefore, Western philosophical thought, when analyzed, is generally nothing more than these two schools. Although I am not a person who studies philosophy, I cannot help but study the relationship between Western philosophical thought and their social development, as well as the advantages and disadvantages of these two schools of thought in their history, and draw a conclusion. The progress of Western science was launched after the Renaissance movement in the fourteenth and fifteenth centuries. The driving force behind its revival was Greek thought, because during the European Middle Ages, everyone was obscured by Christianity, superstitiously believing in God and becoming slaves of monks, without the awareness of their own efforts, thus creating a dark state everywhere. This is the famous Dark Age in history. During this era, all sciences, arts, literature, and thought could not develop. Europe at that time was really terrible. At this time, someone came out to correct the bias and remedy the deficiencies, and revived the Greek thought that had been buried for more than a thousand years. The reason why Greek thought was overwhelmed by Christian thought in the past was that it emphasized too much the development of individualism and the satisfaction of the flesh, to the extreme of licentiousness, resulting in the decline of Rome. At that time, Christian thought emerged in response to the times, correcting the then selfish and licentious individualism. However, Christian thought also obliterated the development of personality too much, and also created the darkness of the Middle Ages. Thus, the Renaissance movement revived Greek thought again, emphasizing individuality and making individuals self-aware. From this, it can be seen that Western philosophical thought has its own advantages and disadvantages, and there is no perfect one. After the Renaissance, two flowers were produced: (A) the Industrial Revolution, in which all materials were fully developed, creating their material civilization; (B) the French Revolution, which promoted the improvement of political and social systems in various countries. However, now, European thought has been stimulated by the ills of modern society, triggering an epoch-making mutation. The concrete manifestation of this mutation, belonging to the left wing, is the Soviet Communist Revolution, and belonging to the right wing is Fascism (see my Modern Legal System Overview, published by Commercial Press). Although the natures of these two doctrines are extremely different, they have several spirits in common, such as implementing dictatorship, not tolerating doubt, and not tolerating freedom, which are all more or less the same. This is the great change in modern Western thought. The world now seems to be in turmoil again, but this turmoil is actually just returning to its original path. Therefore, Westerners' thoughts, when exposed as a Western magic lantern show, change back and forth, but in the end, it is the same old trick, nothing rare. There is now a group of people who specialize in speculation. Seeing that this thing has risen, they throw it out; seeing that that thing is cheap, they buy it in. People who go to the stock exchange all want to get rich, but as a result, many people end up throwing themselves into the Huangpu River. At the same time, people who do political work are also just as pitiful. Seeing new things from abroad, they desperately buy them in and vigorously promote them, but as a result, they are never successful. If this continues and we do not establish our own doctrines but blindly follow others, the result may be more than just sending 400 million people to the Huangpu River. This is how dangerous it is. We must plan for the nation for a hundred years or a thousand years. Speculating all the time will not work. Therefore, I do not buy in or sell out, doing that kind of get-rich business. I advocate being impartial and fair, getting the best of both worlds. Since we have already experienced the advantages and disadvantages of Greek thought and Christian thought from historical experience, we should take the strengths and discard the weaknesses, correct the bias and remedy the deficiencies, to adjust it. My self-reliance, on the one hand, takes "obligations and responsibilities" as its foundation, and on the other hand, takes the country and society as its object, so on the one hand, it does not allow personal selfishness and self-interest, and on the other hand, it does not obliterate self-development. In altruism, obedience, belief, and all other aspects, it is similar to Christian thought, and in personal self-awareness, it is consistent with Greek thought, but in freedom and the spirit of self-satisfaction, it is contrary to Greek thought. Therefore, on the philosophical foundation, my self-reliance can be said to be a product of adjusting the two major Western philosophical thoughts by taking the strengths and discarding the weaknesses, correcting the bias and remedying the deficiencies.

Shipping Forecast for Incoming Vessels 165

(October)
