Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven 167

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Not Understanding the Drifting, Peeking at the Door Pities the Young Girl, Wishing to Hear of the Hardships, Cherishing Jade, Visiting the Poor Home

Li Shilian pointed to the tea room attendant at the door of the tea room and said, "You can ask him and you will understand." The attendant smiled and came in and whispered, "We have several business girls here. Does Mr. Zhang want to see them? One of them, who was standing in the courtyard just now, is also from another province, an official stranded in Xi'an." When Zhang Jiefu heard this, a few diagonal lines of laughter appeared on his face, and he asked, "If I call them in to take a look, how much will it cost?" Before the attendant could answer, Li Shilian laughed and said, "We are here to seek a position, and we haven't earned a penny yet, but we are going to spend such frivolous money here. Wouldn't that be too meaningless?" Zhang Jiefu laughed and said, "I'm just curious and want to take a look." Li Shilian laughed and said, "If you say you are curious, I can introduce someone to you to see." So he told him everything he had seen about the refugee girl and what Jia Duocai had reported. The attendant next to him said, "Oh, saying others don't know, but mentioning No. 8 Wangjia Alley, that's at Aunt Hu's house with bound feet. What don't we know? Most of the clothes here are sent to her to wash. That's right, today I saw several women coming to her house, probably the ones Mr. Li is talking about, right? That's easy to see. I'll bring him here tomorrow, without spending any money." When Zhang and Li heard that they didn't have to spend money, they both agreed. Their conversation was overheard by Cheng Zhiqian. He thought to himself, "These people either want to scheme for a small official position or calculate other people's women. It's a bit annoying to listen to it here." So he strolled out the door to see what they were doing. These two were quick-witted and thought that he was someone who had dealings with the director, and there would always be times when they needed to ask him for help. They should not show any improper behavior in front of him. So they both put away their smiles, and Zhang Jiefu struck up a conversation and said, "Ah! These two Germans are really spending a lot of money. They still want to eat Western food in this kind of place." (39)

A Year of Good Scenery 168

— By Zhai Xiufeng

Su Shi's poem says, "A year of good scenery you must remember, especially when oranges are yellow and tangerines are green."

A friend who has traveled all over the Minjiang and Pearl River basins said, "In the deep autumn of the South, it is still hot, but you can sweat less. The lush green leaves are also thinner than in summer, which makes them even more lovely. And the oranges and tangerines, which are specialties of the South, are red and yellow, and pile up on the branches, almost breaking the branches. It is truly a spectacle."

Originally, the scenery of the South is worthy of people's praise, especially the oranges and tangerines of Southern China, which have thin skin and precious taste, with no veins sticking to the skin, and no residue left after eating, which is enough to make people admire. Haimen, which faces the river and the sea, only produces tangerines because of the soil and climate. They taste sour, and fewer people like to eat them, but the orange-yellow color is also extremely beautiful.

One day, I took a leisurely walk in the countryside, and at the corner of a thatched house, I saw a middle-aged woman who was about to wither, scolding her eight- or nine-year-old son, who had a sallow complexion. The child was just crying. It turned out that the middle-aged woman had sold a tree of tangerines to a fruit vendor in exchange for a few days' worth of food. The child, who did not understand the ways of the world, was crying and making a fuss because he wanted to keep them for himself to eat, which angered her, and she beat him fiercely a few times.

The real society is like hell. An innocent child, of course, does not understand the hardships of the real society.

"If you don't have food, you will starve to death. If you don't have tangerines to eat, you won't starve to death! You want to keep the tangerines and don't want to sell them. Do you want to eat or not?..." I walked away and still heard her half-scolding and half-teaching.

"If you don't have tangerines to eat, you won't starve to death!" Ah, a year of good scenery you must remember, is this a snapshot of a year of good scenery?

Drops 169

— (Jian Fen)

Don't look down on drops! Drops are the mother of all things in the universe. Believe it or not! High mountains and continents are based on a little sand and soil, and vast oceans begin with a drop of rainwater; believe it? Drops are the mother of all things in the universe.

Picking Ginkgo Fruits 170

— Rong Yu

In the early autumn evenings, the shouts of vendors selling hot ginkgo fruits disturbed the streets and alleys, attracting children to take out their money to buy them.

In my hometown, Songjiang, there were also vendors selling hot ginkgo fruits. However, the ginkgo fruits they sold were not like those sold by vendors in Shanghai, who bought raw ones from dried goods stores and stir-fried them. Instead, they contracted the tree from the tree owner and picked them themselves. Because in my hometown, there are many ginkgo trees, and every summer, the branches are full of fruits, like grapes. When a strong wind blows, they will also fall like raindrops, hurting people's heads.

Speaking of the ginkgo fruits we eat, what we eat is not actually the fruit flesh, but the kernel. Because when the ginkgo fruit first forms, it is the size of a plum, with a green skin and black spots. Its fruit flesh is not only sour and astringent and inedible, but even if it touches a person's skin, it will peel off a layer of skin. Therefore, when ginkgo fruits are first picked, they must first be soaked in water to rot the fruit flesh, and then the kernels are picked up, dried, and then used.

The villagers believe that ginkgo trees are possessed by spirits, so before picking the fruits, they burn incense, light candles, and offer three animals, kowtowing respectfully several times before daring to climb the tree with a long ladder and then use a long pole to knock down the clusters of fruits.

The way villagers buy ginkgo fruits from tree owners is also commendable. They agree on a price when the fruits are forming, pay a deposit, and pay the full amount when they are ripe and picked. Whether the ginkgo fruits ripen well or poorly, how many are harvested, depends on fate, and neither side regrets it. Moreover, after the villagers pick the fruits, they will definitely send a few pounds to the tree owner, and the host and guest are courteous and harmonious, which is rare in all kinds of transactions!

An Illustrated Water Margin 171

— Hua Binghe

Shi Nai'an's Water Margin, the characters depicted within, some speculate were based on Gong Shengyu's eulogies for thirty-six figures. According to records within the "Guixin Zashi", such as the eulogy for Guan Sheng, which states: "Guan Sheng, with his great blade, could he be a descendant of Yun Chang? Yun Chang was righteous and brave; you are his posterity." Thus, Water Margin, in its writing, resembles Yun Chang's appearance. After Gong's eulogies, there were further illustrated eulogies by Chen Zhanghou and Du Jin of the Ming Dynasty. The Du version had a Qing Dynasty early Guangbai Songzhai edition, totaling one hundred and six figures. The Chen version had a Zuigengtang edition (also known as "An Illustrated Water Margin," a Ming Dynasty edition, rarely circulated), starting from Song Jiang to Xu Ning, totaling forty figures. Both books' eulogies are quite readable. Now, I transcribe two from the Chen version as follows:

"On a peach blossom horse, a pomegranate skirt, a heroine with a silken parasol." – Hu Sanniang

"Carrying a gourd, singing a partridge song, a tavern woman of the Hu." – Gu Dasao

Recently, according to a Tianjin dispatch from the Outer Theories Agency: "A large number of female bandits have been discovered within Yu Tian County. ... It is reported that the bandits' military equipment is extremely sophisticated, all are capable female soldiers who use their beautiful appearances to carry out seduction to accomplish their robberies." Considering the recent rampant banditry in eastern Luan, these female bandits, in particular, greatly resemble the style of Hu Sanniang and Gu Dasao. The so-called "using their beautiful appearances to carry out seduction" probably starts with impersonating something similar to tavern women of the Hu. As for carrying out robbery, that is simply a heroine with a silken parasol. An Illustrated Water Margin. Although it depicts the heroes of Liangshan Marsh vividly, it ultimately stained the history of the Song Dynasty with a political blemish. And now, we especially do not wish to discover a newly illustrated Water Margin under the Kuomintang's rule of the Blue Sky with a White Sun.

— Shiying

The Ephemeral Record of Imperial Fragrance 172

— Original Author Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

That's quite true! The Three Eastern Provinces and the Chinese mainland are indeed one family. Previously, there may have been some separation, but since the Qing Dynasty established its capital, the various characteristics of the people of the Three Eastern Provinces have been almost entirely assimilated by the people of the central plains. Where else is there a difference?

"At the end of the Ming Dynasty," the Empress Dowager's conversational floodgates were opened wide due to this sentiment. "There was a General Wu Sangui stationed here, standing in opposition to us. Unexpectedly, at that time, the interior of China was being disturbed by roving bandits beyond imagination. Not only were the government troops unable to suppress them, but they were repeatedly defeated by them. Finally, even Emperor Chongzhen's throne gradually became untenable. So General Wu sent people to us to borrow troops for aid. We immediately agreed. He even personally opened the gates, welcoming us in. From then on, we drove straight in, obtaining the entire empire. This was a great unexpected harvest! However, from then on, the complete integration of the Chinese mainland and the Three Eastern Provinces may not have been a blessing for both sides."

The Empress Dowager lingered on the small mountain for more than an hour. By the time we were all tired of gazing, Her Old Ladyship was still enthusiastically gazing into the distance. Later, she suddenly issued a very peculiar order, saying that she wanted to go to the seaside to see where the Great Wall enters the sea. I could not figure out why she would specifically want to inspect that insignificant part.

"In the past," she pointed to those dilapidated remains and said in a tone of emotion, "this part of the Great Wall along the coast was built particularly strong compared to other places. The area is also particularly large, as if it was also meant to serve as a long seawall." (149)

Places Visited

Scenery of the Min River 174

— Shazhou

After we stayed overnight in Dongping, which resembled a basin, we arrived at Xijin after breakfast the next day. We had been running in the mountains all day, and I heard that even the character "mountain" was causing headaches. But the guide said that to go to Dongyou, we would have to climb over a Niutou Ridge, so we immediately decided to take the waterway. The waterway was a section of the Dongxi.

The small, pointed-tail grasshopper boat had no rudder or oars. The shallow water flow was just a little deeper than the boat's hull. The riverbed was entirely made of sedimentary rock. The tip of the pole touched the rocks, producing a crisp sound. The speed of the grasshopper boat could also be heard in this sharp sound. When sailing on the shallows, the sound of the water flowed in a continuous rush. The boatmen took off their shoes and went into the water, helping to pull the boat along. The sugarcane-crushing watermills were wailing mournfully, but the mountains and fields were so beautiful. The leaves on the plains were still so lush. The climate of the southern country is like spring in all seasons.

Upon arriving at Shuikou, we still climbed over several mountains, but I had already reached the bank of the Min River.

Before reaching the bank of the Min River, I had imagined the Min River to be vast, but when the Min River was in sight, I felt that reality differed from imagination.

The high mountains on both sides had already defined the course of the Min River. The water trickling from the mountain streams had become so deep and green here. Rushing from upstream to this place, it then rushed away from this place. I don't know why the water flow had to be so hurried, but isn't this a very ready explanation of life? So, I developed a sense of fragility toward the Min River. The Min River is melancholy!

The civilian boats equipped with steamship equipment were full of people from the ×× Command. The boatmen and passengers were arguing over a price, each refusing to yield. After hearing a burst of gunfire, women cautiously emerged with frightened expressions, their bare feet sturdy. The task of fetching water here is done by women. If the saying "the South has many beautiful women" is true, then the beautiful women of the South are beautiful for their health. I wonder what the researchers of human beauty think?

Traveling by boat from Shuikou to Minqing does not take ten hours. The green mountains on both sides are so close and so relaxing. Listening to the sound of the boat oars, the sound of the water flowing under the boat, my heart is at peace, as if I have placed myself in the distant homeland of the water city. But the hateful nightmare-like reality startled me again, shattering my homesickness into fragments.

It seems like a legend, but do the men with bare bodies covered in yellow paper talismans really still exist in the real world? But their ferocious laughter, their evil voices, are all clearly present in my memory! But I do not feel that these believers in evil magic are hateful. Instead, I think they are a bunch of foolish and ignorant people. While China is frantically manufacturing batches of killing weapons in various countries of the world, it still retains this ridiculous magic that prevents bullets from penetrating. But when people use poison gas or death rays to kill you, I wonder if there is any magic that will prevent poisonous gas from penetrating?

Arriving at Minqing, it was just time to light the lamps. Minqing, in the respite of war flames, is silent.

Hebei Won the High School Soccer Championship 177

Beiping Led 2-1 in the First Half

Hebei Won the Championship 5-2 Overall

(Tianjin, 14th) The high school men's soccer final was held at 9:00 AM this morning in the first soccer field within the track and field venue. In the first half, the score was 1-2, with Beiping winning. In the second half, Hebei won 4-0. The overall result was 5-2, with Hebei winning the high school men's soccer championship. The competition between the two sides was extremely fierce. Mao Gonghe, the right forward of Hebei, injured his knee joint. After treatment by the health section, he recovered. The lineups of the two teams are as follows:

▲Hebei Team

Chen Erde, Wang Hongrong, Liu Baoen, Sun Zhitin, Sun Sijing, Liang Mingzong, Li Guangzi, Sun Fulai, Zhao Qichun, Sun Yongquan, Wang Gonghe

▲Beiping Team

Wang Yumin, Jin Adu, Fu Xinqiu, Xu Feimin, Zhang Guowei, Lin Songfa, Wu Guicheng, Zhong Guanming, Wang Jingxi, Lian Xuanxun, Zhang Zhizhen

▲First Half (Tianjin, 14th) In the high school men's soccer final, Beiping took the offensive at the beginning. The five forwards communicated and pressed towards the Hebei position. Center forward Wang Jingxi dribbled the ball quickly and attacked at a point ten yards in front of the Hebei goal, but the attack was unsuccessful. The ball was rescued by Hebei defender Wang Fenrong, passed to Sun Sijing, who then passed to Sun Fulai. It was snatched by Beiping's Jin Adu, intercepted and sent forward. Lian Yixun rushed forward, dribbled the ball quickly, and attacked again at a point fifteen yards in front of the goal. The ball went over the goal, missing it by a small margin. After competing like this for a long time, Wang Jingxi received assistance from center back Zhang Guowei, broke through directly, and passed the defensive line. Hebei goalkeeper Chen Erde could not save it in time, and Wang kicked in one goal. After this, the coordination of the Beiping team improved, and the ball always rose and fell in the Hebei area. Later, Wu Guicheng of the Beiping team was penalized for a corner kick. The landing point was exactly in front of the goal. Chen Erde and the five Beiping forwards rushed forward together, using ten feet to kick. In the chaos, Lian Yixun kicked in one goal. Hebei lost two cities in a row, but did not give up. They counterattacked more forcefully. Soon, Sun Sijing passed a ball to Sun Fulai, who passed the Beiping defensive position and scored with a strong kick at a point seven yards in front of the goal. Holding on until the end, the first half ended with 2-1, with the Beiping team taking the lead.

▲Second Half At the beginning of the second half, Hebei's momentum suddenly increased. The forwards were active and exceptionally fast, and the center back line was also able to cooperate, strictly defending the position. Five minutes after the start, Hebei's Sun Yongquan dribbled the ball along the side to the Beiping area, passed to Po Qichun, who was blocked and passed to Sun Fulai. Sun dribbled the ball to a point five yards in front of the goal and shot diagonally, scoring. After Beiping lost a point, the forwards all retreated to the center line to assist the center backs in defense. Five minutes later, Beiping's Chuan Xinqiu kicked the ball out of bounds and was penalized for a corner kick. Hebei was led by Mao Gonghe. The ball landed in front of the goal, and Zhao Qichun headed it, but it did not go in. Sun Yongquan caught up and won another point with a kick. Hebei had already turned defeat into victory and attacked even more forcefully. Ten minutes later, Sun Fulai got a ball passed from Li Guangxiang and swept it low at a point ten yards in front of the goal, scoring. At this point, Beiping's formation was already chaotic. The three Hebei center backs all went to the Beiping position to operate. In the last three minutes, Sun Fulai took advantage of the emptiness of Beiping's defense, dribbled the ball quickly, and fell twice at a point six yards in front of the goal because he was eager to win. The Beiping defenders still did not catch up. Sun jumped up and kicked, and the ball went into the net again. The second half ended with a score of 4-0. In conclusion, Hebei won the championship with 5-2.

After that, Zhang Boling gave a speech, saying that the conference was held during the Double Ten Festival, and Hebei Province presented three gifts to the country: the first was material construction, namely the conference venue; the second was spiritual construction, namely the spirit of male and female athletes. The first had already been delivered, and before the closing ceremony, he did not dare to hope that the second could be accomplished. Only today, at the closing ceremony, did he feel that this gift had also been delivered. This conference has yielded the best results. He himself has served as the chief referee no less than twenty or thirty times in his life, and there have always been disputes. However, this time there were no problems at all. First, it was due to the dedication of the organizing committee; second, it was due to the earnest service of the staff; and third, it was due to the orderliness of each unit. In the future, he hoped that this spirit would be extended to all matters throughout the country, and then the country's future would be promising. Subsequently, representatives from various parties delivered speeches and presented awards. Because the time was late, only one commemorative flag was awarded to each unit. The prizes will be collected by the leaders of each unit later. Educational News

Minister Zhang Jiong of the Ministry of Education's Department of Social Affairs' Views on Revising Textbooks for People's Schools 197

Zhang Jiong, Director of the Department of Social Education of the Ministry of Education, expressed his views on the revision of textbooks for people's schools on the 13th, saying: In the past, textbooks for people's schools in our country generally focused on literacy, while other common sense, civics, and the Three Principles of the People were all subsidiary. Therefore, textbooks for people's schools were often called "Thousand Character Lessons," such as "The Three Principles of the People Thousand Character Lesson," "Farmers' Thousand Character Lesson," "Citizens' Thousand Character Lesson," and "Commoners' Thousand Character Lesson." Even if the term "Thousand Character Lesson" was not explicitly stated, the content also included one thousand characters, such as "Literacy Textbook," "People's Reader," "Women's Reader," and "People's Literacy Textbook." This is because, in the past, those who were enthusiastic about social education and experts in social education believed that the ignorance of the people was due to illiteracy or limited literacy. If the people could recognize about one thousand commonly used characters, they would be able to read newspapers, read books, write practical texts, and absorb all the new knowledge of the current era. It's like a craftsman who has tools such as axes, chisels, knives, and saws, so he can make tables and chairs, build houses, and make other utensils. However, editing textbooks for people's schools with a focus on the number of characters has the following three difficulties:

(1) Sentences cannot be neat;

(2) Words cannot be short and concise;

(3) Meaning cannot be selective.

Now, I will explain Jiong's views on the revision of textbooks for people's schools below:

(1) Regarding words: This time, when editing textbooks, the number of words does not need to be excessive. Eight or nine hundred words are fine, and six or seven hundred words are also acceptable. Efforts should be made to avoid words with complicated strokes and uncommon words. If one character is taught and can be recognized, and the character can be remembered permanently, then it is much more beneficial than forcibly injecting characters that are quickly forgotten afterward.

(2) Regarding sentences: This time, when editing textbooks, the number of words in each lesson and each sentence does not need to be limited. Three or four words in a sentence are fine, and six or seven words in a sentence are also acceptable. However, from beginning to end, easy-to-understand rhymes or idioms should be used so that readers do not feel difficulty, easily develop interest, and have a deeper impression. Even after a long period of time, they can still remember.

(3) Regarding meaning: This time, when editing textbooks, the number of words does not need to be excessive, but the meaning must be rich. Important knowledge about being a person and being a citizen should be included in the textbooks as much as possible, so that after reading this textbook, the people will not only make progress in personal morality, but also know what kind of country China is, what the relationship between the individual and society is, what the relationship between the individual and the country is, and what the serious situation of national crisis is. In this way, they can fulfill their responsibilities as citizens to the country and be motivated to save the country in the face of national crisis. This seems to be beneficial to both the individual and the country.

(4) Regarding volume: This time, when editing textbooks, the most important principles of being a person and being a citizen should be selected, about eighty in total, and compiled into eighty lessons as basic textbooks for use in primary people's schools. In addition, due to differences in region, occupation, customs, and habits, local educational administrative agencies or social education agencies should compile supplementary and application textbooks to complement the textbooks compiled by the Ministry. (Supplementary textbooks do not need to be edited in rhyme in order to be practical.) In this way, the people can absorb as much important knowledge as possible without any other deficiencies or inconsistencies.

The Importance of Pulmonary Tuberculosis Among Shanghai Students (Part 2) 205

— Li Ting’an

II. From the Students’ Perspective: The second harmful aspect of pulmonary tuberculosis is that patients can transmit it to other students, causing them to suffer in the same way.

III. Economic Aspect: This is the third harmful aspect: the nation spends a lot of money to educate students, only for them to die. This is a significant loss. According to educational statistics, it costs about 30,000 yuan to successfully cultivate a university student. If one dies, there is an economic loss of 30,000 yuan!

Therefore, the problem of pulmonary tuberculosis is very serious. Our statistics are not fabricated, but based on examination results. Regarding the issue of pulmonary tuberculosis among students, you should pay attention to the following:

Remedial Measures

Remedial measures for pulmonary tuberculosis are difficult. To break it down, the first key point is:

I. Improving Living Conditions Such as Clothing, Food, and Housing: Improving living conditions such as clothing, food, and housing is quite difficult to do. This is because it is an economic issue. We do not contract pulmonary tuberculosis because our bodies are healthy and have great resistance. The source of resistance comes from appropriate clothing, food, and housing. Clothing only needs to protect body temperature and does not need to be made of fine silk. So that is not a problem. The most important thing is food. Food is like burning coal. If the coal is poor, the furnace will not be very good. There is no time now to talk to you about what to eat. As for housing, fresh air and ample sunshine are essential. All this requires the country's politics to be on track and the economy to have a solution before it can be resolved. Japan has already done it. Our country cannot talk about this under the current situation, even if there is it will only be a small part!

II. Investigation and Testing: In addition to improving living conditions such as clothing, food, and housing, investigation and "tuberculin" testing should be done. Each school should have doctors test for positive reactions and take X-rays. We hope that there is no disease, but if there is, we should quickly find a way to treat it.

III. Treating Patients: In principle, patients can be divided into four levels: most severe, severe, mild, and least severe. Those with the most severe cases should stop attending school immediately to avoid infecting others and harming themselves. Those with mild cases can study, but for a shorter amount of time. Parents should add nutritious foods and have them sleep in fresh air at night. Now, the Health Bureau and the Education Bureau, and other agencies have jointly organized a summer camp, recruiting children and providing nutritious food and appropriate exercise. Daily life is as follows: get up at 7:00 AM, breakfast at 7:30 AM, study at 8:00 AM, milk at 10:30 AM, lunch at 12:00 PM, two hours of sleep after lunch, then playtime, bath at 5:00 PM, and sleep at 8:00 PM. Each six-week session costs twelve yuan, and the Health Bureau subsidizes ten yuan, totaling twenty-two yuan, all of which is used for children's nutrition. I believe that these children's weight will definitely increase, and those with the mildest form of pulmonary tuberculosis can be cured by doing this.

IV. Popularizing Health Education: The human body is like a machine. To drive a car well, we must know the structure of the various parts of the car and take care to protect it. In other words, to keep students healthy, we must also make students understand the condition of their bodies, so health education is the most important. It should be listed as a required subject in the school curriculum. The countries around the world have not been able to pay attention to this. We know that the school’s not paying attention to health education and not teaching the car mechanics the content and driving methods are the same disadvantages. So, understanding the organs of the body, understanding health care methods, and instilling the importance of epidemic prevention are the fourth remedial measures.

Finally, to sum up: First, pulmonary tuberculosis is very common in our country. Second, regarding the students, if you study the statistics just reported, the numbers must be very high! Third, prevention methods are to improve the living environment, investigate and test, treat patients, and popularize health education. These are my opinions on remedial measures. (The End)

Old Medical Explanations of Five Lin and White Turbidity 206

— Xie Yunshou

(Editor's Note) Dr. Xie Yunshou’s recent book, "The Truth About Gonorrhea," details the dangers of gonorrhea, its symptoms, progression, and treatment methods. The content is rich. It is now on sale. The price is 40 cents. It is sold at Dr. Xie's Clinic at 19 Pinghe Lane, Avenue Edward VII, and at the Author's Bookstore and the Datong Bookstore on the Fourth Road. We are excerpting a section of it here as an introduction.

For thousands of years, the people have been shrouded in the power of old medicine. The old doctors' talk of "deficiency," "strain," and "heat" has truly entered their ears, penetrated their minds, and never been doubted. But from the scientific perspective of today, the truth about various diseases has gradually become clear. Such mysterious disease names really have no place to exist. Now I want to explain the "Five Lin and White Turbidity" as described by old doctors.

Old doctors divide gonorrhea into five types: labor lin, heat lin, qi lin, blood lin, and stone lin. They consider labor lin and qi lin to be due to deficiency, heat lin to be due to heat, blood lin to have both heat and deficiency, and stone lin to be caused by heat or deficiency. Over time, it becomes sand and stone. The symptoms of labor lin are caused by labor injury and deficiency, resulting in inability to urinate, sharp pain in the lower abdomen, and white juice coming out in drops. Qi lin causes the lower abdomen to be full and distended, making it difficult to urinate, often with drops after urination. Heat lin causes urination to be hot and red, short and astringent, with sharp pain below the navel. Blood lin causes blood drops or blood streaks in the urine. Stone lin is also called sand lin, causing the lower abdomen to be sharply distended and the penis to be painful as if cut by a knife, with extreme suffering, and the urine to be like sand and stone.

The above are the old doctors' descriptions of the pathology and symptoms of the Five Lin. From the perspective of our new medicine, the scope of the Five Lin they describe is too broad. Any disease with secretions or solids coming out of the urethra can be called lin. Originally, the word lin means dripping. Dripping is a symptom of a disease, not the name of a disease. The naming of a disease should be distinguished by the anatomical position and the type of pathogen. So what the old doctors thought was a very clear division of the Five Lin, from the perspective of new medicine, is still vague and unclear. Speculating on its symptoms, it actually includes various diseases of the genitourinary system. The names of labor, qi, heat, etc., are incorrect. How many new medical diseases are contained in the old medical disease names of the Five Lin? It is naturally difficult to list them one by one in a precise manner. Now I will bring up the most similar new medical diseases for discussion.

The first type is gonorrhea. The cause of gonorrhea is the infection of a pathogen called gonococcus. Its main symptoms are stinging pain during urination, frequent urination, and white or yellow secretions flowing from the urethra. This is during the acute phase, which resembles what the old doctors call heat lin. If the disease is severe and the symptoms are intense, and the urethral mucosa is broken, blood may even flow out along with it. At that time, old doctors would call it blood lin. But gonorrhea is still gonorrhea. It is just that there are differences in the degree of gonorrhea. People who have gonorrhea, if it becomes chronic, usually have very few secretions, or even don't feel it. When they encounter labor, the secretions increase. At that time, old doctors would call it labor lin. In fact, the disease is still gonorrhea, but it is caused by labor. If you don't have the seeds of gonorrhea in your body, gonorrhea will never occur. So the disease name of labor lin is not valid. If the gonococcus spreads to the bladder, you will feel fullness in the lower abdomen and difficulty urinating, similar to what the old doctors call qi lin. In fact, where does qi come from? It is really a kind of gonococcal cystitis. To be clear, his bladder mucosa does have lesions.

The second type belongs to diseases of the bladder. When the bladder is infected by various bacteria (tubercle bacillus, gonococcus, etc.) or due to trauma, colds, poisoning, or acute infectious diseases, inflammation occurs in the bladder, or when tumors and ulcers occur in the bladder, the symptoms are frequent urination and pain during urination. Tenderness in the bladder area (lower abdomen) and cloudy urine are similar to old medical qi lin. Sometimes it is often mixed with blood, which becomes the old medical blood lin. If it is chronic cystitis, there are not many symptoms when you are quiet. When you are working or your body is unsound, the symptoms will become severe. Wouldn't you be able to call it labor lin at that time?

The third type belongs to diseases of the kidneys. Some kidney diseases also have symptoms such as frequent urination, hematuria, and cloudy urine.

The fourth type is urinary calculus, which is similar to the old medical stone lin or sand lin. The formation of stones is due to the precipitation of components in the urine, such as uric acid, phosphate, oxalate, etc. His size is very uncertain. Some are as small as sand grains, and some are as large as chicken eggs. His place of occurrence is also in the kidney, and also in the ureter, bladder or urethra. His symptoms vary depending on the size, shape, and position of the stones. For example, in the kidneys or ureters, renal colic occurs, which is severe pain in the waist. Sometimes it affects the bladder, testicles, upper legs, back, and shoulder blades. There are also fever, frequent urination, hematuria, etc. If it is in the bladder or urethra, there is a strange urinary retention, which is that sometimes you can urinate at will, and sometimes you cannot urinate. There are also severe pain when urinating and bleeding during urination.

In addition, there is "chyluria." Blood is mixed in the urine. This is a disease caused by the parasite Brugia malayi in the kidneys, as well as various diseases in the urethra. So the name of Five Lin and White Turbidity is really broad. In the genitourinary system, such as the kidneys, ureters, bladder, and urethra, all trauma, bacterial infections, poisoning, etc., can cause frequent urination, painful urination, secretions, and blood in the urine. Therefore, in scientific medicine, doctors should diagnose his position and cause one by one. Then it can be called seeing a doctor. Otherwise, it is caused by labor, called labor lin. Urine is hot and red, called heat lin. The lower abdomen is full, called qi lin. There is blood, called blood lin. Stones are produced, called stone lin. Wouldn't it be too easy to see a doctor?

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases 207

— Cheng Hanzhang

(42) Gastric Dilation

(Q) What is called gastric dilation?

(A) It is a disease in which the contents of the stomach are larger and weaker than a normal stomach.

Page 16

(Q) How do people get this disease?

(A) Any narrowing of the pylorus due to various reasons, such as ulcerative scars, cancer, pressure from tumors outside the stomach, congenital pyloric hypertrophy, pyloric spasm, etc., can cause gastric dilation.

(Q) Are there other reasons?

(A) There are also various stomach diseases, such as chronic gastritis, gastric ulcer, stomach cancer, generalized pain, overeating, etc.

Diseases that weaken the stomach muscles can also cause gastric dilation.

(Q) How is the appetite of people with gastric dilation?

(A) The appetite of the patients is mostly poor, with thirst, heavy fullness after meals, acid reflux, heartburn, belching, and pain in the stomach.

(Q) Do people with gastric dilation often vomit?

(A) Yes. There are often symptoms of vomiting.

(Q) How is the shape of the vomit?

(A) The vomit contains a large amount of old food residue, the acidity is very strong (but gastric dilation caused by stomach cancer lacks hydrochloric acid), and it smells sour and rotten. If placed in a quiet place for a while, it can be divided into three layers.

(Q) What symptoms are revealed on the outside of the abdomen?

(A) If the abdominal wall is thin and loose, the spherical bulge of the stomach can be seen. The lower boundary of the stomach is below the navel. The peristaltic movement of the stomach can also be seen.

(Q) What does it feel like when palpated with your hands?

(A) There is a kind of resistance like touching an air pillow.

(Q) What happens when the stomach is shaken?

(A) There is a splashing sound, which is more obvious when the stomach is empty.

(Q) When the degree of gastric dilation is high, how is the patient's whole body affected?

(A) With a high degree of dilation, the gastric contents can still leave residue overnight, and the patient's nutrition is greatly hindered. As a result, the whole body becomes thin, weak, dizzy, lacks water in the tissues, the tongue is dry, the blood is thick, and the urine output is reduced.

(Q) What should be the treatment plan for gastric dilation?

(A) Attention should be paid to dietary care. For food, you should eat more times each day, and each time the portion should be small rather than large. Night eating is strictly prohibited. Beverages should be restricted, and carbonated drinks should not be drunk.

(Q) Should you rest after eating?

(A) You should rest for an hour after eating. Exercise is fine for mild dilation. (To be continued)

Common Treatment Methods for Fever (3) 208

— Li Xing

(II) Diet

Diet is absolutely indispensable for human life. A person's ability to live must come from nutrients. Diet is like gasoline for a car. If the car runs out of gasoline, it cannot move. If a person does not take in enough nutrients for several days or more, the body will naturally become weaker. A sick person, especially a feverish person, consumes a lot of nutrients and body cells within a day. If there are not enough nutrients to repair, then the worsening of the disease is certainly not unexpected. What is said here about diet is not that anyone knows how to provide the patient with an appropriate diet. We must understand the principles of food chemistry, physiological chemistry, and medical knowledge to know that the diet provided to the patient is good for his disease and his body. A brief description of the basic science of the patient's diet is given below for the reader's research:

In recent years, due to the advancement of chemistry and physiological chemistry, we know what the raw materials of food are, what changes occur when they enter the stomach, and what functions nutrients have after being absorbed into the blood. According to the chemical classification method, everything we eat is divided into the following four types: The first type is protein, the function of which in the body is to grow and repair muscles and organs. A part of it is converted into carbohydrates when the body needs it, to generate heat and energy. Foods that are particularly rich in protein are meats, eggs, soybeans (tofu), walnuts, peanuts, milk, etc. Rice and wheat also contain a small amount of protein. A person weighing 150 pounds needs 70 grams (about two taels) of protein per day. Each gram of protein can be converted into four calories of heat. The second type is carbohydrates (starches and sugars), the function of which in the body is to generate heat and energy (note that generating heat is not "fever." Humans are not cold-blooded animals; their bodies must constantly generate heat.) It was explained in the previous article that the body temperature of a healthy person is 98.6 degrees Fahrenheit. Someone asked, what is the body temperature of a healthy person in the Arctic Ocean? What is the body temperature of a person in the tropics? The answer is both 98.6 degrees. Why? The human body is a wonderful chemical machine that can generate heat and energy itself, and when healthy, it can also control the body to have a certain temperature. A locomotive in a train has coal in its furnace, and water is added to the boiler to generate heat and energy. The coal in the human body is carbohydrates, which come from rice, flour, sugar, vegetables, and fruits. Each gram of carbohydrate can generate four calories of heat. This is the most important category of food. The third type is oils (or fats). The function of oily foods in the body is to generate heat or store energy or protect the body. Meat and vegetable oils, walnuts, peanuts, and rapeseed also contain a lot of oil. Each gram of oil can generate nine calories of heat. The fourth type is water. Water is the medium for various vital elements in the body. If the body lacks carbohydrates due to not eating food, the body will first use the stored glycogen (the sugar stored in the body) to generate heat and energy, just like a person who has no income first uses up his savings. After the glycogen is used up, the body gradually converts fat into carbohydrates and uses it for generating heat and energy. The third step is to convert a part of the muscles and organs (protein) in the body into carbohydrates for the same purpose. In short, if the nutrients in the diet of a feverish patient are insufficient, he must convert his own muscle cells into materials for generating heat and energy. This is the reason why the body loses weight due to improper diet. Conversely, if the patient can get rich and suitable nutrients, the body will certainly not lose weight.

Hygiene Common Sense for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes 209

— Tang Renjin

(19) Explanation of Brain Leakage

When people suffer from nasal congestion, thick purulent secretions flow from the nose, and the sense of smell is reduced, they call it brain leakage. In fact, how can the brain leak? If it is true, then unless the head is injured, so that the skull is broken, the brain can leak out. At this time, the life of the sufferer will also have problems. As for the fact that the brain leaks out from the nasal cavity, I have not seen it, and I have not even heard of it. The reason why it is commonly called brain leakage is probably because the secretions from the nasal cavity flow out from the deep part of the nasal cavity, as if they flow out from the brain. So the words "brain leakage" are used to describe this condition. It cannot be considered a disease name. From the perspective of medical anatomy, the nose and brain are completely separated by bone walls. These bone walls are all the bone walls that make up the paranasal sinuses. Therefore, if the paranasal sinuses become inflamed, the mucous membrane inside these bone walls can immediately swell and turn red. Initially, it secretes mucus. Later, it secretes pus. However, his illness is different. Because the paranasal sinuses (originally called Sinus Paranasalis) can be divided into four cavities. They are (1) the maxillary sinus Sinus Maxillaris (2) the frontal sinus Sinus Frontalis, (3) the ethmoid cells CellulaeEthmoidales, and (4) the sphenoid sinus Sinus Sphenoidalis. The anatomical relationship of these four paranasal sinuses has its own special situation. Therefore, the patient's subjective symptoms and clinical observations are also different. I will briefly talk about it separately now. Perhaps the explanation of brain leakage may be more clear.

(I) Acute Maxillary Sinusitis 210

Sinuitis Maxillaris Acuta

There are many causes of acute maxillary sinusitis. It can be divided into: 1. It is most often secondary to acute nasal catarrh and influenza. 2. It is secondary to scarlet fever, measles, and pneumonia. 3. Surgery in the nasal cavity, foreign bodies in the nasal cavity, injuries to the maxillary bone, syphilis and tumors of the sinus wall, etc., can also cause the occurrence of this disease. 4. Often caries can also cause this disease. That is, among the second premolar, the first molar, the second molar, and the third molar. If there is caries, his alveolar process (the part where the teeth take root) can often develop osteomyelitis or osteitis. Eventually causing sinusitis.

In the early stage of this disease. There are often symptoms such as fever, chills, systemic fatigue, and loss of appetite. As for the pain of suffering from this disease. It is in the maxillary bone area. There is often a feeling of tension. Or complain of pain. The pain often affects the frontal area. And it can increase his strength due to coughing, sneezing, or tilting the head forward. There are also toothache, nasal congestion, excessive nasal discharge, and reduced sense of smell. It is also a common symptom. At this time, the patient's cheek. Most are swollen and red. And there is tenderness. If you use a nasal speculum to examine the nasal cavity. You can see the mucous membranes of the inferior turbinate and middle turbinate. Both are very red and swollen. In the middle nasal passage and the inner surface of the inferior turbinate. There is pus or pus line. Pus is usually mucopurulent. Sometimes mixed with blood. The bacteria contained in this pus. Probably suppurative streptococcus and pneumococcus are the most common. As for suppurative staphylococcus, diphtheria bacillus, influenza bacillus, etc. That is relatively rare.

If this disease is treated properly. It can be completely cured in one or two weeks. Otherwise, it will turn to chronic maxillary sinusitis. That is difficult to treat.

Speaking of the treatment of this disease. Initially, diaphoretic medicine and warm compress method should be used. Or illuminate with a Sarox lamp. Or use an electric light head bath. Both can make the secretions easier to absorb. On the one hand, efforts should be made to make the swelling of the nasal mucosa. Quickly subside. Because the secretions in the sinus. Can therefore be easily discharged. If the pus discharge is obstructed. Then a catheter must be used. Probe into the sinus. Wash out the pus. If it is acute maxillary sinusitis caused by caries. Of course, a dentist should be consulted at the same time. This is the right thing to do. (To be continued)

(Corrections) In the previous issue (3), the word "contraction" in "scar contraction" was mistakenly written as "piece," and the word "result" in (4) was mistakenly written as "give," the word "dry" in "dry" was mistakenly written as "explode," and the word "face" in "eyelid" in the entire issue was mistakenly written as "face."

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (25) 211

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter VIII Clinical Examination Methods

Perhaps some people will say; although the various aspects of clinical examination methods are important; but this is a matter for the doctor himself, and the patient does not need to know so clearly. That's a good point. But we must know that the general medical knowledge of Chinese patients is extremely lacking. When they are sick, although they cannot do without new medicine, what they "prostrate themselves" to is only the amazing treatment results. They are completely ignorant of whether the recognition of the disease is truly accurate. Therefore, many doctors, although their attitude is very humble, and they are definitely not easy to make a diagnosis, but as a result, they are mostly incompatible with the patient; even for the various precise and detailed examination work, they think it is very trivial and annoying, and does not help the patient at all. This kind of misconception exists in the minds of the general patients, almost nine out of ten. They do not know the true meaning of science, which is to question and eliminate arbitrary judgments. New medicine is a product of science, and of course it is no exception. In order to eliminate this misunderstanding, I feel that there should also be a clear understanding in the minds of the general public about the necessary reasons for the various examination work in the clinic.

The importance of clinical examination methods has been described above; the scope he includes is also very broad. According to his nature, it can be divided into the following six types; (1) past medical history, (2) physical examination, (3) sputum examination, (4) blood examination, (5) specialized diagnosis, (6) X-ray diagnosis. For the convenience of readers, I will now describe the general situation of each type one by one below.

Five Years of Sino-French University Pharmacy 212

— Jinru

(1) Origin of Establishment: Pharmacy is one of the most practical and essential specialized sciences of modern times. It is impossible not to study it. Anyone with basic scientific knowledge would not deny this. Unfortunately, Chinese people are bound by thousands of years of outdated thinking, excluding medicine and pharmacy from the traditional occupations of scholars, farmers, artisans, and merchants. Especially for pharmacy, it is seen as insignificant. Although medicine has progressed over the years, with schools established and talents cultivated, and famous doctors emerging, pharmacy has received little attention. There are very few pharmacists. To seek new and advanced pharmacy knowledge, one must study abroad, with no other way to learn. So-called traditional Chinese medicine still adheres to ancient methods of decoction and preparation, without utilizing scientific extraction or imitating new drugs. This allows imported drugs to be sold in large quantities without resistance. Moreover, with the increase of modern medicine, the quantity of imported drugs also increases, resulting in a loss of tens of millions of dollars each year, which is lamentable. Looking at other countries, pharmacists and chemists are competing to collect Chinese medicinal materials and study them tirelessly. For example, ephedrine, which has a diaphoretic effect, was discovered in Ephedra, and eumenol, which has a menstrual regulating effect, was discovered in Chinese angelica. These are significant achievements of their research. Shennong tasted hundreds of herbs thousands of years before the Western calendar, becoming the ancestor of drug research, far earlier than the invention of Western medicine. China is rich in natural and high-quality medicinal materials. If Chinese people can continue the inventions of their predecessors, add further research, and establish factories to produce their own drugs, selling the products overseas, wouldn't it benefit the world, bring blessings to mankind, and shine in the world's international medical and pharmaceutical community? It would also be a way for the country to increase revenue and wealth. Therefore, Dr. Chu Minyi, a medical doctor and pharmacist, and Dr. Song Wusheng, a medical doctor and doctor of science, were willing to sacrifice some of their time and energy to discuss with leading figures in education, Li Shizeng and Cai Yuanpei, as well as the Shanghai New Drug Trade Association, to jointly establish a pharmacy college. The aim was to cultivate Chinese pharmaceutical talents in preparation for establishing factories to produce new drugs, to stop the outflow of funds and benefit the people's livelihood.

(2) Establishment Process: In the spring of 1929, leading figures in education, Li Shizeng, Chu Minyi, and Song Wusheng, planned to establish a pharmacy college in Shanghai. They discussed it with pharmaceutical industry leaders Huang Chujiu, Yuan Hesong, Tu Kaizheng, and Pan Ruitang, who all expressed deep sympathy and promised to provide strong support. Later, they met Cai Yuanpei, who also strongly supported the idea. Li Shizeng then obtained the consent of the board of directors of the Sino-French University in Beiping, which agreed to provide a monthly subsidy of 2,500 yuan as regular expenses. The Shanghai New Drug Trade Association contributed 10,000 yuan, and the Sino-French Education Fund Committee allocated 50,000 yuan, totaling 60,000 yuan as start-up funds. Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Chu Minyi, Song Wusheng, Tu Kaizheng, Yuan Hesong, Zhou Bangjun, Huang Yusheng, and Zhang Xianda were jointly elected to form a board of directors to prepare for the establishment. It was named the Private Sino-French University Pharmacy College. Chu Minyi was appointed as the president, and Song Wusheng as the dean of academic affairs. In the autumn of 1929, a school site was found, and regulations were formulated and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record. The Ministry of Education considered the term "college" for pharmacy to be inconsistent with the university organization law, and ordered it to be renamed the Private Sino-French University Pharmacy Special Training Department. Until the summer of 1932, the Ministry ordered the cancellation of the board of directors, making it completely subordinate to the Private Sino-French University in Beiping. The president was renamed director to comply with university regulations. The board of directors of the Sino-French University then submitted an application to the Ministry of Education for registration and increased the regular expenses to 4,000 yuan per month. In November of the same year, the Ministry sent personnel to inspect the department. They found that the main courses focused on practical application, and both teachers and students worked diligently. However, the equipment of the library and laboratory was limited by economic constraints and could not be fully developed. Based on the report, the Ministry of Education approved the temporary registration, requiring improvements to the library and laboratory equipment within one year. In the spring of 1934, the Ministry of Education sent personnel to inspect again. They had a very good impression and issued an order to formally approve the establishment.

Page 17

Free Talk

After Reading "Dissent on Creation and Time" 213

— Huang Huaibai

On the 19th of last month, Mr. Zhishui published an article on this journal, expressing dissent on my work "Creation and Time." In this dissent, there are many opinions that contradict mine, which I am very grateful for. Originally, the truth of a matter is that the benevolent see benevolence, and the wise see wisdom. There is no need to force agreement. However, the more truth is debated, the clearer it becomes. I feel that in Mr. Zhishui's dissent, there are some places that are close to far-fetched and presumptuous, so I have to say a few more words:

Mr. Zhishui began by mentioning the three Greek tragedians: Aeschylus, Sophocles, and Euripides. He generally said, "The three of them each wrote eighty or ninety or even more than a hundred works. They cannot but be said to be 'prolific,' yet they were not therefore not 'great'." But what we need to know is that the statement that these three tragedians each wrote eighty or ninety works is just a legend. In fact, the extant works of Aeschylus and Sophocles are only seven each, and the extant works of Euripides are only eighteen. Mr. Zhishui himself felt that citing these three Greek tragedians as evidence of "prolificness" was not very reliable, so he said: "But Greece is too ancient after all, and Greek 'history' is somewhat 'mythical' and cannot be considered good evidence." He believed that reliable evidence was to cite people like Scott, Dumas, Balzac, Tolstoy, and Zola to prove that "prolificness" is not harmful to "greatness." However, what we cannot ignore here is that Scott and others were able to win the dual titles of "prolific" and "great" writers, was their writing attitude "too casual"? Did they "botch" their works? Did they obtain their dual titles through "long-term effort and hard work?" Let's look at Scott first. He was burdened with huge debts, so he had to overwork to repay them. His hard work was incessant day and night throughout his life. In the year before his death, he was still working hard on his *Fair Maid of Perth*. Balzac suffered from the same disease as Scott, and was constantly harassed by creditors. He got up in the middle of the night every day and started writing, and during the day he had to go to the printing press to proofread. He was a most hardworking "mental laborer." Zola's Rougon-Macquart series also took more than twenty years of effort to write. Based on these facts, I dare say that the honors that Scott and others have won in the literary world have all been obtained through long-term effort and hard work. When they wrote each work, their attitude was extremely cautious, and they were not "hasty works" written at random. However, for a writer to want to have both "prolificness" and "greatness" is not an easy thing after all. Therefore, there are still people who criticize Scott's works for not having very real inner emotions and thoughts, and Zola also committed the fault of being verbose and cumbersome in his descriptive techniques. These great writers still inevitably have minor flaws due to their "prolificness," and the same can be said of others. So we can say this: to be both "prolific" and "great" is the best, followed by "better to have nothing than something shoddy," and the worst is to be a writer who "strives for quantity without seeking quality."

Mr. Zhishui said: "When we read Goethe's biography, we know that he did not spend 'fifty years' exclusively on 'Faust'." This is natural. Goethe, like us, was a mortal who needed to make a living. Those "fifty years" occupied most of his life, and he, like us, needed to live. When he wrote "Faust," he was still living on the same earth as us, and he could not completely escape the entanglements of human affairs on this earth. At least eating, sleeping, reading, and talking must have taken up part of his time. What I said about him spending fifty years writing Faust can only be said to be "roughly" so. It is not that he absolutely never stopped writing during those fifty years. Mr. Zhishui seems to have taken those "fifty years" a bit too rigidly.

Mr. Zhishui finally said that I "put aside the writer's life experience, etc., and only made judgments based on the rigid relationship between 'creation and time,' which is difficult for contemporary writers to accept." He also said that based on "the examples I cited and the criticisms of contemporary writers, it cannot be said that his views are limited to rigid time relationships." These words are Mr. Zhishui's personal presumptions. In my article "Creation and Time," when did I say that "creation" only needs "sufficient time" and can abandon other conditions? Of course, there are many conditions required for creation. Are they only "life experience," "observation," and "thought," as Mr. Zhishui said? There are also "imagination," "emotion," and "descriptive skills," which can be known by "common sense." However, my point is that "sufficient time" is also one of the important conditions for creation. Because the title of my article is "Creation and Time," I only stated the importance of "time" to "creation." There was naturally no need to mention anything about life experience, etc., which went beyond the topic. Because I did not mention it, Mr. Zhishui said that my views were limited to time relationships and that I put aside all other aspects. Isn't this presumptuous?

"Presumption" can obliterate other people's opinions. In debate or criticism, relying solely on "presumption" is certainly a very convenient method. However, this is too dangerous. Therefore, good critics dare not try this weapon, "presumption," lightly.

Scientific Explanation of Arhats Born from Clamshells 214

— Jiang Hongli

Let us temporarily put aside biology and science, and just understand that Buddhists like to release animals, and we can get the explanation of Arhats born from clamshells from Mr. Chen Zizhan.

For three days, newspapers competed to publish this piece of news: "A turtle floated to the shore of Wusong, as big as a round table, with the Tianqi reign year and the words 'Peng Mou Released' engraved on its carapace."

Arhats born from clamshells are just the same thing. Buddhists are afraid of sin if they eat clams, and they feel it is not worthwhile to release them for nothing. So, they seek fun by casting small lead arhats and gluing them with tin to the inside of the clamshells, and then putting them back into the water. The clams continue to live in the water, and over time, the clamshells grow thicker, and the lead arhats are also coated with a layer of clamshell material. If there are no flaws, at first glance, it would be considered to be naturally formed.

The Aurora University Museum on Rue Luban has two such clamshells, each with more than ten arhats. Mr. Chen has already said that Arhats born from clamshells have been seen in ancient times, and now they are seen again. That's all there is to it, so what's so strange about it? (Unpaid)

In Sickness 215

— Zhide

In sickness, even the smallest things can trigger unprovoked anger.

Yesterday, because I couldn't resist my wife's persistent persuasion, I reluctantly took the dose of laxative (I was already a little unhappy). By evening, I had a strong urge to relieve myself, and it got worse and worse. Although I was very thirsty, I couldn't even get a chance to swallow a sip of water. Fortunately, I managed to get through the first half of the night before it gradually stopped. My heart was already filled with resentment. But when I lay in bed, I was too tired to care about anything.

Today, I woke up at exactly ten thirty. My mind was much clearer. My mouth was terribly dry, and my stomach felt hungry. However, when I saw my wife standing by the bed, staring at me blankly, the resentment that filled my heart last night involuntarily surged up. But when she saw that I was awake, she quickly handed me a cup of tea and asked gently, "Are you feeling better now? Have a sip of water to moisten your throat."

That made it difficult for me to explode. I had to drink the tea and think of ways to make things difficult for her: "Um, is there anything to eat?"

Because I clearly knew that there wasn't a single penny in the house right now. Moreover, she had told me at breakfast yesterday that that meal had used up all the remaining noodles, and the rice jar had been swept clean three days ago.

Sure enough, when she heard my question, she immediately showed hesitation and embarrassment. So I took advantage of the situation and urged her even more urgently: "Hurry up! What are you standing there for? Don't you know you have to eat something after having diarrhea all night?" As I spoke, I fixed my eyes on her, watching how she would solve this problem. At this moment, I had long forgotten the responsibilities and obligations that a husband should fulfill towards his wife.

However, it was too far beyond my expectations. As soon as I stopped speaking, I really didn't expect that she didn't even have the hesitant expression just now. Instead, she smiled even more gently and responded with a "yes" and turned to leave the house. Afterwards, I clearly heard the sound of her opening and closing the front door, which naturally made me suspicious. I predicted that she would either go to get credit for me or borrow money for me - how could she sincerely live with me! So in my heart, the flames of anger grew even more, like a volcano waiting to explode.

When I heard the door ring again, my wife came back with two pink paper bags, smiling happily. I couldn't help but give her a sentence right away: "What did you go to do just now?"

Obviously, she was startled by my loud voice. Only then did she notice the unhappy look on my face. But she completely misunderstood: "Did I make you wait too long? I went out to buy you some snacks." She put the paper bags on my bedside, still smiling, and said, "Eat them. The bag on top is chicken cake, and the one below is nanba crisps. I know you like to eat these, so I got them on credit at Second Uncle's shop."

"On credit again!" I interrupted her even more sharply. Then she became so timid: "Could it be otherwise? There's nothing in the house..."

At this moment, the volcano that had long been waiting to explode in me began to erupt.

"Okay, okay, I can go without eating if there's no money at home! ... Such expensive things, even rich people in our village wouldn't necessarily be willing to eat them as meals when they're sick. What about us? ... In order to eat, you can brazenly do it. Of course, you don't feel anything, but that's digging a hole for me, embarrassing me! ... Does it mean that a person can eat whatever they like? I like to eat so many things, I'm just afraid I can't afford it ... The root cause is to blame Second Uncle - blame him for opening a snack shop here! ..."

"Actually, I don't understand, I haven't treated you even half as well as I should ... You're deliberately arguing with me, you don't want me to get well! ..."

Whenever I throw such a tantrum, it is very difficult to restrain myself for a while. At the same time, every time my wife is subjected to such harsh scolding, she doesn't say a word, she just sits beside me and sobs sadly. This time was no exception: my wife just sobbed without saying anything. And I, who was extremely agitated in my sickness, found it even more difficult to stop the fire of anger once it had erupted.

This went on until it was almost time to light the lamps, when the aggravated pain violently attacked me. After a series of unconscious faints, I finally managed to extinguish the unprovoked fire of anger. My wife, with red and swollen eyes, busily took care of me again in a panic.

On the Indian Ocean 216

— Hei Ying

Hoping for a pleasant sea voyage, it wasn't until this return journey home that the Conte Rosso liner sped across the smooth-as-mirror Indian Ocean. It had the speed to reach Shanghai directly in a week - I mean, from Singapore.

In my memory, it seemed like the Mid-Autumn Festival: if not, why was the moon so bright?

There are few storms at sea in autumn. It had been two days at sea since leaving Singapore: the sea water was getting darker and darker. Standing on the deck and looking at the vast expanse, you could imagine the depth of the water. I loved to sneak to the bow of the ship early in the morning, before people woke up, to watch the sunrise. A blood-red sun burst out of the seabed and rolled into the sky, wouldn't you guess that wasn't a flavorful miracle? I also loved to sit alone on the deck on lonely nights, listening to the clattering of the machinery and watching the silver moon. At that time, I was younger and knew less about the world than I do now. Maybe that was why the Italian sailors liked me so much, and they often came to chat with me when they were free. The one who looked like a fat pig spoke some English, so we spent the most time together. He always praised Mussolini in front of me, saying that this fascist leader was the greatest man in the world.

- Have you read Mussolini's autobiography?

Once, he suddenly asked me about such a book.

- No.

I shook my head.

- In Italy, every young person has read this book. You know, Mussolini is the greatest man in the world!

But I wasn't very excited. Think about it; would a overseas Chinese student who grew up in a colony have a good political consciousness? Those rulers were really clever, they had ways to make you understand nothing. After being a good student in a church school for several years, reading many books about my Lord Jesus, I finally walked away like a miracle of the sun rising from the bottom of the sea. - Now, I am on the Indian Ocean.

People with future aspirations are always happy: moreover, there are no dangerous winds and waves at sea in autumn to make you afraid?

And it was the time when "the moon is especially bright on Mid-Autumn Festival"! That night I sat alone at the bow of the ship with my Ukalele. The waves crashed against the hull, making a harsh sound. Besides that, everything was quiet. There were always foolish people in the world; weren't those sleeping in the stuffy cabins wasting the good night?

Strangely, I couldn't pluck the strings and sing anything. Could it be that I had forgotten all the tunes that I loved to sing under the coconut trees? The moon poured down on the sea, reflecting silver light. The wind had the feeling of autumn, and I felt a little cold wearing only a thin shirt. Knowing that I was getting closer and closer to my ancient homeland, I didn't know why I was so excited that I just wanted to shout out loud - what should I shout? Young people always find it so easy to throw reason into the sea.

How can I forget the sea voyage on the Indian Ocean? Here, I saw the sunrise in the east. I suddenly became brave in front of this magnificent scene! I talked and laughed with the admirer of Mussolini, and ate Italian bread together. Even more so, under the Mid-Autumn moon, I carefully recalled the unforgettable stories of the coconut grove, and also considered the unknowable future. ...
