Economic Supplement

Problems with Consignment Trade in Foreign Markets 218

— Kong Dian

(1)

In recent years, China's foreign trade has been impacted by the dumping of foreign goods, leading to a growing trade deficit. From January to August this year alone, in just eight months, imports exceeded exports by a staggering 360 million yuan. If our countrymen do not change their deeply ingrained mentality of subservience and reject unnecessary foreign goods, the total collapse of the national economy may be imminent, and soon it will be staring us in the face. However, in terms of international trade, from a passive perspective, it is the sacred duty of the people to plug loopholes and prevent trade deficits; from an active perspective, it is still essential to develop export businesses and explore overseas markets. Recently, the call to revitalize foreign trade has been widespread, becoming a national consensus. However, today, not only are ordinary merchants largely ignorant of foreign market conditions, but also export trade support institutions such as shipping companies, banks, and marine insurance companies are often lacking and unprepared, making direct trade difficult to achieve. Therefore, this article briefly describes the theory and practice of consignment trade, hoping to provide reference material for those discussing and engaging in the export business.

Consignment trade, also known as consignment sales, is a method in which the owner of goods consigns them to a merchant in another location, on the condition of paying a certain commission, entrusting the merchant to sell them on their behalf. In this arrangement, the person entrusting others to sell goods is called the consignor (Consignor or Shipper), and the person entrusted to sell goods is called the consignee (Consignee). This type of transaction is not only common in foreign trade but also quite prevalent in the domestic market. The reasons for its popularity in international trade are twofold:

(1) To promote various goods in foreign markets, direct transactions with local buyers, without going through any intermediary merchants, should be the principle. However, opening branch offices is not only very costly, but it is also difficult to fully understand the commercial customs and supply and demand conditions of that market in a short period of time. Therefore, it is better to seek out local merchants and enter into a consignment agreement with them, and then change the strategy when the time is right and it is definitely sufficient to deal directly with local buyers.

(2) The distribution locations of special commodities around the world are often fixed. For example, London for wheat and New York for raw silk. Those engaged in these businesses in various countries mostly gather here to gather commercial information. Commission Merchants specializing in acting as agents for others in buying and selling are particularly numerous. Opening branch offices and directly engaging in sales may not be sufficient to compete with others, so it is better to entrust commission merchants to sell on one's behalf, putting oneself in an advantageous position.

For this reason, during the transitional period of international trade, a country engaging in export business, if it feels that it lacks the experience of selling goods in foreign markets, mostly uses the consignment method as a principle. Before the European War, most of the United States' exported goods were consigned to British and German trading companies for sale, which is a notable example.

(2)

Consigned goods can be divided into two types according to the different terms of consignment: First, regarding the sale of goods, if the consignor does not specify a definite price and allows the consignee to handle the matter with full authority according to market conditions, this is called Unlimited Consignment (Without Limit). Conversely, if the consignor places various restrictions on the timing, method, and selling price, etc., this is called Limited Consignment (With Limit). There is much discussion about the advantages and disadvantages of the two in ordinary commerce. However, in foreign trade, the two parties are separated by vast oceans, making it difficult to oversee and balance everything. Moreover, market conditions change rapidly, and opportunities are fleeting. If the consignee's commission agent is truly reliable and trustworthy, they will be able to make independent decisions and take immediate action using the most efficient and effective methods. Therefore, unlimited consignment is often adopted. However, it must be noted that if this method is adopted and the consignee is eager to recover the amount of the documentary bill, they may dispose of the goods at will regardless of market conditions, resulting in a selling price that is far beyond the consignor's expectations and incurring losses. This often happens, so it is still appropriate to maintain certain conditions when entering into a contract.

In consignment trade, a Commission Merchant, although selling goods in its own name, does not bear the profits or losses resulting from the sales. Therefore, its relationship with the consignor is legally a type of mandate, and the extent of its authority comes purely from this mandate. Usually, a contract is signed, stipulating on the one hand that the consignee should seek the greatest benefit for the consignor within the possible scope, and after the goods are sold, notify the consignor by letter or telegram, and prepare a statement along with the payment; (however, usually the consignor makes a documentary bill with the bank to obtain the price of the goods when sending the goods,) and on the other hand stipulating that the consignee may first deduct advances and commissions from the price of the goods. Advances are payments made on behalf of the consignor, and commissions are the remuneration that the consignee should receive. If they are not paid, the consignee has the right to retain the goods.

(3)

Choosing a Commission Merchant is no different from choosing other firms, and the only goal is to ensure reliability. The most effective method is for the exporter to conduct on-site inspections or send a delegate to investigate. However, the following methods are commonly used:

(1) Magazines and Newspapers: In recent years, advertisements in newspapers and magazines have increased with their circulation. For example, Shen Bao and Xinwen Bao often have records of foreign merchants overseas needing Chinese goods. Magazines such as the Industrial and Commercial Bi-monthly published by the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, because it is responsible for guiding the development of overseas markets, thoroughly investigates and records the store names, commodity names, business locations, etc., of foreign merchants who want to trade with Chinese merchants and purchase Chinese specialties. Other commercial monthly reports issued by chambers of commerce in Shanghai, Hong Kong, Hankou, etc., also often contain such advertisements.

(2) Directories of Businessmen and Industrialists: Also commonly known as telephone directories. The most famous and longest-running directory of businessmen and industrialists in the world is Kelly's Directory of Merchants, Manufacturers and Shippers of the World, published annually in the United Kingdom. It comprehensively lists prominent merchants, import and export businesses, factories, banks, insurance companies, and shipping companies from all over the world, and includes indexes by business type and location for easy reference. Other directories such as Dean's Export Merchant Shippers published in the United Kingdom, Adresboek Van Nederland published in the Netherlands, Annuaris d'Italia' published in Italy, Severiges Idandelrs Kalander published in Sweden, Norges Handels Kalender published in Norway, International Trade Developer published in Japan, Annuaire du Commerce published in Switzerland, Annuaire de Commerce published in Belgium, and Annuaris Commercial published in Portugal are also quite detailed, and many of them contain advertisements. Subscribing to them will surely lead to finding a suitable consignee.

(3) Assistance from Chambers of Commerce: Chambers of commerce, such as general chambers of commerce in various places, are responsible for promoting overseas trade and have some connections with chambers of commerce in various countries. If they are entrusted to seek out goods for which one is exporting, with trading terms and other trade reports, they will certainly be able to provide some assistance.

(4) Entrusting Consulates: Consular officials are responsible for developing commerce. Although many of the consuls stationed overseas in China are mediocre in knowledge and do not know what their duties are, they are also quite enthusiastic in supporting merchants and civilians. Requesting them to investigate the market conditions in the place of residence or reputable firms is not difficult to achieve a reasonable effect.

(5) Entrusting Corresponding Banks: Although only the Bank of China currently has branches overseas among Chinese banks, each bank that operates foreign exchange business has corresponding agencies in major commercial ports around the world. If one entrusts them to introduce them, they will be able to inform them of the credit status and business outlines of traders in that location, and after another contact, the two parties can freely communicate and proceed with transactions.

(4)

From the perspective of practical situations, the forms of consignment of goods to foreign markets for sale in export trade can generally be divided into the following four types:

(1) Manufacturers ship their products directly to the central markets of foreign countries and entrust them to importers there for sale.

(2) Domestic exporters, entrusted by manufacturers, transport their goods to the central markets of foreign countries and entrust them to importers in those markets for sale at the manufacturers' own risk and calculation.

(3) Exporters, in order to expand sales channels, use reputable commission agents in foreign markets and entrust them to sell on their behalf.

(4) Exporters, in order to develop new markets, tentatively entrust importers in those places to sell with the intention of trial sales.

Among these four, the first type, where manufacturers directly entrust foreign merchants to sell, is very common in various countries. However, foreign trade requires special knowledge and skills in terms of export procedures, recovering payment, and communication. It is inevitable that there will be many obstacles if manufacturers take on sales themselves. The second type, where manufacturers entrust exporters who then entrust others to sell, inevitably increases costs because it requires paying double commissions, which is also unfavorable. The third type, using powerful merchants in the export destination to share a portion of the market and occupy a certain position, is most suitable for goods that are abundant in production and have international sales channels. The fourth type is most suitable for developing new markets. China's autonomous foreign trade is just beginning, and in terms of consignment sales, it is most appropriate to adopt this method. The question that arises is: Which market should one start with?

Regarding market research, in various countries, consuls stationed overseas are required to submit detailed reports monthly, which are published by the competent authorities to inform merchants. In China, the consuls are mostly limited in knowledge, and the government does not urge them, so it is impossible to know the details of overseas market conditions. However, the number of Chinese nationals residing overseas, just in Southeast Asia alone, has reached six or seven million. In addition to a portion of these expatriates engaging in manual labor, most of them open shops in their locations and directly engage in transactions with the locals. In the past, Japanese goods accounted for the majority of goods sold. Since the violent occupation of the Northeast by the Japanese, they have been motivated by righteous indignation and have severed relations with the Japanese. Therefore, their need for domestic goods is very strong. Moreover, these markets are only separated from us by a narrow strip of water, and their customs and habits are similar to those of the mainland. To develop overseas trade, Southeast Asia is the most suitable market for us.

Once the market has been selected, the following items can be studied in detail:

A. Regarding the supply side:

A. The producer and manufacturer of the goods, B. The status of production and supply, C. Competing products and competitors, D. Are there substitutes and what are their advantages and disadvantages?

B. Regarding the demand side:

A. Area of demand, B. Uses, C. Season of demand, D. Amount of demand during a certain period.

C. Regarding transactions:

Such as commissions, delivery methods, payment collection methods, units of sale of goods, packaging, and local weights and measures, etc.

If each of these is studied in detail, all problems can be solved easily.

(5)

The direct parties involved in consignment trade are the consignor and the consignee. Once the consignor has obtained the consignee's consent to sell the goods on their behalf, a contract should be signed, and the following matters should be noted:

(1) Agreement on Commissions: Commissions are the consignee's only income in consignment trade. Even if the consignor suffers losses as a result of the sales, they must be responsible for payment. Therefore, it is essential to clearly specify the fee rates in the contract in advance. Although the percentages may not be consistent due to different commercial customs in different places, they are usually determined based on the actual sales figures of the goods. There are also those who calculate it based on the prices listed in the shipping documents. For foods and fruits, etc., after being transported for a long time, some are inevitably spoiled. After inspection by the commodity inspection office, only those that are intact are allowed to be sold. Therefore, according to the customs in Liverpool, England, the commission that the consignee should receive is not based on the actual sales figures of the goods; even the goods that are rejected as a result of inspection are also treated as sold and must pay commissions to the consignee. Therefore, when encountering such special customs, the calculation of commissions should be clearly stipulated at the time of contracting to avoid future disputes.

(2) Guarantee of Payment: For consigned goods that the consignee extends credit to customers, there is a risk of delays or defaults in payment. Therefore, for safety's sake, the consignor should enter into a Delcredere Contract with the consignee, so that there will be a certain guarantee in case of danger in the future. However, after concluding this type of contract, the consignee's responsibility is inevitably increased. Therefore, the consignor usually gives a certain Delcredere Commission as special remuneration, and the percentage is always determined according to market customs.

(3) Conclusion of Documentary Bill Contract and Payment of the Balance: The goods consigned to the consignee are essentially a type of consignment sale, not a purchase by the consignee themselves. Therefore, in principle, payment should only be made after the goods are sold. However, in order to facilitate the consignor's financial circulation and maintain the entrusted relationship for a long time, the consignee usually allows the consignor to issue bills of exchange using the shipped goods as collateral, with themselves as the payer, which is the so-called documentary draft. As for the amount that can be used for documentary bills, if it is only decided by the consignor unilaterally, it will inevitably be too large. Generally, the two parties decide based on 60-70% of the price listed in the shipping document. The remaining amount should be returned by the consignee to the consignor, and the timing and method of payment can be determined separately.

(4) Agreement on Interest: For consigned goods, on the one hand, before they are sold, the consignee must pay the documentary bill amount and also pay import taxes, tonnage taxes, storage fees, inspection fees, and other miscellaneous expenses on behalf of the consignor. On the other hand, after the goods are sold, the consignee can freely use the proceeds within a certain period of time. Therefore, a creditor-debtor relationship arises between them at the same time. To avoid future disputes, both parties should agree on the interest rate for incoming and outgoing amounts in the contract to be appropriate.

The above is just a brief overview of the matters that consignors and exporters should pay attention to in consignment trade, focusing on the major aspects. In fact, the way to promote a country's international trade lies in those engaged in the export business personally standing on the front lines, going to overseas markets in person, and directly contacting foreign consumers, and then they will be able to awaken their potential desires and eliminate those who compete with us. Only then can the general trend of trade have the hope of being developed and promoted. Looking at the situation after the European War, American manufacturers have changed their previous mentality of entrusting German merchants to sell and have established their own overseas branch offices. The British even said that the reason why Japanese goods are rampant and swept the world is that their merchants enter other countries' markets directly without relying on local merchants. Therefore, consignment sales can only be regarded as a temporary measure in the process of developing overseas markets and cannot be regarded as a regular practice.

A Review of Our Country's Cooperative Law 219

— Chen Honggen

The cooperative society is a new type of enterprise in our country, originating in the eighth year of the Republic of China. It has only been around for a little over a decade. Initially, it was not popular because the general public did not understand the meaning and importance of cooperation. Although the authorities had the will to promote cooperative enterprises, they were unable to do so due to the country's many troubles. Therefore, they could only let this newborn infant seek its own maintenance, and the cooperative enterprise has survived in this situation for more than a decade. This can be regarded as a common phenomenon in the early stage of the cooperative movement in various countries around the world. However, in the process of gradual evolution, it is inevitable that some legal problems will arise. Therefore, the need for cooperative laws and regulations is becoming more and more urgent. Therefore, by the middle of the nineteenth century, major European countries had successively formulated cooperative laws and regulations. Some are attached to the general commercial law without indicating the words "cooperative society", such as the French Cooperative Law; some are attached to the commercial law but specifically indicate the name of the cooperative society, and a special chapter is devoted to discussing it, such as the cooperative laws of Switzerland, Belgium, Italy, Sweden, and other countries; another type is to order separate laws and regulations for cooperative societies outside the general commercial law, such as the British Cooperative Law; among them, the third type is the most suitable, and most countries have adopted this system when formulating cooperative laws in recent years.

The existence of cooperative laws in our country can be traced back to Mr. Dai Jitao's Draft Industrial Cooperative Law in the ninth year of the Republic of China. Later, the provincial and municipal governments realized the increasing importance of cooperative enterprises, and successively formulated cooperative laws and regulations, no less than a dozen in total. They are listed below:

Law Name Implementation Area Implementation Period

Draft Industrial Cooperative Law Nationwide Not implemented

Jiangsu Province Provisional Regulations on Cooperative Societies Jiangsu July of the 17th year

Shanghai Municipal Provisional Regulations on Consumer Cooperative Societies Shanghai October of the 17th year

Shandong Provisional Articles of Association for Cooperative Societies Shandong November of the 18th year

Zhejiang Province Regulations on Cooperative Societies Zhejiang December of the 18th year

Nanjing Municipal Provisional Articles of Association for Cooperative Societies Nanjing Same as above

Articles of Association for Forestry Cooperative Societies Guangdong Same as above

Jiangxi Province Provisional Regulations on Cooperative Societies Jiangxi February of the 19th year

Hebei Province Provisional Regulations on Cooperative Societies Hebei April of the 19th year

Hankou Municipal Provisional Articles of Association for Cooperative Societies Hankou July of the 19th year

Hunan Province Provisional Regulations on Cooperative Societies Hunan March of the 21st year

Regulations on Rural Cooperative Societies in Bandit Suppression Areas Rural October of the 21st year

The above-mentioned cooperative laws and regulations are all local. Their content either imitates Japan or simulates each other, and most of them are incomplete. At a time when cooperative enterprises are booming, a unified set of laws and regulations is needed to enable cooperative enterprises to enter a proper and unified path. However, our country's cooperative laws and regulations are so scattered and fragmented, each going its own way. Difficulties are felt in all aspects of guidance and control, and obstacles have arisen in the future of cooperative enterprises. The government also recognized the importance of this matter, and in May of the 20th year, the Ministry of Industry formulated the Provisional Regulations on Rural Cooperative Societies, hoping that they could be implemented throughout the country. However, the result was that very few provinces and localities followed them. Moreover, since these regulations were promulgated by ministerial order, they were not reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan and formally promulgated by the National Government. There were some omissions in the legislative procedure, and it is also doubtful whether they have sufficient effectiveness for promotion. Therefore, the Central Political Council decided on ten major principles of the Cooperative Law in September of the 21st year of the Republic of China. Based on these principles, the Legislative Yuan drafted a Draft Cooperative Law, consisting of nine chapters and eighty-seven articles. In November of the same year, the Economic Committee of the Legislative Yuan reviewed and revised it, reducing it to nine chapters and seventy-six articles. It was passed by the Central Political Council, and formally promulgated by the National Government on March 1st of the 23rd year, named the Cooperative Law. The various points in its content have been repeatedly scrutinized by experts, and it should be much more complete than the laws implemented by various provinces and cities in the past. Moreover, there are several points of superiority that are not available in the cooperative laws of other countries. However, since our country's experience in cooperative enterprises is still shallow, lawmakers may rely on precedents or make presumptions, and there may be one or two points that can be criticized. Now, based on my humble opinion, I will select the important points for analysis and discussion. It is inevitable that there may be some biased views. Readers are requested to point them out.

(1) Stipulations on the Nature of Cooperative Societies 丨丨 It goes without saying that cooperative societies are different from ordinary companies. The Cooperative Law should first state the nature of cooperation to prevent other for-profit organizations from misappropriating the name of cooperative societies and obtaining various legal protections and privileges (such as tax exemptions). According to the laws and regulations of various countries, this point is often not clearly expressed, resulting in the existence of many fake cooperative societies. For example, the Swiss Cooperative Law states that a cooperative society is an organization formed by a group of individuals with a common economic purpose, which seems too broad. Article 1 of our country's Cooperative Law states: "The cooperative society referred to in this law refers to a group that is based on the principle of equality, on the basis of mutual aid, uses common management methods to seek the economic interests and improve the lives of its members, and whose number of members and amount of capital can be changed." This provision can help the general public understand the nature of cooperative societies and can distinguish between for-profit organizations that falsely claim to be cooperative societies. Therefore, I believe that this point is a major feature of our country's Cooperative Law.

(2) Statement of the Business and Responsibilities of Cooperative Societies 丨丨 According to Article 5 of Chapter 1 of the Cooperative Law, "The business and responsibilities of the cooperative society shall be stated in its name." For example, "Moling Town Shuangling Township Agricultural Production Utilization and Marketing Limited Liability Cooperative Society" has a total of twenty-one characters. Some people think that the name is too long and inconvenient to read, and it is even more difficult for farmers to understand its meaning. Mr. Dong Shijin said that the best way to name a cooperative society is to determine it according to the actual duties, such as "irrigation cooperation" and "cultivated land consolidation cooperation," without using formal words such as "production" and "marketing." I think that the main function of the name is to deal with the outside world. On the one hand, it is for registration procedures, and at the same time, it gives the outside world a concept of the business of the cooperative society. Moreover, in the immature state of cooperative enterprises in China, it is not appropriate if the names cannot be unified. In order to take into account the convenience of legislation and facts, the name can be reduced as much as possible without impairing its concept. For example, the last two characters of "limited liability" can be removed. If several businesses are operated concurrently, the first character of each business can be taken to form the name. In this way, the aforementioned name can be changed to "Moling Town Shuangling Township Agricultural Production Utilization Limited Cooperative Society." Sometimes the three characters "Moling Town" can also be omitted, leaving only twelve characters.

(3) Concurrent Operation of Businesses 丨 For countries where cooperative enterprises are just starting, those who engage in them are prone to failure because they are not familiar with the details. The center of cooperative enterprise promotion in our country is farmers and lower-middle-class society. Their knowledge is already insufficient, and their cooperative skills are even more lacking. It is difficult to operate several businesses concurrently. Otherwise, it will only be a matter of making false claims, which will not help the actual situation or even cause losses. Article 3 of the Cooperative Law stipulates that "The business of the cooperative society may be one or several of the items listed in this article," which indicates that concurrent operation is possible. However, we need to recognize the factual difficulties. At least in the next few years, the business of a cooperative society should not be too complicated. If several businesses are related and cannot be separated, we can also examine their performance and actual situation before operating other businesses concurrently, so that there is no risk of failure. In short, the government authorities should take a guiding position in cooperative enterprises, which is by no means comparable to the laissez-faire situation in Europe and the United States.

(4) Regarding Registration Procedures 丨 According to Article 8 of Chapter 2 of the law, the cooperative society shall, within one month after convening the founding meeting, passing the articles of association, electing directors and supervisors, and organizing the board of directors, register with the competent authority at its location. The articles of association referred to here do not stipulate a certain format and content for reference, and the competent authority at the location is not clearly defined as an administrative agency (such as in Japan) or a judicial agency (Germany). According to Article 9, "After receiving the application mentioned in the previous article, the competent authority shall issue an approval or disapproval within fifteen days." If this can be implemented, it is also optimistic. However, in fact, government offices are extremely slow to handle matters. Moreover, administrative officials in remote provinces do not understand the importance of cooperation. It is feared that this registration procedure will be difficult to complete so quickly. For example, there are several cooperative societies in Hebei that have been trained for many years and have the assistance of the China International Famine Relief Commission, but they have not yet completed the registration procedures. In other countries, if the government office makes it difficult to register, the cooperative society can still have the right to appeal to the High Court (such as in the United Kingdom), but there is no provision for this point in our country's Cooperative Law, which inevitably hinders the future of cooperative enterprises.

(5) Member Liability 丨 Article 11 of the Cooperative Law states: "...Members of unlimited liability cooperative societies shall not be members of other unlimited liability cooperative societies." From the wording, this article is very complete and can prevent cross-membership and protect cooperative societies from losses. However, the actual situation may not be the case. The reason is that Chinese farm families are different from the small family system in Europe and the United States. Fathers, sons, and brothers live together in one place, and most of their properties have not been separated. Now, if two brothers are both of legal age and join Cooperative Society A and Cooperative Society B as unlimited liability members, what should be done if one of the societies suffers a loss and the entire property is taken out for compensation, and then the other society suffers a loss again? This is a major problem. Moreover, in recent years, credit cooperation has been the most developed, and members often falsely use the names of others to join multiple societies in order to obtain loans. This phenomenon poses a great difficulty in legislation and must be prevented.

(6) Member Subscription Shares and Amount per Share 丨 According to Article 15, "Each member shall subscribe to at least one share, and no more than 20% of the total shares... The amount per share shall be at least one yuan in national currency and no more than twenty yuan." The restriction on the amount of shares subscribed is to prevent the monopoly of a few members. As for the amount per share, some countries have set a maximum amount (such as Japan, which stipulates that the amount per share shall not exceed 50 yen), and our country also restricts its minimum amount. I think there are at least two shortcomings: (1) Lack of flexibility 丨 If there is no minimum amount, it can be freely adjusted below the maximum amount. The share capital can be low when there are many members and high when there are few members. (2) The economic conditions of general workers and farmers are low, and the amount of two yuan may be slightly high.

(7) Dividends 丨 The law stipulates that the interest on cooperative shares "shall not exceed 1% per annum." It is not appropriate to give interest on cooperative shares. As Mr. Dai said in the principle of industrial cooperative societies, "Distributing profits based on the amount of investment is not in the spirit of cooperation." The dividend on ordinary company shares is only 1% per annum at most, and the dividend on cooperative shares is also stipulated to be so high, which truly loses the meaning of cooperation.

(8) Member Withdrawal 丨 The cooperative laws of various countries mostly recognize the right of cooperative society members to request withdrawal. Article 24 of the Cooperative Law promulgated this time states: "Members may withdraw from the society at the end of the year, but shall submit a written request three months in advance." This restricts the opportunity to withdraw to the end of the year. It will be inconvenient for withdrawing members who have moved to a distant place to change jobs. My intention is to divide one year into two periods, that is, there is an opportunity to withdraw every six months. In this way, the society's handling of affairs will not be inconvenienced much, and it will indeed benefit the withdrawing members greatly.

(9) Cooperative Society Inspection Matters 丨 Regarding the inspection of cooperative societies, the laws of various countries have clear provisions. For example, the United Kingdom and India are subject to the inspection of judicial agencies, Germany and Austria are subject to the inspection of the "Inspection Union" of the cooperative society's autonomous organs, and Japan is subject to the supervision of administrative agencies. In our country, which is in the stage of nurturing cooperative enterprises, we should also imitate this system so that they can develop in an orderly manner. However, the Cooperative Law only stipulates that internal supervisors, members, and creditors can review the financial and business situation, and does not stipulate what kind of agency outside the society can supervise it.

(10) Liability of Directors 丨 Article 35 stipulates: "When a cooperative society operating the business in Article 3, Paragraph 4 is unable to repay its savings debts, the directors shall be jointly and severally liable for repayment." The so-called business in Article 3, Paragraph 4 refers to credit cooperation, which is the most prone to losses. The law stipulates that the directors shall be jointly and severally liable for repayment. The directors are elected from the members by the members' meeting and are no different from other members. They only need to be citizens of the Republic of China, be over 20 years old, and have a legitimate occupation to be elected (see Article 10 of the Cooperative Law). Under these simple conditions, it is indeed questionable whether they should bear such a heavy responsibility. Whether the directors should also have other conditions (such as a minimum amount of assets) is a question for discussion today. Otherwise, this provision is equivalent to being in vain. 丨

Metals: Tinplate Sales Smooth for Local and Out-of-Town Buyers 226

The recent tinplate market has been exceptionally good. Local factories and buyers from Tianjin, Qingdao, Pinghan, and other regions have shown strong demand, leading to substantial transactions. Records show that in the past two to three days, over 1,600-1,700 dan (units of weight) have been traded. Due to the sharp rise in foreign exchange rates, prices are not expected to increase. Current market opening prices for 90-pound American tinplate with a single coat are 15.75 yuan, and 100-pound tinplate is 16.50 yuan. 90-pound tinplate with a double coat is 32 yuan, and 100-pound tinplate is 33.50 yuan. German and Italian tinplate with a 90-pound single coat is 15.25 yuan, and 100-pound tinplate is 15.75 yuan. 90-pound tinplate with a double coat is 33.50 yuan, and 100-pound tinplate is 31.50 yuan. British and French tinplate are out of stock, so there are no market reports. (Twenty-two, eleven yuan)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

On Smoking 227

— Shuxian

According to news from the Jianghai Customs Statistics Department, the recent annual consumption of cigarettes in various provinces across the country, excluding frequent instances of private manufacturing and tax evasion, amounts to a staggering 400 million yuan annually. This alarming figure forms a striking contrast with the country's entire population.

The Chinese seem particularly interested in smoking, and cigarettes seem to have an extraordinary connection with the Chinese. From esteemed gentlemen to those picking up cigarette butts on the streets, old and young, men and women, regardless of social status, everyone loves to have a cigarette in their mouth. Although cigarettes vary in quality and price, all cigarettes are smokable. Those who don't smoke seem out of place. Based on individual economic circumstances, this has created a massive consumption figure.

Smoking not only provides no benefit to the human body but also causes significant harm. This is something that everyone in the current 20th century seems to understand. However, smokers knowingly violate this principle, even willing to eat less but unable to resist smoking a cigarette. The first greeting between friends is a cigarette, and a cigarette is also used when feeling mentally exhausted or physically tired. Theaters, dance halls, and various public entertainment venues in major cities, as well as toilet rooms in schools, organizations, and factories, have become major bases for cigarette consumption!

I am also a die-hard smoker and have twice made up my mind to quit, but each time I couldn't last more than ten days before unconsciously falling back into old habits. This is, of course, partly due to my lack of willpower, but also because smoking has become a common social habit.

It is generally agreed that smoking should be quit, especially in these times of economic panic and difficult living conditions. However, how to implement a quitting method is a very difficult problem to solve! In my opinion, the only way to achieve good results is to voluntarily adopt the method of smoking less rather than more, not smoking rather than smoking less, and never smoking rather than not smoking.

Autumn at Paotai Bay 228

— Yefei

The rice stalks in the fields have turned golden, and farmers are busy harvesting the crystallization of their hard work and sweat.

Those of us who live in noisy cities year-round feel as if we are in another world when we enter the embrace of nature. The hardships of life and the vulgarity of the city are all swept away to the other side of the Atlantic, and one feels much clearer at heart.

Drifting, drifting; I drift along the Huangpu River. If not for the golden rice stalks interspersed with the oily green wilderness on both sides, I would almost forget that it is autumn!

A huge riverboat in the river slowly sails out of the Wusongkou. Several motorboats are shooting like arrows, cutting through the river's surface and breaking the yellow and turbid waves. The waves splash onto the bank, making a roaring sound.

The twilight envelops the earth, and the evening glow follows the setting sun, reflecting a beautiful golden yellow on the rippling sea. The scattered sails in the distance are tilted forward in the leisurely misty waves, and several lone ducks flap their wings and soar into the sky.

"The setting sun flies together with the lone duck, and the autumn water shares the same color with the long sky." This beautiful picture! Only at this time, only in this place, can I appreciate and enjoy it.

A large crowd of people is gathered on the bank of the Three Gorges Waterway, talking and laughing. These are men and women who have squeezed out of the city, preparing to come here for a breath of fresh air. The sea breeze glides over everyone's faces, and their clothes flap in the wind. The women's hair flutters in the wind, and gusts of wind roll up the dust and sand on the ground and send them flying into the air.

A very long stone embankment in front of me is exposed on the sea surface, lying quietly in the yellow and turbid waves. Many men and women are venturing on the embankment, and my feet are itching, so I finally jump onto the embankment and run forward desperately, running forward. However, its ruggedness and steepness are even more difficult than the Shu Road. With just a moment of carelessness, there is a danger of slipping into the sea and joining the wave gods! However, seeing four or five modern misses and misters walking peacefully in front of us, I can't help but feel ashamed!

At the end of the stone embankment, under the lighthouse, two girls are sitting, taking off their swimsuits, wiping the water stains from their bodies, and putting on blue serge cheongsams. However, their shoes and socks are not yet on, and they are standing and laughing like barefoot immortals.

Looking at a patch of azure sky, white clouds are slowly moving, really like a wisp of light smoke, and gradually fading away in an instant. A light blue warship is moored outside the Three Gorges Waterway, without flags or smoke, standing quietly, lifelessly, like a dying old man. Raging waves roll toward the stone embankment, stirring up a magnificent roar, and the waves soak our clothes.

Stepping onto the bank, I want to admire the true face of Mount Lu at the West Fort, but a wire mesh blocks the way: "As instructed: No visitors allowed. Notice from the Wusong Fort Administrator." In the lotus pond beside the road, the green lotuses still grow thickly like umbrellas, but there are no water lilies, and they are already showing some signs of withering!

Over there, two young men in suits are tightly embracing a girl in student uniform and walking on the grass. Here, a girl in green and a girl in red are leaning on the same young man's arms and eating purple grapes. What is going on? I think that is spring in autumn!

The vast night is pressing down tightly, and smoke is rising from the roofs of rural homes. I ride in a bright moon-like small car, creaking back to Paotaiwan Station, and finally the short little train drags us back to Shanghai.

Bank Failures 229

— Xinzi

Not long after the Wuhua Bank failed, now the China Industrial Bank has also failed. Although the reasons for the failures are all due to the failure of speculative ventures, and the managers had to leave when they were in dire straits, the fact that the banking sector has not been able to develop normally due to economic stagnation in recent years, and thus had to invest in other areas, is also a major reason.

In recent years, the banking sector has seen cash concentrated in the cities due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy, while urban industry and commerce have been in a state of decline due to the recession. Given these two reasons, the amount of cash held by banks has been increasing day by day. On the other hand, expenses cannot be reduced, and the interest rates for depositors increase daily. Lending money is risky in such a market, as there is a fear that it will not be repaid. If no loans are made, the money will not generate more money while sitting in the vault. Under layers of difficulties, the banking sector only has two options: speculative ventures and investments in real estate.

The first path is to invest in margin trading of public bonds, or even the wheat and cotton markets, using one's own judgment to leverage depositors' money, hoping to profit in the process. However, this is an extremely dangerous path, and the manager's occasional carelessness can easily lead to complete defeat.

The second path is to invest in real estate, the most common approach being to build large buildings. On the one hand, the empty rooms are rented out to others, and on the other hand, this wins the trust of depositors while increasing the bank's fixed assets. The future rental income from this large property is used to pay interest to depositors and generate profits for the bank itself.

The risks of the first path have been mentioned above. The second path is also not a proper one. Although the buildings are built, the emptiness of the vault is inevitable. If a financial crisis were to occur, would the bank not be forced to close down immediately? Considering the purpose of banks themselves, they should be regulating the economy. By spending large sums of money in these two areas, isn't the bank itself becoming empty?

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

Therefore, in view of the recent failures of two banks, and the alarming shadow of many other banks in the future, for the sake of the stability of the national economy, we should take both active and passive measures.

Actively, the current concentration of cash in the cities (more accurately, in the banks) is related to solving the entire social problem. We hope that the authorities and financial giants will come up with sound plans.

Passively, we ask the Bankers Association to publicly report the names of its member and non-member banks, and to clearly state the ultimate responsibility of its members, guaranteed by them. Furthermore, they should regularly send personnel to inspect existing members, and should give careful consideration to new members seeking to join.

In this way, we can avoid causing people to be at a loss, and the national economy will not be greatly affected.

Men of Letters and Poverty 230

— Yugong

In the past and present, when a man of letters is praised by society as "poor but ambitious," he mostly takes it as a qualification to be proud of. In reality, there are very, very few truly poor men of letters.

Take Yan Hui, a worthy disciple of Confucius, for example. Confucius praised him, "Hui is worthy. He lives in a humble alley without any resentment." He seems to be an extremely poor man, but he had thirty mu (unit of land) of fields attached to the city, which makes him a small landlord. Take Tao Yuanming, the pastoral poet, for example. Because he left behind a poem about begging for food, it gives people the impression that he was a poor poet, but when he returned home rather than bowing down for five dou (unit of measure) of rice, he still had welcoming servants and overgrown fields. In reality, he was a considerable landlord.

A friend told me that in ancient times, saying someone was poor meant they didn't hold official office.

I don't know if this is verifiable. However, based on the examples of Yan Hui and Tao Yuanming mentioned above, it is certainly reliable.

Extending from this, it can be seen that those who held official office in ancient times were rich people, and officials were also called nobles. It can be seen that when a man of letters became an official, he gained both wealth and status. This idea—promotion and fortune—was the same for men of letters in ancient and modern times.

However, the ancients also had a deceptive saying that writing "improves with poverty," meaning to encourage poor men of letters to "accept their fate" and that while they lack material possessions, they have better reputations. But those who said that certainly didn't understand the plight of the poor, it's utter nonsense. A person who worries about clothing and food all day long doesn't even have the mood to write, so how can there be good writing? This is the experience of all poor men of letters. There are more and more deceptive sayings from the ancients, this is just a small example.

Furthermore, nowadays, a man of letters who loses his job can make a living by selling his writing, which is much better than unemployed workers. This is something that poor men of letters should not blame fate for.

Street Singers in a Deep Alley 231

— Tuoren

At midnight, the trees outside the window are rustling in the autumn wind, and the dim yellow light of the street lamp at the corner of the alley is swaying in the wind. The gauze curtain on the window is beautifully printed with layers of floating shadows of leaves. The sky is just black and dull.

My lonely heart is even more melancholy on this deep autumn night. As if I were sleepless, one fantasy after another flits across my eyes, plunging me deeply into a dream of fantasy, recalling the joys and sorrows of life.

The stagnant sky is even darker, and the wind is blowing even more fiercely. In an instant, it has started to rain. Ah! The autumn night rain brings an even thicker chill.

The autumn wind blows fiercely through the rain, and the glass on the window is pattering. In the quiet atmosphere of this deep alley, the sound of the rain is so frightening, it's as if a person in the desert is listening to the howling wind, that's how frightening it is.

From far, far away, a burst of long, low singing comes, mixed with the sound of rain, flying into my ears, startling me from my dream state. Curiously, I stretch my head and look out the window through the glass.

Gradually, the singing subsides, and only the melodious sound of the bamboo flute is heard. But that sound carries a sad melody. In an instant, the woman's singing starts again, her song also so sad, harmonizing with the flute.

Ah! This is the song of a blind girl, and in the quiet alley of this late night, it seems especially desolate and tragic. The most feared thing for a wanderer is to hear the lament of another wanderer!

The rain is still falling, the sky is still so black and gloomy, and my heart is even more lonely and sad. Ah! The sadness of the wanderer!

The surroundings of the night are so quiet, so empty!

The blind girl's singing finally fades away, and my heart feels a burst of emptiness! Surrounding my deep heart is an even more terrifying loneliness.

Ah! Wanderer, your heart is destined to be lonely forever.

Amateur Mailbox

Divorce Procedures 232

Dear Editor:

I am a miserable woman bound by an old-fashioned marriage. In my childhood, my parents arranged for me to marry a man who had returned from abroad. At that time, I was about sixteen or seventeen years old, and my knowledge was very naive, and I had not yet thought about the pain of old-fashioned marriages. For two years after the marriage, I did not feel any trouble. Later, he said he wanted to go abroad again to make a living, so we were separated and could not meet. At first, he still sent letters frequently and sent my living expenses from time to time. However, soon, not only did he not remit living expenses, but also the letters became fewer. Because my source of income was cut off, I had to return to my mother's home and live off my father and brothers. For more than three years, I sent several letters, but he only replied to one, saying that he was unemployed in another place and had not yet found a suitable job, so he could not keep his promise to send living expenses back. Because he had not found a job and had not returned to his home country, it seemed like he had abandoned me. Therefore, I had no choice but to hire a lawyer to write him a letter, hoping that he would strictly abide by his promise and remit living expenses every month, otherwise we would dissolve the relationship. His reply was very vague, almost the same as the previous letter. Now I have asked the lawyer to write a second letter, saying that if he does not keep his promise, we will have to divorce. However, his reply has not yet arrived.

I am now suffering terribly and don't know what the future holds. I have the following three questions and hope that you can help me resolve them.

(1) If he does not provide living expenses for more than three years, can I declare a dissolution of the relationship and freedom to marry by publishing a statement in the newspaper myself? Is this legally problematic?

(2) If, after the second letter from the lawyer mentioned above, I do not wait for his reply and marry myself, will the letter from the Shanghai lawyer have the effect of a "divorce"?

(3) If I do not leave Shanghai, can I sue him for paying the previous living expenses and compensation for losses?

Respectfully submitted, Biryun

Editor's Note: The questions you have asked cannot be legally established and have many difficult circumstances. I will answer them separately below:

(1) If someone's whereabouts are unknown for more than three years, it constitutes a reason to sue for divorce. However, a lawsuit must be filed in court, and a divorce can only be legal after a divorce is granted. If one party declares a divorce in the newspaper, it is illegal and therefore invalid. Furthermore, failure to provide living expenses can only be reported as malicious abandonment, which is also a reason to sue for divorce, but it is not the same as whereabouts being unknown.

(2) Marrying someone else without going through legal divorce procedures constitutes bigamy. Publishing in the newspaper and the lawyer's notice have no divorce effect. Apart from the fact that divorce can be agreed upon by both parties for any reason, if it is the will of one party, it is not effective unless there is a legal reason and a judgment by the court.

(3) If you do not leave Shanghai and sue for divorce, it is possible, but the other party must also be from Shanghai, otherwise the Shanghai court has no jurisdiction. As for the repayment of living expenses and compensation for losses, it depends on whether there is sufficient reason.
